Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony on Loan with Additional Claim of Repayment
Commentary on two testimony cases from Kanz al-Daqaiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a witness's additional claim about repayment does not invalidate the original testimony for the debt, and distinguish between partial and full repayment claims.

Core Idea
A witness's claim of repayment does not nullify the loan testimony; the judge only considers external evidence.

This lesson examines two scenarios in testimony on a loan: when a witness adds that part or all of the debt was repaid. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between the witness's knowledge and the court's acceptance of testimony. You will learn why the testimony for the loan stands and why the repayment claim requires separate proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the two cases: (1) two witnesses testify to a loan of 1000, one says 500 repaid; (2) two witnesses testify to a loan, one says fully repaid. Note the different rulings on the repayment claim.
The first case is partial repayment, the second full repayment.
2
Note the ruling on the loan
In both cases, the testimony for the loan is accepted. Write down: the loan is proven by two witnesses, so it stands regardless of the additional claim.
3
Understand the ruling on repayment
The repayment claim is not accepted because it is made by only one witness. For partial repayment, it is not accepted unless another witness joins; for full repayment, it is also not accepted.
The text says the repayment claim is not heard (لا يسمع).
4
Analyze the rationale
The judge does not consider the witness's personal knowledge. The witness may know repayment occurred, but the court bases its decision on the evidence presented. The principle: 'الشافهة لا ينظر إلى اعتقاده' (the judge does not look at his belief).
This is from the commentary: القاضي لا ينظر إلى اعتقاده.
5
Apply the distinction between partial and full repayment
In partial repayment, the witness may still have a role (he testifies for the remaining debt). In full repayment, the witness seems to have no basis to testify, but the loan testimony is still accepted because it is a separate fact. The judge only validates the external shahada.
The text explains this distinction to remove the doubt that full repayment would nullify the testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو) شهدا بألف وقال أحدهما قضاه منها خمسمائة تقبل بألف ولم يسمع قوله قضاه إلا إن شهد معه ، آخر وينبغي أن لا يشهد حتى يقر المدعي بما قبض ولو شهدا بقرض ألف وشهد أحدهما أنه قضاه جازت الشهادة على القرض ولو شهدا أنه قتل لا هـ . الألف أبي حنيفة، وعندهما جازت على الأقل ا قوله : (ولو) شهدا بألف وقال أحدهما قضاه منها خمسمائة تقبل بألف ولم يسمع قوله قضاه إلا أن شهد معه آخر) لاتفاقهما على وجوب وانفراد أحدهما بقضاء النصف فلا يقبل لعدم كمال الحجة، ولا يكون ذلك تكذيباً لشاهد القضاء فيما شهد به بأصل المال لأنه لم يكذبه فيما شهد له وإنما كذبه فيما شهد عليه وذلك يمنع كما إذا شهدا له بشيء ثم شهدا عليه بحق فإن شهادتهما له لا تبطل وإن كذبهما، وقدمنا فروعاً مبينة على هذا الأصل في أول الباب عن الخانية. ولا بد من كون المدعي ادعى الألف وأنكر القضاء إذ لو قال لم يكن لي عليه إلا خمسمائة لم تقبل أصلاً لأنه أكذب شهوده؛ كذا في العمدة. وإن اعترف بالقضاء لزمه خمسمائة ؛ كذا في العمدة قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يشهد حتى يقر المدعي بما قبض كيلا يصير معيناً على الظلم والمراد من «ينبغي» معنى يجب فلا تحل له الشهادة وقدمنا حكم ما إذا تحمل شهادة ثم أخبر بما يرفعها من دين ونكاح وقتل أول الشهادات وقد ذكرها في فتح القدير هنا .
قوله : (ولو شهدا بقرض ألف وشهد أحدهما أنه قضاه جازت الشهادة على القرض) لتمام الحجة في القرض وعدمها في القضاء، وإنما ذكر هذه وإن علم حكمها مما قبلها لاختلاف الموضوع فإنها في القرض وما قبلها في مطلق ألف وهي في انفراد أحدهما بقضاء الكل وما قبلها بقضاء النصف، والأولى مسألة القدوري والثانية مسألة الجامع الصغير. ومن جهة المعنى فإنه ربما يتوهم عدم القبول في الثانية لأنه لما علم بالقضاء انتفت شهادته أصلاً فحين شهد كانت باطلة بخلاف قضاء البعض فإنه يقول شهدت لبقاء الخمسمائة وشهدت بالألف أو لا كما تحملت فكان الأداء واجباً علي بخلاف ما إذا علم بقضاء الكل فإن الأداء لم يجب أصلاً فذكرها لدفع هذه الشبهة. وإنما قبلت لأنه صادق فيما أخبر به من القرض متقدماً ولا ينظر القاضي إلى اعتقاده إنما ينظر إلى أداء شهادته؛ كذا في المعراج.
His statement: (And if) two witnesses testify to one thousand and one of them says that he repaid five hundred of it, the testimony is accepted for one thousand, and his statement about repayment is not heard unless another witness joins him. And it is advisable that he does not testify until the plaintiff acknowledges receipt. And if two witnesses testify to a loan of one thousand and one of them testifies that he repaid it, the testimony for the loan is accepted. And if two witnesses testify that he killed... end. The thousand Abu Hanifa, and according to the two, it is accepted for the least. End. His statement: (And if) two witnesses testify to one thousand and one of them says that he repaid five hundred of it, the testimony is accepted for one thousand, and his statement about repayment is not heard unless another witness joins him) because they agree on the obligation and one of them alone testifies to the repayment of half, so it is not accepted due to lack of complete evidence. And that does not constitute discrediting the witness of repayment regarding what he testified to about the principal debt because he did not discredit him in what he testified for him, but rather he discredited him in what he testified against him, and that prevents, as when they testify for him for something then later testify against him for a right; their testimony for him is not invalidated even if they contradict him. And we have presented branches based on this principle at the beginning of the chapter from al-Khaniyyah. And it is necessary that the plaintiff claims the one thousand and denies the repayment, because if he says 'I had nothing due from him except five hundred,' it is not accepted at all because he has discredited his witnesses; as in al-Umdah. And if he admits to the repayment, five hundred is binding on him; as in al-Umdah. His statement: (And it is advisable that he does not testify until the plaintiff acknowledges receipt) so that he does not become an aider in injustice. And the meaning of 'advisable' here is obligatory, so it is not permissible for him to testify. And we have presented the ruling for when he undertakes testimony then reports something that removes it, like debt, marriage, or killing, at the beginning of the chapter on testimonies, and it is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir here.
His statement: (And if two witnesses testify to a loan of one thousand and one of them testifies that he repaid it, the testimony for the loan is accepted) because the evidence is complete for the loan and not for the repayment. He mentions this even though its ruling is known from what preceded because of the difference in subject matter: here it is a loan, and before it was an absolute thousand; here it is one of them testifying to repayment of the whole, while before it was repayment of half. The first is from al-Quduri, the second from al-Jami' al-Saghir. From a meaning standpoint, one might mistakenly think it is not accepted in the second case because he knew about the repayment, so his testimony is nullified from the start, unlike partial repayment where he says he testified for the remaining five hundred and testified for the thousand as he bore witness, so the performance was obligatory upon him, unlike when he knows of full repayment, where performance is not obligatory. So he mentioned it to remove this doubt. And it is accepted because he is truthful in what he reported about the loan earlier, and the judge does not look at his personal belief; the judge only looks at the performance of his testimony; as in al-Mi'raj.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement and commentary on two related cases: (1) when both witnesses agree on a debt of 1000, but one adds that 500 was repaid; and (2) when both witness a loan of 1000, but one testifies that the entire loan was repaid. In the first case, the testimony is accepted for the full 1000 (the common part), and the additional claim of partial repayment is not accepted because it is a separate matter requiring its own evidence (another witness). The plaintiff must deny repayment; if he admits to it, he is bound. The commentator, Zayla'i, emphasizes that the judge does not consider the witness's personal knowledge; the external testimony is what matters. However, if the witness knows the repayment is true, he should not testify until the plaintiff acknowledges receipt to avoid aiding in falsehood (the word 'ينبغي' here means obligatory). In the second case (full repayment), the testimony for the original loan is accepted despite the witness's knowledge of repayment, because the loan itself is proven by two witnesses; the repayment is a separate claim not proven. This is distinguished from the partial repayment case. The passage also notes that these two cases are from different sources: the first from al-Jami' al-Saghir, the second from al-Quduri (referring to Mukhtasar al-Quduri). The reason for accepting the loan testimony despite the witness's knowledge is that the judge only considers the presented evidence, not the witness's inner state.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): Repayment or discharge of a debt.
تكذيب (takdhīb): Discrediting or contradicting a witness's testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify to a loan of 1000, and one of them says the entire loan was repaid. What is the ruling?
A) The testimony is rejected entirely because of contradiction.
B) The testimony for the loan is accepted, and the claim of repayment is not accepted.
C) Only the repayment testimony is accepted, not the loan.
D) The witness who claimed repayment is discredited, so his original testimony is also invalid.

Key Takeaway
A witness's additional claim of repayment does not invalidate the original testimony for the loan; the judge accepts the loan based on the two witnesses and disregards the unsupported repayment claim.

Witness Disagreement on Time or Place: Verbal vs. Physical Acts
Ruling on verbal vs. physical acts in witness disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle distinguishing verbal and physical acts to determine the acceptance of testimony when witnesses differ on time or place.

Core Idea
Testimony on verbal acts accepted despite differing time/place; on physical acts not, because words can be repeated, actions cannot.

In this passage, the author supplements his text by citing al-Kafi's rule on witness disagreement. The rule hinges on whether the event testified is a verbal act (qawl) or a physical act (fi‘l). Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the admissibility of testimony in various legal contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the event's nature
Determine whether the subject matter of testimony is a verbal act (e.g., sale, divorce) or a physical act (e.g., usurpation, murder). Also note if a verbal act has a physical condition (e.g., marriage requires witness presence).
The key is the mashhud bihi (thing testified about), not associated acts.
2
Apply the rule for verbal acts
If the event is a verbal act, the testimony is accepted despite differing time or place because speech can be repeated.
Examples: sale, divorce, agency, loan.
3
Apply the rule for physical acts
If the event is a physical act, or a verbal act with a physical condition, the testimony is rejected because actions cannot be repeated identically.
Examples: usurpation, murder, marriage (due to witness presence).
4
Trace the underlying principle
Recognize the rationale: words can be reiterated, but physical acts are singular events.
This principle (talil) is the basis of the distinction.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Practice with hypotheticals: e.g., witnesses disagree on time of a gift (verbal) vs. time of an assault (physical).
Check if the main act is qawl or fi‘l.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى اختلاف الشاهدين في الزمان أو المكان. وذكره في الكافي فقال : وإذا اختلف الشاهدان في المكان أو الزمان في البيع والشراء والطلاق والعتق والوكالة والوصية والرهن والدين والقرض والبراءة والكفالة والحوالة والقذف تقبل، وإن اختلفا في الجناية والغصب والقتل والنكاح لا تقبل، والأصل أن المشهود به إذا كان قولاً كالبيع ونحوه فاختلاف الشاهدين فيه في الزمان أو المكان لا يمنع قبول الشهادة لأن القول مما يعاد ويكرر، وإن كان المشهود به فعلاً كالغصب ونحوه أو قولاً لكن الفعل شرط صحته كالنكاح فإنه قول وحضور الشاهدين فعل وهو شرط فاختلافهما في الزمان أو المكان يمنع القبول لأن الفعل لا يعاد.
And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, did not mention the difference of the two witnesses in time or place. And it is mentioned in al-Kafi, saying: When the two witnesses differ in place or time in sale, purchase, divorce, emancipation, agency, will, pledge, debt, loan, discharge, suretyship, transfer of debt, and slander, it is accepted. But if they differ in assault, usurpation, murder, and marriage, it is not accepted. The principle is that if the subject matter of testimony is a verbal act like sale and the like, then the difference of the two witnesses in time or place does not prevent acceptance of testimony because speech can be repeated and reiterated. But if the subject matter is a physical act like usurpation and the like, or a verbal act where a physical act is a condition of its validity like marriage—for it is speech but the presence of two witnesses is a physical act and a condition—then their difference in time or place prevents acceptance because a physical act cannot be repeated.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from al-Kafi, cited to supplement the author's omission. It provides the rule for when witnesses disagree on the time or place of the event. The principle distinguishes between verbal acts (aqwāl) and physical acts (af‘āl). For verbal acts such as sale, divorce, emancipation, etc., testimonies are accepted even if witnesses differ on time or place, because words can be repeated; the same contract could have been made at different times. For physical acts such as usurpation (ghasb), assault, murder, and also marriage (which is a verbal contract but requires witnesses as a condition, which is a physical act), the testimony is not accepted if there is disagreement on time or place because a physical act is a singular event that cannot be repeated identically. The ruling reflects the Hanafi principle that the subject matter's nature determines the admissibility of testimony when details conflict.

Key Terms
قول (qawl): A verbal act; the subject matter of testimony is a spoken declaration.
فعل (fi‘l): A physical act; the subject matter of testimony is a tangible action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify to a sale, but one says it occurred on Monday and the other says Tuesday. What is the ruling?
A) The testimony is rejected because of the discrepancy in time.
B) The testimony is accepted because sale is a verbal act that can be repeated.
C) The testimony is accepted only if they agree on the day.
D) The testimony is accepted for part of the sale but not all.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of testimony with time/place disagreements depends on whether the event is a verbal act (words can be repeated) or a physical act (unique occurrence).

Testimony for a Debt with Partial Repayment Claimed by One Witness
Ruling with proof on partial contradiction in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one witness claims partial repayment of a debt and explain the principle of completeness of evidence.

Core Idea
A lone witness's repayment claim is rejected; complete evidence requires two witnesses.

When two witnesses confirm a debt but one adds that part was repaid, how does the court treat this? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the testimony for the full amount stands, but the repayment claim is rejected for lack of complete proof. We will dissect the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two testimonial components
Separate the joint testimony (both agree on the debt) from the sole witness's statement (repayment).
The witnesses agree on the obligation (1,000 debt); only one asserts a discharge of 500.
2
Determine the ruling for each component
The joint testimony is accepted for the full debt; the sole repayment claim is rejected unless a second witness supports it.
Acceptance of the debt is based on two witnesses; rejection of repayment is due to incomplete evidence.
3
Understand the rationale: kamil al-hujja
The principle: complete evidence requires either two witnesses or one witness plus an oath. The lone claim lacks this.
The repayment claim is half evidence (shibh hujja), not enough to be heard.
4
Analyze the analogy to later testimony against the same witness
Just as witnesses who later testify against a person do not invalidate their earlier favorable testimony, the contradiction here does not invalidate the original debt testimony.
The contradiction is in what is testified against (repayment to plaintiff), not for (debt owed by defendant).
5
Consider the plaintiff's role
If the plaintiff admits only 500, the testimony is rejected entirely because he discredits his own witnesses.
The plaintiff must claim the full sum and deny repayment for the debt testimony to stand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو شهدا بألف وقال أحدهما قضاه منها خمسمائة تقبل بألف ولم يسمع قوله قضاه إلا أن شهد معه آخر وينبغي أن لا يشهد حتى يقر المدعي بما قبض قوله : (ولو) شهدا بألف وقال أحدهما قضاه منها خمسمائة تقبل بألف ولم يسمع قوله قضاه إلا أن شهد معه آخر لاتفاقهما على وجوب وانفراد أحدهما بقضاء النصف فلا يقبل لعدم كمال الحجة، ولا يكون ذلك تكذيباً لشاهد القضاء فيما شهد به بأصل المال لأنه لم يكذبه فيما شهد له وإنما كذبه فيما شهد عليه وذلك يمنع كما إذا شهدا له بشيء ثم شهدا عليه بحق فإن شهادتهما له لا تبطل وإن كذبهما، وقدمنا فروعاً مبينة على هذا الأصل في أول الباب عن الخانية. ولا بد من كون المدعي ادعى الألف وأنكر القضاء إذ لو قال لم يكن لي عليه إلا خمسمائة لم تقبل أصلاً لأنه أكذب شهوده؛ كذا في العمدة. وإن اعترف بالقضاء لزمه خمسمائة ؛ كذا في العمدة قوله : (وينبغي أن لا يشهد حتى يقر المدعي بما قبض كيلا يصير معيناً على الظلم والمراد من «ينبغي» معنى يجب فلا تحل له الشهادة وقدمنا حكم ما إذا تحمل شهادة ثم أخبر بما يرفعها من دين ونكاح وقتل أول الشهادات وقد ذكرها في فتح القدير هنا .
If two witnesses testify to a thousand, and one of them says, 'He repaid from it five hundred,' the testimony is accepted for the thousand, and his statement of repayment is not heard unless another witness joins him. And it is proper that he should not testify until the plaintiff acknowledges receipt. The commentator says: (And if they testify) etc.: Because they agree on the obligation, and one of them alone claims repayment of half, so it is not accepted due to lack of complete evidence. This is not a discrediting of the witness regarding his testimony for the principal, because he did not discredit him in what he testified for him, but rather discredited him in what he testified against him, and that prevents acceptance, just as if they testified for him for something and then testified against him for a right, their testimony for him is not invalidated even if they are contradicted. We have already presented branches based on this principle at the beginning of the chapter from al-Khaniyyah. It is necessary that the plaintiff claimed the thousand and denied the repayment, because if he said, 'I had only five hundred of his due,' it is not accepted at all because he has discredited his witnesses; similarly in al-`Umdah. And if he acknowledges the repayment, five hundred is binding on him; similarly in al-`Umdah. The commentator says: (And it is proper that he should not testify until the plaintiff acknowledges receipt), so that he does not become an aider in oppression, and the meaning of 'proper' is obligatory, so testimony is not permissible for him. We have already presented the ruling for one who undertakes testimony and then informs of something that nullifies it, such as debt, marriage, or killing, at the beginning of the section on testimonies, and it has been mentioned in Fath al-Qadir here.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses a scenario where two witnesses testify that the defendant owes the plaintiff one thousand, but one of the witnesses adds that five hundred of that amount has already been repaid. The ruling is that the testimony for the full thousand is accepted, but the statement about repayment is not heard unless supported by another witness. The reasoning is that both witnesses agree on the obligation of the debt, so the evidence for it is complete. However, the lone claim of repayment is only half the evidence needed, so it is rejected for lack of complete proof (kamil al-hujja). This does not discredit the witness regarding the original debt because the contradiction is in what he testifies against the plaintiff (repayment), not in what he testifies for him (the debt). An analogy is drawn: if two witnesses testify for a person and later testify against him, the earlier testimony remains valid. The commentary also clarifies that the plaintiff must have claimed the full thousand and denied repayment; otherwise, if he admits to only five hundred, the testimony is rejected entirely as he discredits his own witnesses. The phrase 'proper' (yanbaghi) means obligatory here; the witness should not testify until the plaintiff acknowledges receipt to avoid aiding oppression. This ruling is grounded in the principle of completeness of evidence and is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Legal testimony in court, requiring two male witnesses or one male and two females for financial claims.
قضاء (qada): Repayment or discharge of a debt.
كمال الحجة (kamil al-hujja): Complete evidence; the requirement for full proof in testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where two witnesses testify to a debt of 1,000, and one witness says that 500 was repaid, what is the ruling?
A) Both the testimony for the debt and the repayment claim are accepted.
B) The testimony for the debt is accepted, but the repayment claim is not heard unless supported by another witness.
C) The testimony is rejected entirely because of the contradiction.
D) The repayment claim is accepted as a separate testimony.

Key Takeaway
When witnesses agree on a debt, the full amount is proven; a lone claim of partial repayment lacks complete evidence and is not accepted.

Testimony for Loan with Full Repayment Claim by One Witness
Explanation of ruling when one witness claims full repayment of a loan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school accepts testimony for a loan even when one witness also claims full repayment, and distinguish between the witness's internal knowledge and formal testimony.

Core Idea
The judge rules on formal testimony, not the witness's belief.

In Hanafi fiqh, testimony is evaluated based on what the witness formally declares, not his private knowledge. This passage addresses a situation where two witnesses confirm a loan, but one adds that the borrower fully repaid it. The ruling may seem counterintuitive, but it is grounded in the distinction between the act of testifying and personal certainty. Let us examine the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testimony about the loan. The ruling is that it is accepted (sahih) despite one witness also claiming full repayment.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the principle that the judge looks only at the performance of testimony (ada' al-shahada), not the witness's internal belief. This is a rule of evidence in Hanafi law.
The author cites al-Mi`raj to support this.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The rationale: the testimony for the loan is complete because both witnesses agree on it; the repayment claim is from only one, so it is incomplete. The judge separates the two statements.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
Other schools might argue that the witness's knowledge of repayment nullifies his entire testimony. The Hanafi view distinguishes the two facts.
Cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi because it relies on the clear rule of formal testimony and is supported by the principle that evidence for the loan is complete.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو شهدا بقرض ألف وشهد أحدهما أنه قضاه جازت الشهادة على القرض) لتمام الحجة في القرض وعدمها في القضاء، وإنما ذكر هذه وإن علم حكمها مما قبلها لاختلاف الموضوع فإنها في القرض وما قبلها في مطلق ألف وهي في انفراد أحدهما بقضاء الكل وما قبلها بقضاء النصف، والأولى مسألة القدوري والثانية مسألة الجامع الصغير. ومن جهة المعنى فإنه ربما يتوهم عدم القبول في الثانية لأنه لما علم بالقضاء انتفت شهادته أصلاً فحين شهد كانت باطلة بخلاف قضاء البعض فإنه يقول شهدت لبقاء الخمسمائة وشهدت بالألف أو لا كما تحملت فكان الأداء واجباً علي بخلاف ما إذا علم بقضاء الكل فإن الأداء لم يجب أصلاً فذكرها لدفع هذه الشبهة. وإنما قبلت لأنه صادق فيما أخبر به من القرض متقدماً ولا ينظر القاضي إلى اعتقاده إنما ينظر إلى أداء شهادته؛ كذا في المعراج.
The commentator says: (If they testify to a loan of one thousand and one of them testifies that he repaid it, the testimony for the loan is accepted) because the evidence is complete for the loan and incomplete for the repayment. He only mentioned this ruling, even though its ruling is known from what preceded, because the subject differs: this is about a loan, while the previous was about an absolute thousand; this is about one of them claiming full repayment, while the previous was about partial repayment. The first is the issue of al-Quduri, and the second is the issue of al-Jami' al-Saghir. From a semantic perspective, one might imagine non-acceptance in the second (full repayment) because when he knows of the repayment, his testimony is altogether nullified, so when he testified, it was invalid, unlike partial repayment where he says, 'I testified for the remaining five hundred and I testified for the thousand or not as I undertook, so performance was obligatory upon me,' unlike the case of full repayment where performance was not obligatory at all. So he mentioned it to refute this misconception. It is accepted because he is truthful in what he informed concerning the loan previously, and the judge does not look to his belief; he only looks to his performance of testimony; similarly in al-Mi`raj.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It deals with two witnesses testifying to a loan of one thousand, but one witness later testifies that the borrower fully repaid the loan. The ruling is that the testimony for the loan (the original lending) is accepted. The reasoning is that the evidence for the loan is complete (both witnesses agree on the loan), but the evidence for the repayment is incomplete (only one witness). This is similar to the previous case of partial repayment, but the author mentions it separately because the previous case involved an absolute debt (not specified as loan) and partial repayment, while this case specifies a loan and full repayment. There is a potential misconception: when a witness knows of full repayment, his testimony for the loan might be considered invalid because he knows the debt is discharged. However, the ruling clarifies that the judge looks only at the act of testimony, not the witness's internal knowledge. The witness is truthful about the loan having occurred; his claim of repayment is a separate matter. This ruling is from the Hanafi madhhab and is found in al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, which are part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
قرض (qard): A loan of fungible items, typically money, where the borrower is obligated to repay the equivalent.
أداء الشهادة (ada' al-shahada): The act of giving testimony in court, as opposed to the witness's personal knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses testify to a loan of one thousand, and one of them also testifies that the borrower fully repaid the loan, what is the ruling for the testimony about the loan?
A) The testimony for the loan is rejected because the witness's statement about repayment contradicts it.
B) The testimony for the loan is accepted, but the repayment claim is not heard.
C) Both testimonies are accepted, and the court will decide based on preponderance.
D) The testimony for the loan is accepted only if the other witness supports the repayment claim.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the validity of testimony depends on the formal act of testifying, not the witness's internal beliefs, so a loan testimony remains valid even if the same witness later claims full repayment.

Disagreement in Time/Place: Pure Statements vs Acts
Core ruling on witness disagreement: pure statements vs acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between pure statements and acts in witness testimony and state the Hanafi position on qadhf.

Core Idea
Pure statements are repeatable; acts are unique — disagreement only invalidates testimony for acts.

When witnesses disagree on the time or place of an event, does their testimony become invalid? The Hanafi school answers by looking at the nature of the testified matter. This lesson explores the foundational distinction between pure statements (qawl mahd) and physical acts (fi‘l), and the specific dispute regarding accusations of adultery (qadhf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
Determine whether the testified event is a statement (e.g., sale, divorce) or an act (e.g., usurpation, assault).
The distinction hinges on whether the event can be repeated.
2
Apply the general rule
If it is a pure statement, disagreement in time/place does not invalidate. If it is an act, it invalidates.
The act in one time/place is a different event.
3
Locate the qadhf exception
Accusation of adultery is a statement, but the Sahibayn argue that disagreement still invalidates.
This is because each testimony might be a direct accusation or a report.
4
Analyze the dispute
Abu Hanifa accepts reconciliation; the Sahibayn reject. Understand the reasoning behind each.
Abu Hanifa: one could be reporting the other’s direct accusation.
5
Note the practical consequence
In cases of qadhf, the ruling differs: accepted (Abu Hanifa) vs rejected (Sahibayn).
The text does not give a definitive tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى اختلاف الشاهدين في الزمان أو المكان. وذكره في الكافي فقال : وإذا اختلف الشاهدان في المكان أو الزمان في البيع والشراء والطلاق والعتق والوكالة والوصية والرهن والدين والقرض والبراءة والكفالة والحوالة والقذف تقبل، وإن اختلفا في الجناية والغصب والقتل والنكاح لا تقبل، والأصل أن المشهود به إذا كان قولاً كالبيع ونحوه فاختلاف الشاهدين فيه في الزمان أو المكان لا يمنع قبول الشهادة لأن القول مما يعاد ويكرر، وإن كان المشهود به فعلاً كالغصب ونحوه أو قولاً لكن الفعل شرط صحته كالنكاح فإنه قول وحضور الشاهدين فعل وهو شرط فاختلافهما في الزمان أو المكان يمنع القبول لأن الفعل في زمان أو مكان غير الفعل في زمان أو مكان أخر فاختلف المشهود به . ثم قال أبو يوسف ومحمد: إذا اختلف شاهدا القذف في مكان أو زمان لا تقبل وإن كان قولاً لأن كل واحد منهما إن كان إنشاء فهو غيران وليس على كل قذف شاهدان، وإن كان أحدهما إنشاء والآخر إخباراً فهما لا يتفقان لأن الإنشاء أن يقول زنيت أو أنت زان والإخبار أن يقول قذفتك بالزنا، وأبو حنيفة يقول : يحتمل أنه أحدهما الإنشاء والآخر الإخبار فيثبت عندهما قذفه سمع فشهدا به اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين : الشهادة بعقد تمامه بالفعل كرهن وهبة وصدقه يبطلها الاختلاف في زمان ومكان إلا عند محمد ا هـ . فعلم به أن ما في الكافي من أن الرهن والهبة والصدقة من قبيل البيع ونحوه قول محمد وقول الشيخين بخلافه والحاصل كما في جامع الفصولين أن الاختلاف لا يخلو من وجوه ثلاثة : إما في زمان أو مكان أو إنشاء أو إقرار، وكل منها لا يخلو من أربعة أوجه : إما في الفعل أو في القول أو في فعل ملحق بالقول أو عكسه. أما الفعل فيمنع قبول الشهادة في الوجوه الثلاثة، وأما القول المحض كبيع ورهن مطلقاً. وأما الفعل الملحق بالقول وهو القرض فلا يمنع وأما عكسه كنكاح فيمنع وهذا موافق لما في الكافي، وفصل قاضيخان في فتاواه في الرهن والهبة والصدقة بأنهم إذا شهدوا على معاينة القبض واختلفا في الأيام والبلدان جازت شهادتهم في قولهما خلافاً لمحمد، وإن شهدوا على إقرار الراهن والواهب والمتصدق بالقبض جازت في قولهم اهـ. وفي شرح ابن وهبان تنبيه الاختلاف في المكان الاختلاف في الزمان ولا عكس الجواز أن يشهد عليه في وقتين مختلفين في مكان واحد ا هـ . وفي الخانية : ولو اختلفا في الثياب التي كانت على الطالب أو المطلوب أو المركب أو قال أحدهما كان معنا فلان وقال الآخر لم يكن معنا، ذكر في الأصل أنه يجوز ولا تبطل هذه الشهادة ا هـ. ثم اعلم أن ظاهر إطلاقهم أن الاختلاف في الزمان في الأقوال غير مانع شامل لما إذا تفاحش أو لا لأنهم يمثلونه بأمس واليوم فلا فرق بين القليل والكثير؛ كذا في القنية.
The author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the disagreement of witnesses in time or place. It is mentioned in al-Kafi, where it says: If the two witnesses disagree in place or time in sale, purchase, divorce, manumission, agency, will, pledge, debt, loan, disavowal, surety, transfer, and accusation of adultery, the testimony is accepted. But if they disagree in assault, usurpation, murder, and marriage, it is not accepted. The principle is that if the testified matter is a statement, like sale and the like, then the disagreement of the witnesses in time or place does not prevent acceptance of the testimony, because a statement can be repeated. If the testified matter is an act, like usurpation and the like, or a statement where the act is a condition of its validity, like marriage (it is a statement, but the presence of witnesses is an act and condition), then disagreement in time or place prevents acceptance, because the act in one time or place is different from the act in another time or place, so the testified matter differs. Then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If the witnesses of accusation of adultery disagree in place or time, it is not accepted, even though it is a statement, because if each of them is a direct accusation (insha'), they are two different accusations, and there are not two witnesses for each accusation; if one is a direct accusation and the other is a report (ikhbar), they do not agree, because the direct accusation says 'You committed adultery' or 'You are an adulterer,' and the report says 'I accused you of adultery.' Abu Hanifa says: It is possible that one is direct and the other is report, so the accusation of adultery is established upon hearing them testify to it. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: Testimony regarding a contract whose completion requires an act, like pledge, gift, and charity, is invalidated by disagreement in time and place, except according to Muhammad. It is thus known that what is in al-Kafi that pledge, gift, and charity are of the type of sale and the like is the view of Muhammad, while the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold otherwise. The summary, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn, is that disagreement does not fall short of three aspects: either in time, place, or whether it is direct or acknowledgment; and each of these does not fall short of four aspects: either in act, statement, act annexed to statement, or its opposite. As for act, it prevents acceptance of testimony in the three aspects. As for pure statement, like sale and pledge absolutely, it does not prevent. As for act annexed to statement, which is loan, it does not prevent. As for its opposite, like marriage, it prevents. This is consistent with what is in al-Kafi. Qadi Khan detailed in his Fatawa regarding pledge, gift, and charity that if they testify to witnessing the delivery (qabd) and differ in days and countries, their testimony is accepted according to the two shaykhs, contrary to Muhammad; if they testify to the admission (iqrar) of the pledgor, donor, or almsgiver of delivery, it is accepted in their view. In Sharh Ibn Wahban: A note: disagreement in place is like disagreement in time, but not vice versa; it is permissible to testify against someone at two different times in one place. In al-Khaniyyah: If they differ regarding the clothes that were on the plaintiff or defendant, or the mount, or one said 'So-and-so was with us' and the other said 'He was not with us,' it is mentioned in al-Asl that it is permissible and this testimony is not invalidated. Know that the apparent general applicability of their words that disagreement in time in statements is not a barrier includes whether it is enormous or not, because they give examples like yesterday and today, so there is no difference between little and much; similarly in al-Qunyah.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the effect of disagreement between witnesses regarding the time or place of the testified event. It begins by noting that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not address this topic, but it is covered in al-Kafi. The principle is: if the subject matter is a pure statement (qawl), like sale, divorce, etc., disagreement in time or place does not invalidate the testimony because statements can be repeated. If it is an act (fi'l), like assault or usurpation, disagreement invalidates because the act in one time/place is a different event. For marriage and similar contracts that require witness presence as an act, disagreement also invalidates. There is a specific dispute regarding accusation of adultery (qadhf): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say disagreement invalidates because the testimonies become inconsistent (one might be direct accusation, the other a report). Abu Hanifa, however, accepts it because they can be reconciled as one reporting the other's accusation. For contracts like pledge, gift, and charity that require delivery (qabd) as an act, there is a view from Muhammad that they are like statements, but the majority (the two shaykhs) consider them as acts annexed to statements, so disagreement in time/place invalidates only if they testify to witnessing the delivery. However, if they testify to an admission of delivery, disagreement does not invalidate. The passage also includes exceptions for trivial details like clothing or presence of others, where disagreement does not invalidate. The overarching principle is that pure statements are not time/place-sensitive, while acts and conditions are. This is a critical refinement of the earlier general rules from al-Kafi, incorporating the positions of the founding imams and later jurists like Qadi Khan.

Key Terms
قول محض (qawl mahd): Pure statement; a verbal act that is not tied to a physical action for validity, such as sale, divorce, etc.
إنشاء (insha'): Direct declaration creating a legal effect, e.g., 'You are divorced,' or 'You committed adultery' (as a direct accusation).
إخبار (ikhbar): A report of a past event or statement, e.g., 'He accused me of adultery.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of testified matter is NOT invalidated by disagreement between witnesses in time or place?
A) An act like usurpation (ghasb).
B) A statement conditioned on an act like marriage (nikah).
C) A pure statement like sale (bay').
D) A statement about a physical object like clothes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that witness disagreement in time/place only invalidates testimony for acts, not for pure statements, with a specific dispute on qadhf.

Expansion: Contracts Requiring Acts and the Three-Fold Classification
Expansion of the rule to contracts requiring delivery and the three-fold classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three-fold classification (act, pure statement, act annexed to statement) to contracts like pledge, gift, and charity, and identify the intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Contracts requiring delivery are treated as acts; disagreement invalidates unless witnesses testify to admission.

The general rule from the previous lesson is expanded in this passage. Contracts like pledge (rahn), gift (hiba), and charity (sadaqa) require physical delivery. The Hanafi jurists disagree on whether disagreement in time/place invalidates testimony. This lesson unpacks the classification from Jami' al-Fusulayn and the detailed ruling of Qadi Khan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Jami' al-Fusulayn lists: act (fi'l), pure statement (qawl mahd), act annexed to statement (fi'l mulhaq bi al-qawl), and its opposite (like marriage).
These categories determine the effect of disagreement.
2
Classify pledge, gift, charity
According to the two shaykhs, these require delivery (act) so they are like acts; Muhammad treats them as pure statements.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Apply Qadi Khan's detail
If witnesses testify to witnessing the delivery and disagree, the two shaykhs reject (except Muhammad). If they testify to an admission of delivery, all accept.
The key is whether the testimony is about the act itself or an acknowledgment.
4
Note the final classification
The passage concludes: acts always invalidate; pure statements never; acts annexed to statements (like loan) never invalidate; statements requiring acts (like marriage) invalidate.
This matches the principle from al-Kafi.
5
Analyze the minor exceptions
Disagreement about trivial details (clothes, presence of a person) does not invalidate testimony.
This shows the principle is applied reasonably.

The author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the disagreement of witnesses in time or place. It is mentioned in al-Kafi, where it says: If the two witnesses disagree in place or time in sale, purchase, divorce, manumission, agency, will, pledge, debt, loan, disavowal, surety, transfer, and accusation of adultery, the testimony is accepted. It is thus known that what is in al-Kafi that pledge, gift, and charity are of the type of sale and the like is the view of Muhammad, while the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold otherwise. As for act, it prevents acceptance of testimony in the three aspects. As for pure statement, like sale and pledge absolutely, it does not prevent. As for act annexed to statement, which is loan, it does not prevent. As for its opposite, like marriage, it prevents. This is consistent with what is in al-Kafi. In Sharh Ibn Wahban: A note: disagreement in place is like disagreement in time, but not vice versa; it is permissible to testify against someone at two different times in one place. In al-Khaniyyah: If they differ regarding the clothes that were on the plaintiff or defendant, or the mount, or one said 'So-and-so was with us' and the other said 'He was not with us,' it is mentioned in al-Asl that it is permissible and this testimony is not invalidated. Know that the apparent general applicability of their words that disagreement in time in statements is not a barrier includes whether it is enormous or not, because they give examples like yesterday and today, so there is no difference between little and much; similarly in al-Qunyah.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the effect of disagreement between witnesses regarding the time or place of the testified event. It begins by noting that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not address this topic, but it is covered in al-Kafi. The principle is: if the subject matter is a pure statement (qawl), like sale, divorce, etc., disagreement in time or place does not invalidate the testimony because statements can be repeated. If it is an act (fi'l), like assault or usurpation, disagreement invalidates because the act in one time/place is a different event. For marriage and similar contracts that require witness presence as an act, disagreement also invalidates. There is a specific dispute regarding accusation of adultery (qadhf): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say disagreement invalidates because the testimonies become inconsistent (one might be direct accusation, the other a report). Abu Hanifa, however, accepts it because they can be reconciled as one reporting the other's accusation. For contracts like pledge, gift, and charity that require delivery (qabd) as an act, there is a view from Muhammad that they are like statements, but the majority (the two shaykhs) consider them as acts annexed to statements, so disagreement in time/place invalidates only if they testify to witnessing the delivery. However, if they testify to an admission of delivery, disagreement does not invalidate. The passage also includes exceptions for trivial details like clothing or presence of others, where disagreement does not invalidate. The overarching principle is that pure statements are not time/place-sensitive, while acts and conditions are. This is a critical refinement of the earlier general rules from al-Kafi, incorporating the positions of the founding imams and later jurists like Qadi Khan.

Key Terms
فعل ملحق بالقول (fi'l mulhaq bi al-qawl): An act annexed to a statement, like loan (where the statement of lending is followed by delivery); the act is considered analogous to the statement.
إنشاء (insha'): Direct declaration creating a legal effect, e.g., 'You are divorced,' or 'You committed adultery' (as a direct accusation).
إقرار (iqrar): Admission or acknowledgement, e.g., 'I admit that I delivered the pledge.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs, testimony on a pledge (rahn) is invalid if witnesses disagree in time/place. However, Qadi Khan made an exception. What is that exception?
A) If the pledge is in writing.
B) If the witnesses testify to witnessing the delivery (qabd).
C) If the pledge is of high value.
D) If the witnesses are relatives.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school further refines the rule: contracts requiring delivery like pledge are treated as acts, but Qadi Khan's exception allows testimony on witnessing delivery to be accepted despite disagreement.

Testimony for Qadhf with Temporal or Spatial Difference
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting qadhf testimony when witnesses differ on time or place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on qadhf testimony when witnesses differ on time or place and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In qadhf, if witnesses differ on time/place, Abu Hanifa accepts testimony; Sahibayn reject it because of the insha'/ikhbar distinction.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the acceptance of testimony in a qadhf (false accusation of zina) case when the two witnesses disagree on the time or place of the alleged statement. The disagreement centers on whether such a difference indicates a contradiction in the testimony or merely a variation in how the utterance was perceived (as a direct accusation or a report of an accusation). Understanding this dispute refines your ability to analyse witness testimony in hadd cases and appreciate the strictness required in qadhf proceedings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify what Abu Hanifa holds regarding the acceptance of qadhf testimony when witnesses differ on time or place. Abu Hanifa accepts the testimony based on the possibility that one witness heard the direct accusation (insha') and the other heard a report of that accusation (ikhbar).
This is the minority position within the school.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: they reject the testimony. Understand their two-part reasoning: (a) if both utterances are insha', they are separate acts requiring two witnesses for each; (b) if one is insha' and the other ikhbar, they are incompatible because insha' and ikhbar are distinct forms of speech.
The Sahibayn's view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
Analyse the proof of each side
Abu Hanifa relies on ihtimal (possibility) – that the two witnesses could be testifying to the same slander heard in two ways. The Sahibayn argue that the nature of the utterances (insha' vs ikhbar) creates a true contradiction in the testimony, so it cannot be accepted.
No textual evidence is cited; the dispute is based on rational analysis (talil).
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, the testimony is accepted, and the hadd punishment for qadhf can be imposed on the accused. Under the Sahibayn's view, the testimony is rejected, and the accused is not liable for hadd unless other evidence exists.
The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn, so in practice the testimony is rejected.
5
Apply the mufta bihi to a scenario
Given a case where witnesses differ on time or place, state the ruling per the mufta bihi: the testimony is not accepted, and the qadhf case fails. Then explain why this strictness is justified in hadd cases.
Hadd punishments require the highest level of certainty; any significant discrepancy undermines certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال أبو يوسف ومحمد: إذا اختلف شاهدا القذف في مكان أو زمان لا تقبل وإن كان قولاً لأن كل واحد منهما إن كان إنشاء فهو غيران وليس على كل قذف شاهدان، وإن كان أحدهما إنشاء والآخر إخباراً فهما لا يتفقان لأن الإنشاء أن يقول زنيت أو أنت [؟زان] والإخبار أن يقول قذفتك بالزنا، وأبو حنيفة يقول : يحتمل أنه أحدهما الإنشاء والآخر الإخبار فيثبت عندهما قذفه سمع فشهدا به اهـ.
Then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If the two witnesses of slander differ in place or time, it is not accepted even if it is a statement, because each one of them, if it is creation (insha') it is two different things [?] and there are not two witnesses for every slander; and if one is creation and the other is report (ikhbar), they do not agree because creation is to say 'you committed zina' or 'you are a fornicator' and report is to say 'I accused you of zina'. And Abu Hanifa says: It is possible that one is creation and the other report, so the slander he heard is established with them and they testified accordingly.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the acceptance of testimony for slander (qadhf) when the two witnesses differ on the time or place of the alleged utterance. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) reject the testimony. Their reasoning: if both utterances are creations (insha'), they are distinct acts and two witnesses are needed for each distinct qadhf; if one is creation and the other is report (ikhbar), the two statements are incompatible because creation is a direct accusation and report is a claim of having made an accusation. Abu Hanifa, however, accepts the testimony, arguing that it is possible that one witness heard the creation and the other heard the report, both referring to the same act of slander. The ruling in the school is that the view of the Sahibayn is the relied-upon position for fatwa, as qadhf requires strict proof.

Key Terms
إنشاء (insha’): An utterance that creates a legal effect directly, e.g., 'You are a fornicator' (a direct accusation).
إخبار (ikhbar): An utterance that reports a past event, e.g., 'I accused you of zina'.
قذف (qadhf): The act of accusing a person of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) without four witnesses.
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Difference or disagreement; here, the witnesses differ on time or place of the alleged utterance.
مفتى به (mufta bihi): The relied-upon position for issuing fatwa.
احتمال (ihtimal): Possibility; the legal principle that if a plausible reconciliation exists, the testimony may be accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is testimony on qadhf rejected when witnesses differ on time or place?
A) Because the witnesses are lying.
B) Because if both are insha', each is a separate act; if one insha' and one ikhbar, they are incompatible.
C) Because the qadhf is not proven.
D) Because the time difference is too great.

Key Takeaway
In qadhf testimony, the Sahibayn's view (rejection when witnesses differ on time/place) is the mufta bihi due to the strictness of hadd punishments.

Testimony for Contracts Completed by Act: Classification and Ikhtilaf
Ruling on testimony with classification of differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify contracts based on their completion (act or saying) and determine whether a difference in witness testimony invalidates it according to the Hanafi school, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
For contracts completed by act, difference in testimony invalidates; but Muhammad treats them like pure sayings.

This passage from Jami' al-Fusulayn presents a detailed classification of how differences in witness testimony affect validity depending on the nature of the contract. Contracts are not all treated equally: those completed by an act (like rahn, hiba, sadaqa) are generally invalidated by any difference in time, place, or narration, except according to Imam Muhammad who likens them to purely verbal contracts. Understanding this classification is key to mastering the Hanafi rules on testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exception
Note that for contracts completed by an act (fi'l) such as rahn, hiba, sadaqa, a difference in time or place among witnesses invalidates the testimony. However, Imam Muhammad holds that these are like pure sayings and difference does not invalidate.
The exception is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the three categories of difference
The passage states that differences can be in time, place, or in the act of creation/acknowledgment (insha'/iqrar). Each category has four subtypes concerning the contract's nature.
This classification helps determine the effect of any discrepancy.
3
Apply the rule to each subtype
For each category, the contract is considered: (a) an act (fi'l) – difference prevents acceptance; (b) a pure saying (qawl mahd) – difference does not prevent; (c) an act annexed to a saying (qard) – difference does not prevent; (d) the opposite (saying annexed to act, like nikah) – difference prevents.
The key distinction is whether the contract is completed by a physical act or a verbal utterance.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The majority (the two shaykhs – Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that rahn, hiba, sadaqa are acts and thus difference invalidates. Imam Muhammad treats them as pure sayings. The passage notes that this is the view of Muhammad, while the two shaykhs differ.
The mufta bihi is the majority view, though Muhammad's view is acknowledged.
5
Conclude with the operative ruling
For fatwa, the relied-upon position is that testimony for contracts completed by act is invalidated by difference in time or place. This applies to rahn, hiba, and sadaqa. For pure sayings (sale, absolute rahn) and acts annexed to sayings (qard), difference does not invalidate. For sayings annexed to acts (nikah), it does.
This classification is consistent with earlier sources like al-Kafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جامع الفصولين : الشهادة بعقد تمامه بالفعل كرهن وهبة وصدقه يبطلها الاختلاف في زمان ومكان إلا عند محمد ا هـ . فعلم به أن ما في الكافي من أن الرهن والهبة والصدقة من قبيل البيع ونحوه قول محمد وقول الشيخين بخلافه والحاصل كما في جامع الفصولين أن الاختلاف لا يخلو من وجوه ثلاثة : إما في زمان أو مكان أو إنشاء أو إقرار، وكل منها لا يخلو من أربعة أوجه : إما في الفعل أو في القول أو في فعل ملحق بالقول أو عكسه. أما الفعل فيمنع قبول الشهادة في الوجوه الثلاثة، وأما القول المحض كبيع ورهن مطلقاً. وأما الفعل الملحق بالقول وهو القرض فلا يمنع وأما عكسه كنكاح فيمنع وهذا موافق لما في الكافي
And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Testimony for a contract whose completion is by an act, like rahn (pledge), hiba (gift), and sadaqa (charity), is invalidated by difference in time and place except according to Muhammad. So it is known from this that what is in al-Kafi—that rahn, hiba, and sadaqa are of the category of sale and the like—is the view of Muhammad, and the view of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) is contrary to that. And the summary is as in Jami' al-Fusulayn: the difference is not free from three aspects: either in time, or place, or insha' (creation) or iqrar (acknowledgment). And each of these is not free from four faces: either in act (fi'l), or in saying (qawl), or in an act annexed to a saying, or its opposite. As for the act, it prevents acceptance of testimony in all three aspects. As for pure sayings like sale and rahn absolutely, it does not prevent. As for an act annexed to a saying, which is qard (loan), it does not prevent, and as for its opposite like nikah (marriage), it prevents. And this agrees with what is in al-Kafi.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Jami' al-Fusulayn regarding testimony for contracts that are completed by an act (such as rahn, hiba, sadaqa). For these contracts, if witnesses differ on time or place, the testimony is invalidated—except according to Imam Muhammad, who apparently considers them like purely verbal contracts. The author then explains that this difference stems from the classification of differences into three categories: time, place, or nature (insha'/iqrar). Each category has four subcategories: act, saying, saying annexed to act, or act annexed to saying. The general rule: if the testimony concerns an act (fi'l), difference in any category prevents acceptance. For pure sayings (like sale or rahn), difference does not prevent. For acts annexed to sayings (like qard, where the saying 'I lend to you' is followed by the act of handing over), difference does not prevent. For sayings annexed to acts (like nikah, where the saying requires the presence of witnesses as an act), difference does prevent. This classification is consistent with earlier sources like al-Kafi.

Key Terms
فعل (fi'l): A physical action, as opposed to a verbal utterance. Here, it refers to the physical completion of a contract (e.g., handing over possession).
قول محض (qawl mahd): A purely verbal contract, like sale or rahn, where no physical delivery is required for validity.
فعل ملحق بالقول (fi'l mulhaq bi al-qawl): An act that is annexed to a saying, meaning the saying is primary but the act completes it, e.g., qard (the saying 'I lend' plus delivery).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the classification in Jami' al-Fusulayn, which type of contract is testimony invalidated by difference in time or place?
A) Pure saying like sale
B) Act annexed to saying like qard
C) Act (fi'l) such as rahn, hiba, sadaqa
D) All contracts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies contracts by their mode of completion (act vs. saying), which determines whether a difference in witness testimony invalidates the testimony.

Witnessing Possession vs. Acknowledging Possession: Qadikhan's Distinction
Intra-Hanafi distinction on testimony validity in possession-based contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between testimony based on witnessing physical possession and testimony based on acknowledgment of possession, and state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding time/place differences.

Core Idea
An act of possession is singular; an acknowledgment can be repeated — this nature determines testimony validity.

This passage from Qadikhan's Fatawa examines a critical nuance in testimony law: does a discrepancy in the time or place stated by witnesses automatically invalidate their testimony? The answer depends on whether the witnesses testify about witnessing the actual act of possession (mu'ayanat al-qabd) or about hearing an acknowledgment of possession (iqrar bi al-qabd). Qadikhan clarifies the Hanafi positions, highlighting an intra-madhhab disagreement on the first scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two testimony scenarios
Read the passage and list the two types of testimony: (1) testifying on witnessing the physical taking of possession; (2) testifying on hearing the party acknowledge possession.
These correspond to mu'ayanat al-qabd and iqrar bi al-qabd.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, state whether the testimony is valid or invalid. Note that for mu'ayanat al-qabd there is a dispute, while for iqrar all agree it is valid.
The phrase "fi qawlihima" refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn); "khilafan li Muhammad" indicates Imam Muhammad's opposing view.
3
Locate the point of ikhtilaf
Identify which scenario has disagreement. Only mu'ayanat al-qabd is disputed: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept it despite time/place differences; Imam Muhammad rejects it.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Understand the rationale
Explain why the distinction exists: witnessing possession is a single physical act — if witnesses differ on time/place, they may be referring to different events. Acknowledgment is a statement that can be repeated, so differing times/places do not contradict.
Imam Muhammad sees the physical act as requiring uniformity; the Sahibayn are more lenient.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Given a scenario where two witnesses testify about a gift delivery — one says Monday in Cairo, the other says Wednesday in Alexandria — determine the ruling under each imam's view.
This step reinforces the practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفصل قاضيخان في فتاواه في الرهن والهبة والصدقة بأنهم إذا شهدوا على معاينة القبض واختلفا في الأيام والبلدان جازت شهادتهم في قولهما خلافاً لمحمد، وإن شهدوا على إقرار الراهن والواهب والمتصدق بالقبض جازت في قولهم اهـ.
And Qadikhan detailed in his Fatawa regarding rahn, hiba, and sadaqa: that if they testify on witnessing physical possession (mu'ayanat al-qabd) and they differ in the days and countries, their testimony is valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Wait: 'fi qawlihima' refers to the two shaykhs?), contrary to Muhammad. And if they testify on the acknowledgment of the pledgor, donor, or charitable giver regarding possession (iqrar bi al-qabd), their testimony is valid in all their views.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
Qadikhan distinguishes between two types of testimony for contracts involving physical delivery: (1) Testimony based on witnessing the actual transfer of possession (mu'ayanat al-qabd). If the witnesses differ on the day or location, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) the testimony is accepted, contrary to Imam Muhammad. (2) Testimony based on hearing the person acknowledge having received possession (iqrar). In this case, the testimony is accepted by all (including Muhammad) because the subject is a statement (iqrar) which can be repeated, so difference in time or place does not harm. The phrase 'fi qawlihima' refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but note that earlier 'khilafan li Muhammad' indicates that Muhammad holds the opposite in the first scenario, so 'fi qawlihima' likely means the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) is that it is valid; Muhammad disagrees. This is consistent with the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
معاينة القبض (mu'ayanat al-qabd): Witnessing the actual physical taking of possession (e.g., handing over the pledged item).
إقرار بالقبض (iqrar bi al-qabd): A statement by the person that he has received possession; this is a verbal utterance, not an act.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of an item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When witnesses testified on witnessing possession
B) When witnesses testified on acknowledgment of possession

D) In neither case

Key Takeaway
Qadikhan distinguishes testimony on witnessing possession (disputed between Sahibayn and Muhammad) from testimony on acknowledgment of possession (unanimously valid).

Material vs. Inconsequential Differences in Testimony
Clarifications on place/time difference and inconsequential details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish material differences (time, place for acts) from inconsequential differences (clothing, presence) in witness testimony and state the Hanafi ruling on each.

Core Idea
Not every discrepancy in testimony invalidates; only differences that go to the core fact matter.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies when a difference in witnesses' accounts undermines their testimony in Hanafi fiqh. The first ruling equates a difference in place to a difference in time for acts, but notes the converse is not true. The second ruling demonstrates that trivial details like clothing color or the presence of a bystander do not affect validity. Understanding this helps evaluate witness reliability in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rulings
Parse the passage: first ruling deals with place vs. time difference; second ruling deals with differences in clothing or mention of a third person.
These are separate issues introduced by 'تنبيه' and 'وفي الخانية'.
2
Analyze the place/time rule
Apply the principle: for witnessing an act (e.g., a contract), a difference in place invalidates just as a difference in time does. However, for a speech act (e.g., talaq), a difference in place alone may not invalidate because the location is incidental to the utterance.
The text says 'ولا عكس' meaning the reverse does not hold: same place at different times can be valid.
3
Apply the inconsequential differences ruling
Examine the specifics: clothing of parties, type of mount, mention of a specific person – these are not deemed material to the core fact, so testimony remains valid.
Based on al-Asl (the main work of Imam Muhammad).
4
Evaluate a sample case
Present a scenario: two witnesses agree that Zayd borrowed from Amr, but one says it was in winter and the other says summer. Determine if testimony is invalidated based on the rules.
Difference in time for an act invalidates (unless it is a pure saying).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح ابن وهبان تنبيه الاختلاف في المكان الاختلاف في الزمان ولا عكس الجواز أن يشهد عليه في وقتين مختلفين في مكان واحد ا هـ . وفي الخانية : ولو اختلفا في الثياب التي كانت على الطالب أو المطلوب أو المركب أو قال أحدهما كان معنا فلان وقال الآخر لم يكن معنا، ذكر في الأصل أنه يجوز ولا تبطل هذه الشهادة ا هـ.
And in Sharh Ibn Wahban: a note: difference in place is like difference in time, but not vice versa; it is permissible to testify about him in two different times in one place. And in al-Khaniya: And if they differ regarding the clothes that were on the claimant or the defendant or the riding beast, or one said 'so-and-so was with us' and the other said 'he was not with us', it is mentioned in al-Asl that it is permissible, and this testimony is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This brief passage contains two separate rulings. First, from the commentary of Ibn Wahban: a reminder that a difference in place (city) is considered equivalent to a difference in time regarding its effect on testimony—i.e., both invalidate for acts—but the converse is not true: testimony at different times in the same place can be accepted. Second, from al-Khaniya (likely al-Khaniyya al-Kubra by al-Hasan ibn Mansur al-Uzjandi al-Farghani): minor differences in testimony, such as the color of clothes worn by the parties or whether a third person was present, do not invalidate the testimony. This illustrates that not every discrepancy is legally significant; only those that go to the core of the fact (e.g., time, place, or nature of the act) matter.

Key Terms
اختلاف في المكان (ikhtilaf fi al-makan): Witnesses give contradictory accounts of the location of the event.
اختلاف في الثياب (ikhtilaf fi al-thiyab): Witnesses differ on the description of clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Testimony is invalidated
B) Testimony is permissible and not invalidated
C) Testimony is accepted only if they agree on the shirt
D) Testimony is rejected

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, only discrepancies that affect the core fact (time, place for acts, identity) invalidate testimony; minor details like clothing are inconsequential.

The Principle of Ikhtilaf Fahish in Testimonies on Sayings
Rule on fahish difference in testimonies on sayings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on difference in time for testimonies on sayings and identify when an excessive difference (fahish) invalidates the testimony.

Core Idea
For sayings, difference in time is normally harmless, but excessive difference renders testimony void.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that a difference in time (e.g., yesterday vs. today) does not invalidate testimony about a verbal statement (qawl), because statements can be repeated. However, what if the difference is extremely large, like months vs. years? This lesson examines a case from al-Qunyah where such a fahish difference led to rejection, even though the witnesses were not required to give a date.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The author states that the apparent meaning of their (the Hanafi jurists) absolute statements is that difference in time for sayings does not prevent acceptance. Note that they exemplify with a small difference (yesterday vs. today).
This rule applies even if the difference is large, based on the absolute wording.
2
Analyze the exception from al-Qunyah
Read the case: two witnesses differ by about 2 years (seven months vs. three years). The judge rejects their testimony because the difference is excessive (fahish), even though they were not required to give a date. Determine what makes this difference 'fahish'.
The key is that the difference is so extreme that reconciliation is impossible.
3
Extract the ruling
State the rule: For testimonies on sayings, difference in time is normally not a problem. However, if the difference is excessive (fahish), the testimony is rejected. This is a qualification of the general absolute rule.
The ruling is about admissibility, not about the underlying act.
4
Contrast with small differences
Compare with the case of 'yesterday and today' – a small difference does not invalidate because the statement could have been repeated on both days. The excessive case shows that when the gap is too large, the witnesses cannot both be testifying to the same event.
The threshold for 'fahish' depends on the context and how far back the event is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن ظاهر إطلاقهم أن الاختلاف في الزمان في الأقوال غير مانع شامل لما إذا تفاحش أو لا لأنهم يمثلونه بأمس واليوم وهو ليس بمتفاحش. وفي القنية : أقام شاهدين على الصلح فالجأهما القاضي إلى بيان التاريخ فقال أحدهما أظن كان منذ سبعة أشهر أو أقل أو أكثر وقال الآخر أظن منذ ثلاث سنين أو أزيد لا تقبل لما اختلفا هذا الاختلاف الفاحش وإن كان لا يحتاجان إلى بيان التاريخ ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير قبيل باب تفويض الطلاق معزياً إلى كافي الحاكم: لو اختلفا في الوقت أو المكان أو الزمان بأن شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها يوم النحر بمكة والآخر أنه طلقها في ذلك اليوم بالكوفة فهي باطلة لتيقن كذب أحدهما، ولو شهدا بذلك في يومين متفرقين بينهما في الأيام قدر ما يسير الراكب من الكوفة إلى مكة جازت شهادتهما، ولو شهد اثنان أنه طلق عمرة يوم النحر بالكوفة والآخر أنه طلق زينب يوم النحر بمكة فشهادتهما باطلة، ولو جاءت إحدى البينتين فقضى بها ثم جاءت الأخرى لم يلتفت إليها ا هـ. وهذا أيضاً مقيد لقولهم إن الاختلاف في الزمان لا يضر في الأقوال فيقال إلا إذا ذكرا مكانين متباعدين . قوله : (ولو شهدا أنه قتل زيدا يوم النحر بمكة وآخران أنه قتله بمصر ردتا) أي لم تقبل الشهادتان لأن إحداهما كاذبة وليست إحداهما بأولى من الأخرى. وأشار إلى أنهما لو اختلفا في الزمان أو الآلة التي وقع القتل بها لم تقبل لما بينا . وذكر في السراج الوهاج : وفائدة ذلك إذا قال إن لم أحج العام فعبدي حر فأقام العبد شاهدين أنه قتل يوم النحر بالكوفة فأقام الورثة أنه قتل بمكة ا هـ . وقيد بكون المشهود به القتل لأنهم لو شهدوا على إقرار القاتل بذلك في وقتين أو مكانين تقبل لأنه قول يعاد ويكرر ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج.
Then know that the apparent meaning of their absolute statements is that difference in time for sayings is not a preventer, encompassing whether it is excessive (mutafahish) or not, because they exemplify it with 'yesterday and today' which is not excessive. And in al-Qunyah: He brought two witnesses for a settlement (sulh) and the judge compelled them to specify the date. One said 'I think it was seven months ago or less or more' and the other said 'I think three years ago or more'. It is not accepted because they differed with this excessive difference, even though they were not required to specify the date. And in Fath al-Qadir, just before the chapter on delegation of divorce, citing Kafi al-Hakim: If they differ in the time or place or hour, such that one witnesses that he divorced her on the Day of Sacrifice in Mecca and the other that he divorced her on that same day in Kufa, it is void because of certainty that one of them is lying. And if they testifed to that on two separate days between which is the distance a rider can travel from Kufa to Mecca, their testimony is valid. And if two testify that he divorced 'Amrah on the Day of Sacrifice in Kufa and another two that he divorced Zaynab on the Day of Sacrifice in Mecca, their testimony is void. And if one of the two proofs (bayyinatan) comes and judgment is given based on it, then the other comes, no attention is paid to it. And this also restricts their statement that difference in time does not harm for sayings; so it is said: except when they mention two distant places. His statement: (and if two testify that he killed Zayd on the Day of Sacrifice in Mecca and another two that he killed him in Egypt, both are rejected), i.e., both testimonies are not accepted because one of them is lying, and neither is more likely than the other. And he indicated that if they differed in time or the instrument (weapon) with which the killing occurred, it is also not accepted for the reason we explained. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The benefit of this is if he said 'If I do not perform Hajj this year, my slave is free', and the slave brings two witnesses that he (the master) was killed on the Day of Sacrifice in Kufa, and the heirs bring two witnesses that he was killed in Mecca. And it is restricted to the subject matter being killing, because if they testified on the killer's confession (iqrar) regarding that in two different times or places, it would be accepted because it is a statement that can be repeated; thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This extended passage addresses several interconnected points about the effect of excessive (fahish) differences and contradictory testimonies. It begins by noting that the general rule—that difference in time for sayings does not prevent acceptance—applies even when the difference is large, but they typically exemplify with a small difference (yesterday/today). However, al-Qunyah provides a case where the difference is so large (seven months vs. three years) that the testimony is rejected, even though the witnesses were not required to specify a date. Then, from Fath al-Qadir, we have cases of divorce and murder: if two witnesses give contradictory places for the same divorce (Mecca vs. Kufa on the same day), it is void because one must be lying. But if the times are far enough apart to allow travel, it is accepted (the same divorce is possible at both places at different times). If the witnesses testify about divorcing two different women on the same day in distant cities, both testimonies are void, and if one case is judged first, the later is ignored. For a murder, if two witnesses say it happened in Mecca and two in Egypt, both testimonies are rejected. However, if the witnesses testify on the killer's confession (iqrar) to the murder at different times/places, it is accepted because a statement (unlike a unique act) can be repeated. The key distinction is between acts (unique, cannot be contradictory) and statements (repeatable, so differences do not necessarily imply lying).

Key Terms
اختلاف فاحش (ikhtilaf fahish): An excessive disparity in testimony regarding time or place that makes reconciliation impossible, e.g., months vs. years.
إقرار (iqrar): A confession or acknowledgment, a verbal statement that can be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In al-Qunyah's case, why was the testimony rejected despite the witnesses not being required to give a date?
A) Because they gave different dates voluntarily
B) Because the difference was excessive (fahish)
C) Because the settlement was invalid
D) Because the judge did not ask for dates

Key Takeaway
For testimonies on sayings, difference in time is harmless unless it is excessive (fahish), in which case the testimony is void.
