Contradictory Testimonies in Divorce and Murder with the Iqrar Exception
Cases of contradictory testimonies in divorce and murder with iqrar exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that contradictory testimonies on an act (divorce, murder) are void if irreconcilable, and distinguish the exception for testimonies on iqrar (confession).

Core Idea
Irreconcilable testimonies on a single act are void; but testimonies on a statement (iqrar) are valid despite differences.

This lesson explores several practical examples from Fath al-Qadir and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that illustrate when contradictory testimonies are rejected. The key distinction is between testimonies about an act (fi‘l) – which cannot occur in two different places at the same time – and testimonies about a verbal statement (qawl/iqrar), which can be repeated. Understanding this distinction is essential for judges, muftis, and students of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the first divorce case
Two witnesses say a divorce occurred in Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice; two others say in Kufa on the same day. Since the same divorce cannot happen in two cities simultaneously, the testimonies are void because one must be lying.
The key is the impossibility of the same act occurring in two distant places at the same time.
2
Compare the conditional acceptance case
If the times are far enough apart (e.g., the distance a rider can travel), then the testimonies can be reconciled: the divorce could have occurred in Mecca first, then the couple moved to Kufa and divorced again. Thus, the testimonies are accepted.
Reconciliation is possible if the time gap allows travel between the two places.
3
Analyze the different-person case
If two witnesses say he divorced 'Amrah in Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice and two others say he divorced Zaynab in Kufa on the same day, both testimonies are void because they contradict each other regarding the same person? Actually, they are about different women, but the passage says they are void. Why? Because the two sets of witnesses cannot both be correct about the same husband performing two divorces at the exact same time in different cities? The text says 'shahadatuhuma batila' – both testimonies are invalid.
The rationale: even though the women are different, the impossibility of being in two places at once makes both testimonies suspect.
4
Apply the murder case
Two witnesses say Zayd was killed in Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice; two others say in Egypt on the same day. Both testimonies are rejected because the same killing cannot occur in two faraway places simultaneously. Neither set is more likely, so both are void.
Also applies if they differ on time or weapon.
5
Distinguish the iqrar exception
If the testimonies are about the killer's confession (iqrar) at different times or places, they are accepted because a confession is a statement (qawl) that can be repeated. The same confession can be made in Mecca and later in Kufa.
This exception is explicitly limited to testimonies on sayings, not acts.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Proof or evidence; especially two witnesses (or one male + two females) on a fact.
إقرار (iqrar): A confession or acknowledgment, a verbal statement that can be repeated.

The Ruling on Contradictory Testimony Regarding Time and Place
Ruling on contradictory testimony in time and place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on contradictory testimony regarding time and place, distinguish gross from minor contradictions, and identify the exception for admissions (iqrar).

Core Idea
If witnesses contradict in a way that makes both accounts impossible, both testimonies are rejected; but testimony on admissions is accepted because statements can be repeated.

In Hanafi fiqh, testimony (shahada) must be consistent in essential details. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains what happens when witnesses disagree on the time or place of an event. This lesson will help you understand the key distinction between gross contradictions, which invalidate testimony, and minor differences, which do not. An important exception is made for admissions (iqrar), where differing accounts are accepted because an admission is considered a statement that can be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act testified about
Determine whether the testimony concerns a substantive fact (like a killing or divorce) or an admission (iqrar). The ruling differs based on this distinction.
Substantive facts: killing, divorce, etc. Admissions: a party's confession.
2
Assess the nature of the contradiction
Evaluate whether the difference in time or place is gross (ikhtilaf fahish) or minor. Gross contradiction means the accounts cannot both be true (e.g., same day in two far apart cities). Minor difference allows for possibility (e.g., yesterday vs. today).
Example: Mecca and Egypt on the same day is gross; yesterday and today is minor.
3
Apply the rule for substantive testimonies
If the contradiction is gross, both testimonies are rejected (tardu). If only one testimony came first and the judge ruled on it, the later contradictory testimony is not considered.
The principle: lammā kāna mustaḥīlan jam‘uhumā – because it is impossible to combine them.
4
Apply the exception for admissions
If the testimony is about an admission (iqrar), even if witnesses differ in time or place, the testimony is accepted because an admission can be repeated and reiterated.
This is because iqrar is a statement (qawl) that can be made multiple times, unlike a single event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
يوم النحر بمكة وآخران أنه قتله بمصر ردتا فإن قضى بإحداهما أولاً بطلت
بأمس واليوم وهو ليس بمتفاحش. وفي القنية : أقام شاهدين على الصلح فالجأهما القاضي إلى بيان التاريخ فقال أحدهما أظن كان منذ سبعة أشهر أو أقل أو أكثر وقال الآخر أظن منذ ثلاث سنين أو أزيد لا تقبل لما اختلفا هذا الاختلاف الفاحش وإن كان لا يحتاجان إلى بيان التاريخ ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير قبيل باب تفويض الطلاق معزياً إلى كافي الحاكم: لو اختلفا في الوقت أو المكان أو الزمان بأن شهد أحدهما أنه طلقها يوم النحر بمكة والآخر أنه طلقها في ذلك اليوم بالكوفة فهي باطلة لتيقن كذب أحدهما، ولو شهدا بذلك في يومين متفرقين بينهما في الأيام قدر ما يسير الراكب من الكوفة إلى مكة جازت شهادتهما، ولو شهد اثنان أنه طلق عمرة يوم النحر بالكوفة والآخر أنه طلق زينب يوم النحر بمكة فشهادتهما باطلة، ولو جاءت إحدى البينتين فقضى بها ثم جاءت الأخرى لم يلتفت إليها ا هـ. وهذا أيضاً مقيد لقولهم إن الاختلاف في الزمان لا يضر في الأقوال فيقال إلا إذا ذكرا مكانين متباعدين .
قوله : (ولو شهدا أنه قتل زيدا يوم النحر بمكة وآخران أنه قتله بمصر ردتا) أي لم تقبل الشهادتان لأن إحداهما كاذبة وليست إحداهما بأولى من الأخرى. وأشار إلى أنهما لو اختلفا في الزمان أو الآلة التي وقع القتل بها لم تقبل لما بينا . وذكر في السراج الوهاج : وفائدة ذلك إذا قال إن لم أحج العام فعبدي حر فأقام العبد شاهدين أنه قتل يوم النحر بالكوفة فأقام الورثة أنه قتل بمكة ا هـ . وقيد بكون المشهود به القتل لأنهم لو شهدوا على إقرار القاتل بذلك في وقتين أو مكانين تقبل لأنه قول يعاد ويكرر ؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج.
Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Disagreement in Testimony. On the day of sacrifice in Mecca and two others that he killed him in Egypt, both are rejected. If he adjudicated by one first, it is invalidated. Yesterday and today, and it is not grossly contradictory. And in Al-Qunyah: He brought two witnesses to the reconciliation, and the judge compelled them to state the date. One said, 'I think it was seven months ago, or less, or more,' and the other said, 'I think it was three years ago or more.' They are not accepted because they differed in this gross difference, even though they are not required to state the date. End quote. And in Fath al-Qadir, just before the chapter on delegation of divorce, citing Kafi al-Hakim: If they differ in the time, place, or period—as when one testifies that he divorced her on the day of sacrifice in Mecca and the other testifies that he divorced her on that day in Kufa—then it is invalid because it is certain that one of them is lying. If they so testify on two separate days between which there is a travel distance from Kufa to Mecca, their testimony is valid. If two testify that he divorced Amra on the day of sacrifice in Kufa and another two that he divorced Zaynab on the day of sacrifice in Mecca, their testimony is invalid. If one of the two pieces of evidence comes and he adjudicates by it, then the other comes, it is not considered. End quote. This also restricts their statement that difference in time does not harm in statements, so it is said: except if they mention two distant places. His saying: (And if two testify that he killed Zayd on the day of sacrifice in Mecca and two others that he killed him in Egypt, both are rejected) meaning the two testimonies are not accepted because one of them is false, and one is not more deserving than the other. He indicated that if they differ in time or the instrument by which the killing occurred, they are not accepted, as we explained. And it is mentioned in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The benefit of this is if one says, 'If I do not perform Hajj this year, my slave is free,' and the slave brings two witnesses that he was killed on the day of sacrifice in Kufa, and the heirs bring witnesses that he was killed in Mecca. End quote. And it is restricted to the case being about killing, because if they testify to the killer's admission of that at two times or places, it is accepted because it is a statement that can be repeated and reiterated; so in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage deals with the rules of contradictory testimony in terms of time and place. It begins by stating that if two witnesses testify about an event (a killing or divorce) and two others testify about the same event but with a different time or place that is mutually exclusive (e.g., one says it happened in Mecca on the Day of Sacrifice, the other says in Egypt on the same day), both testimonies are rejected because one must be false, and neither has precedence over the other. The text clarifies that even a difference in the instrument of killing (e.g., one says killed with a sword, the other with a knife) also leads to rejection. However, an exception is made for admissions (iqrar): if the witnesses testify that the killer admitted the act at different times or places, that testimony is accepted because a statement can be repeated and reiterated. The passage also cites examples from Fath al-Qadir about divorce cases, emphasizing that if the time difference is such that the two events are physically possible (e.g., travel time between Kufa and Mecca), then testimony is valid. The overall principle is that gross contradiction (ikhtilaf fahish) that makes it impossible for both accounts to be true leads to rejection of both testimonies.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given by a witness in court about a fact or event.
اختلاف فاحش (ikhtilaf fahish): A gross contradiction in testimony that makes it impossible for both accounts to be true.
إقرار (iqrar): Admission or confession by a party; testimony on admission can differ in time/place because admissions can be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that Zaid was killed on the Day of Sacrifice in Makkah; two others testify he was killed on the same day in Egypt. What is the ruling?
A) The first testimony is accepted and the second rejected.
B) Both testimonies are rejected because one must be false.
C) Both testimonies are accepted and the judge chooses.
D) The testimony with more witnesses is accepted.

Key Takeaway
Gross contradiction in time or place that makes two testimonies irreconcilable leads to rejection of both, except for testimonies about admissions, which are accepted due to the repeatable nature of statements.

Shahadat — Testimony

Preference Rules for Conflicting Evidence: Death, Gifts, and Manumission During Illness
Three specific cases of conflicting evidence with preference rules.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi preference rule for conflicting evidence in three scenarios: death from wound vs. recovery, gift in health vs. illness, and manumission during illness.

Core Idea
When evidence conflicts, preference is given to the evidence that aligns with the stronger presumption.

This lesson introduces the first three cases from a collection of sixteen rules for resolving conflicting evidence (ta'arud al-bayyinat) in Hanafi fiqh. These cases illustrate how the school prioritizes evidence based on the circumstances, such as whether the underlying act occurred during health or illness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
For each case, list what each party is trying to prove.
Case 1: guardians prove death by wound; injurer proves recovery and later death.
2
Note the preferred evidence
The text explicitly states which evidence is 'awla (preferred). Record it.
Case 1: evidence of the killed is preferred.
3
Infer the underlying presumption
Consider why one evidence is stronger. Often it relates to a default state (e.g., health, freedom).
Case 1: The presumption is that the wound caused death, unless proven otherwise.
4
Compare with adjacent cases
Notice how the same presumption (e.g., health) appears in multiple cases.
Case 2: gift in health vs. illness; evidence of health is preferred.

قوله : (وعلى هذا التفصيل إذا اختلف البائع والمشتري في صحة البيع وفساده) قال في تعارض البحر الرائق ج۷/ م ١٣
And it has been mentioned in Al-Qunyah, from the chapter on two conflicting pieces of evidence and preferring one over the other, useful branches that are needed. We will mention them concisely in issues: First: The guardians of the wounded prove that he died from the wound, and the injurer proves that he was healed and died after ten days. The evidence of the killed is preferred. Second: And if [two] pieces of evidence conflict that the copy... except that they [؟], so it is a correction to the absolute. And his saying: 'And in Al-Qunyah' another correction supporting the first correction. His saying: (The evidence of the killed is preferred) agrees with what is in Al-Qunyah from the chapter on two conflicting pieces of evidence, but in the end of the book of claims in Al-Khulasa: They brought evidence, this on health and the other on death by beating, so the evidence of health is preferred. Similarly in Al-Bazzaziyya and Mushtamil al-Ahkam, and by it Mufti Abu al-Su'ud gave fatwa. End. Summarized from Ta'arud al-Bayyinat by Sheikh Ghanim al-Baghdadi. And in Al-Fatawa al-Hamidiyya citing some fatwas: Evidence of solvency is preferred over evidence of insolvency; evidence of death from wound is preferred over evidence of death after recovery; evidence of the claimant of a gift in health is preferred over evidence of gift during illness; evidence of the claimant of voluntariness is preferred over the claimant of compulsion but the relied-upon is contrary; evidence of health [is preferred]. [Evidence of] fraud and similar value in the sale of an orphan's property by the executor, so evidence of fraud is preferred. Third: The slave girl proves that he freed her during his terminal illness while sane, and the heirs prove that he was of confused mind, so the evidence of the slave girl is preferred, likewise in khul'. Fourth: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning fraud and equivalent value in the father's sale of his child's property, and dispute between buyer and son after reaching majority; there are two sayings. Fifth: Two pieces of evidence conflict that he sold while adult or while minor; the buyer's evidence is preferred because it establishes the incidental. Sixth: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning the woman's discharge of her husband during her health or illness; two sayings. Seventh: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning admission for the heir during the health of the admitter or his illness; the evidence is for the beneficiary of the admission, and the statement is for the heirs in its absence, and he has them swear. Eighth: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning coercion and voluntariness in authorization; the evidence of voluntariness is preferred, and if he adjudicates by evidence of coercion in authorization, it is executed. Ninth: Two pieces of evidence conflict that the sale was valid or coerced; two sayings. Tenth: Two pieces of evidence conflict that the sale was absolute or as security; the evidence is for the claimant of security. Eleventh: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning dislike and willingness in sale, reconciliation, and coercion; the evidence of dislike is preferred. Twelfth: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning whether the wife of the deceased was forbidden six months before his death or permissible at the time of death; the woman's evidence is preferred. He has a niche in the public way, then another claims it is new and the owner claims it is old, and they bring evidence; the evidence is for the one who claims it is new, and it is said the statement is for the claimant because he holds the original. Thirteenth: The evidence of the outsider against the endowment absolutely conflicts with the evidence of the possessor that his seller bought it from the endower and dated; the evidence of the endowment is preferred, and it is said except if the date of the possessor is earlier. Fourteenth: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning the validity and invalidity of the endowment; if the invalidity is due to a corrupt condition in the endowment, the evidence of invalidity is preferred; if it is due to a meaning in the subject itself or otherwise, the evidence of validity is preferred. According to this detail, if the seller and buyer differ concerning the validity and invalidity of the sale. Fifteenth: Two pieces of evidence conflict concerning absolute ownership from an outsider and purchase from another from the possessor; the evidence of the claimant of absolute ownership is preferred. Sixteenth: Two pieces of evidence conflict... [list continues] The evidence of the claimant of dower is preferred over the claimant of a gift; evidence of sanity is preferred over being insane at the time of khul'; evidence of the pre-emptor is preferred over the buyer's evidence; evidence that the person acting was sane is preferred over evidence that he was insane; evidence of the outsider is preferred over the possessor's evidence in claiming absolute ownership; evidence of security is preferred over evidence of absolute; evidence of coercion is preferred over evidence of willingness; evidence of gift is preferred over evidence of loan; evidence of health is preferred over evidence of death; evidence of discharge is preferred over evidence of admission; evidence of sale is preferred over evidence of pledge; evidence of loan is preferred over evidence of mudaraba; evidence of ownership is preferred over evidence of usurpation; evidence of recent origin is preferred over evidence of antiquity; evidence of pledge is preferred over evidence of gift; evidence of ownership transfer is preferred over evidence of loan; evidence of health is preferred over evidence of illness; evidence of invalid is preferred over evidence of valid; evidence of sale is preferred over evidence of gift; evidence of old building is preferred over evidence of new building. And the rest of it is in it, so refer to it; so in Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar by Sheikh Khalil al-Atfal. His saying: (According to this detail, if the seller and buyer differ concerning the validity and invalidity of the sale) He said in Ta'arud of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, volume 7, page 13.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rules for resolving conflicting evidence (تعارض البينات) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by referencing Al-Qunyah and then lists sixteen numbered issues (مسائل) plus additional summary from later sources. Each issue presents a specific scenario where two parties present conflicting evidence, and the ruling states which evidence is given preference (أولى). For example, if the guardians of a wounded person prove he died from the wound, and the injurer proves he recovered and died later, the evidence of the wounded party's side is preferred. In a case of conflicting evidence about whether a sale was during majority or minority, the buyer's evidence is preferred because it establishes the incidental (i.e., the sale occurred). The passage also covers cases involving fraud, endowment validity, coercion vs. voluntariness, and many others. The final part from Hashiyat al-Durr al-Mukhtar provides a list of general preferences (e.g., evidence of sale is preferred over evidence of pledge). The student should note that these rules are specific to Hanafi jurisprudence and reflect the school's method of tarjih (preference) when evidence conflicts. The passage does not provide the underlying reasoning for each rule but focuses on the applied rulings.

Key Terms
تعارض البينات (ta'arud al-bayyinat): Conflict between two or more pieces of evidence that lead to contradictory conclusions.
أولى (awla): Preferable or given precedence in a case of conflicting evidence.
بينة (bayyina): Evidence, typically testimony of two witnesses or other proof, in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of conflicting evidence regarding whether a slave was freed during the master's terminal illness while sane or confused, which evidence is preferred according to the text?
A) The heirs' evidence that the master was confused.
B) The slave's evidence that the master was sane.
C) The evidence of the executor.
D) The evidence of the judge.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi preference rules for conflicting evidence rely on presumptions such as causation, health, and sanity to determine which evidence is stronger.

Shahadat — Testimony

Preferring One Testimony Over Another: Key Hanafi Rules
List of rules for preferring conflicting testimonies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule for preferring conflicting testimonies and apply it to at least five specific scenarios from this passage.

Core Idea
Preference goes to the testimony that establishes the stronger legal default, not the one with more witnesses.

When two testimonies conflict, the Hanafi judge must determine which is more deserving (awlā). This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq enumerates numerous scenarios, each decided based on underlying legal principles such as continuity (istishāb), default validity, and substantive strength. Instead of rote memorization, learning the principles will let you derive the ruling for novel cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
For each scenario, clearly state what each party claims. For example, in rule 3: the slave woman claims a valid pawn during sanity; the heirs claim the owner was insane at the time.
Begin by isolating the precise legal issue in dispute.
2
Determine the legal default
Hanafi law presumes a default state: sanity (ishah al-aql), adulthood, willingness (taw), validity of contracts, continuity of ownership, etc. Identify which default supports one party.
Istishāb (presumption of continuity) is often the basis.
3
Apply the rule of preference
The testimony that supports the default is generally preferred, unless a stronger substantive principle (e.g., protecting orphans from deception) overrides.
For example, testimony of deception over market value because the guardian must act in the orphan's best interest.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scenarios (e.g., rules 4, 6, 9) have two or more opinions. The muftā bihī (relied-upon) position is indicated; if not, the first mentioned is often the preferred one.
Be aware that not all rules are unanimous within the school.

كتاب الشهادات باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
الغبن ومثل القيمة في مبيع الوصي مال الصبي فبينة الغبن أولى. الثالثة برهنت الأمة على أنه رها في مرض موته وهو عاقل وبرهنت الورثة على أنه كان مخلوط العقل فبينة الأمة أولى، وكذا في الخلع. الرابعة تعارضت تعارضت بينتا الكره والطوع في البيع والصلح والإكراه فبينة الكره أولى. الثانية عشر تعارضت بينتا كون زوحة الميت حراماً قبل موته بستة أشهر أو حلالاً وقت الموت فبينة المرأة أولى. الثالثة عشرة تعارضت بينة الخارج على الوقف عليه مطلقاً مع بينة ذي اليد أن بائعي اشتراها من الواقف وأرخ فبينة الوقف أولى، وقيل إلا إذا سبق تاريخ ذي اليد. الرابعة عشرة تعارضت بينتا صحة الوقف وفساده فإن كان الفساد لشرط في الوقف مفسد فبينة الفساد أولى، وإن كان لمعنى في المحل وغيره فبينة الصحة أولى، وعلى هذا التفصيل إذا اختلف البائع والمشتري في صحة البيع وفساده الخامسة عشرة تعارضت بينتا الملك المطلق من الخارج والشراء من آخر من ذي اليد فبينة مدعي الملك المطلق أولى السادسة عشر تعارضت بينتا أولى من بينة الفساد في الشراء بينة مدعي المهر أولى من مدعي الهدية بينة العقل أولى من كونه مجنوناً وقت الخلع، بينة الشفيع أولى من بينة المشتري، بينة كون المتصرف عاقلاً أولى من بينة كونه مجنوناً، بينة الخارج أولى من بينة ذي اليد في دعوى الملك المطلق، بينة الوفاء أولى من بينة البتات، بينة الإكراه أولى من بينة الطوع، بينة الهبة أولى من بيئة العارية بينة الصحة أولى من بينة الموت بينة الإبراء أولى من بينة الإقرار بينة البيع أولى من بينة الرهن بينة القرض أولى من بينة المضاربة، بينة الملك أولى من بينة الغصب بينة الحدوث أولى من بينة السابعة عشرة تعارضت بينتا وجود الشرط وعدمه فبينة المرأة أولى الثامنة عشرة تعارضت بينتا بيع الوصي بعد عزله أو قبله فبينة المشتري أولى لما فيها من زيادة إثبات نفاذ الشراء أو سبق التاريخ، وقيل بينة العزل أولى، وكذا الطلاق والعتاق من الوكيل . التاسعة عشرة تعارضت بينتان في حمار وقال المدعي إنه ملكي غاب عني منذ ثمانية أشهر، وقال ذو اليد اشتريته منذ سبعة عشر شهراً وأقاما البينة فبينة المدعي أولى العشرون ادعت المرأة البراءة من المهر بشرط وادعاها زوجها مطلقة وأقام البينة فبينة المرأة أولى إن كان الشرط متعارفاً يصح الإبراء معه، وقيل بيئة الزوج أولى. الحادية والعشرون أقام أحد الأخوين بينة أن الدار التي في أيدينا كانت لأمي تركتها ميراثاً بيني وبين أبي، وأقام الآخر بينة أنها كانت لأبينا فتركها ميراثاً لنا فبينة الأول أولى لإثباته الزيادة. الثانية والعشرون أقامت المرأة البينة على المهر على أن زوجها كان مقراً بذلك إلى يومنا هذا وأقام الزوج البينة أنها أبرأته من هذا المهر الذي تدعي فبينة البراءة أولى، وكذا في الدين لأن بينة مدعي الدين بطلت بإقرار المدعى عليه لما ادعى البراءة ولم تبطل بينة البراءة، وهذا كشهود البيع والإقالة فإن بينة الإقالة أولى لبطلان بينة البيع بإقرار مدعي الإقالة، وينبغي أن يحفظ هذا الأصل فإنه يخرج به كثير من الواقعات. الثالثة والعشرون ادعى على رجل ستة دنانير فقال المدعى عليه إنه أبرأني عن هذه الدعوى فأقام بينة وأقام المدعي بينة أنه كان أقر له بستة دنانير قيل تصح دعوى الإقرار ثانياً، وقيل لا تصح، وقيل إن ذكر الخصم القبول أو التصديق في يصح . الرابعة والعشرون تعرضت بينة الصحة والفساد في الشراء ففيه قولان. الخامسة والعشرون تعارضت بينتا الإجازة والرد في بيع الفصولي فبينة المشتري أولى .
السادسة والعشرون تعارضت بينتا السكوت والرد في نكاح البكر فبينتها أولى بخلاف ما إذا برهن على إجازتها وهي على ردها فبينته أولى السابعة والعشرون تعارضت بينتا البيع والوقف عليه مسجلاً فبينة مدعي البيع أولى إلا إذا عين الواقف فبينة الوقف أولى لأنه مقضياً عليه فلا بد من التعيين كبينة الملك مع بيئة العتق ا هـ .
البينات للشيخ غانم البغدادي : إذا اختلف المتبايعان أحدهما يدعي الصحة والآخر يدعي الفساد شرطاً فاسداً أو أجلاً فاسداً كان القول قول مدعي الصحة والبينة بينة مدعي الفساد باتفاق الروايات وإن الفساد مدعي يدعي الفساد المعنى في صلب العقد بأن ادعى أنه اشتراه بألف درهم ورطل من الخمر والآخر يدعي البيع بألف درهم فيه روايتان ؛ عن أبي حنيفة في ظاهر الرواية القول قول من الصحة أيضاً والبينة بيئة الآخر كما في الوجه الأول، وفي رواية القول قول من يدعي الفساد، مشتمل الأحكام اهـ
Book of Testimonies: Chapter on Conflict in Testimony. Deception and similar value in the sale by the guardian of the orphan's property: the testimony of deception takes precedence. Third: The slave woman proved that he pawned [her?] in his death illness while sane, and the heirs proved he was of unsound mind: the slave woman's testimony takes precedence, and similarly in khul'. Fourth: Testimonies of deception and similar value conflict in the father's sale of his child's property, and dispute between buyer and child after majority: there are two opinions. Fifth: Two testimonies conflict that he sold while adult or while a minor: the buyer's testimony takes precedence because it establishes the contingent. Sixth: Two testimonies of a woman's discharge of her husband in health or illness: two opinions. Seventh: Two testimonies of acknowledgement to an heir in health or illness: the testimony is for the beneficiary, and the heirs have the say in its absence, and he may have them take an oath. Eighth: Testimonies of coercion and willingness in authorization: the testimony of willingness takes precedence, and if judgment was passed on the testimony of coercion in authorization, it is executed. Ninth: Two testimonies of sale valid or coerced: two opinions. Tenth: Two testimonies of absolute sale or on trust: the testimony is of the one claiming trust. Eleventh: Testimonies of dislike and willingness in sale, compromise, and coercion: the testimony of dislike takes precedence. Twelfth: Two testimonies that the dead man's wife was forbidden six months before his death or lawful at the time of death: the woman's testimony takes precedence. Thirteenth: The testimony of an outsider against the endowment absolutely with the testimony of the possessor that his seller bought it from the founder and dated: the endowment testimony takes precedence; it is said except if the possessor's date is earlier. Fourteenth: Testimonies of validity and invalidity of endowment conflict: if the invalidity is due to a corrupt condition in the endowment, the testimony of invalidity takes precedence; if it is due to a meaning in the object or other, the testimony of validity takes precedence. On this detail, if seller and buyer differ on validity and invalidity of sale: fifteenth: Two testimonies of absolute ownership from an outsider and purchase from another by the possessor: the testimony of the claimant of absolute ownership takes precedence. Sixteenth: Two testimonies... [summary list from 'first of' etc.].
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents numerous rules of tarjih (preference) when two testimonies conflict, a key topic in Hanafi qada' (judicial procedure). The author lists specific scenarios, each with a ruling on which bayyinah (evidence) is preferred. The primary principle is that preference is given based on substantive legal strength, not merely number of witnesses. For example, testimony of deception (ghabn) prevails over market value when a guardian sells an orphan's property, because the guardian must avoid gross underpayment. In the third scenario, the slave woman's testimony about a transaction during the owner's death illness is preferred over heirs' testimony of insanity because the default is sanity. The summary list at the end provides a handy reference: e.g., testimony of dowry beats gift, of reason beats insanity, of coercion beats willingness, of validity beats death, of discharge beats acknowledgement, of sale beats pledge, of recent beats old, etc. The passage underscores that the judge must carefully weigh the substance of each claim. The commentary by Shaykh Khalil al-Fattal and Shaykh Ghanim al-Baghdadi adds further nuance, especially regarding sale validity disputes.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, or strong circumstantial evidence.
التعارض (al-ta'āruḍ): Conflict of two testimonies that are both apparently valid, requiring tarjih.
أولى (awlā): More deserving, preferable; indicates which testimony the judge should accept.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the twelfth scenario, regarding a woman's marital status at the time of the husband's death, which testimony is preferred?
A) The testimony that she was forbidden six months earlier.
B) The testimony that she was lawful at the time of death.
C) The testimony of the majority of witnesses.
D) The testimony with the earliest date.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi tarjih rules prioritize substantive legal defaults; learn the defaults and you can deduce the preferred testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
The Principle of Ziyadat al-Ithbat in Conflicting Testimonies
List of five cases applying ziyada rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the rule that evidence establishing an additional fact (ziyadat al-ithbat) is preferred over evidence that does not, in cases of sales, inheritance, marriage, and debt.

Core Idea
When testimonies conflict, the one that proves an extra fact or validates the transaction is given precedence.

Conflicting testimonies arise frequently in court. The Hanafi jurists developed a set of rules to determine which evidence is stronger. One key principle is that evidence establishing an additional fact or confirming the validity of a transaction outweighs the other. In this lesson, we examine several cases from al-Bahr al-Raiq where this principle is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict
Read each case and determine what two facts are being testified. Look for the element that the preferred evidence adds.
Use the list of cases to see the pattern.
2
Find the additional element
In each case, ask: what fact does one testimony prove that the other does not? That is the ziyada.
For example, in case 21, the first brother proves the house was the mother's before the father's.
3
Apply the preference rule
The testimony with the additional element (ziyada) is declared as the preferred (awla) evidence.
The text explicitly states 'fabinat al-awla' for each case.
4
Confirm the ruling
State the final ruling: which party's evidence is accepted and what legal effect follows.
E.g., in case 22, the husband's evidence of discharge is accepted, so the dower claim is dismissed.

كتاب الشهادات باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
الراهن والمرتهن في قيمة الرهن فبينة الراهن أولى السابعة عشرة تعارضت بينتا وجود الشرط وعدمه فبينة المرأة أولى الثامنة عشرة تعارضت بينتا بيع الوصي بعد عزله أو قبله فبينة المشتري أولى لما فيها من زيادة إثبات نفاذ الشراء أو سبق التاريخ، وقيل بينة العزل أولى، وكذا الطلاق والعتاق من الوكيل . التاسعة عشرة تعارضت بينتان في حمار وقال المدعي إنه ملكي غاب عني منذ ثمانية أشهر، وقال ذو اليد اشتريته منذ سبعة عشر شهراً وأقاما البينة فبينة المدعي أولى العشرون ادعت المرأة البراءة من المهر بشرط وادعاها زوجها مطلقة وأقام البينة فبينة المرأة أولى إن كان الشرط متعارفاً يصح الإبراء معه، وقيل بيئة الزوج أولى. الحادية والعشرون أقام أحد الأخوين بينة أن الدار التي في أيدينا كانت لأمي تركتها ميراثاً بيني وبين أبي، وأقام الآخر بينة أنها كانت لأبينا فتركها ميراثاً لنا فبينة الأول أولى لإثباته الزيادة. الثانية والعشرون أقامت المرأة البينة على المهر على أن زوجها كان مقراً بذلك إلى يومنا هذا وأقام الزوج البينة أنها أبرأته من هذا المهر الذي تدعي فبينة البراءة أولى، وكذا في الدين لأن بينة مدعي الدين بطلت بإقرار المدعى عليه لما ادعى البراءة ولم تبطل بينة البراءة، وهذا كشهود البيع والإقالة فإن بينة الإقالة أولى لبطلان بينة البيع بإقرار مدعي الإقالة، وينبغي أن يحفظ هذا الأصل فإنه يخرج به كثير من الواقعات. الثالثة والعشرون ادعى على رجل ستة دنانير فقال المدعى عليه إنه أبرأني عن هذه الدعوى فأقام بينة وأقام المدعي بينة أنه كان أقر له بستة دنانير قيل تصح دعوى الإقرار ثانياً، وقيل لا تصح، وقيل إن ذكر الخصم القبول أو التصديق في يصح . الرابعة والعشرون تعرضت بينة الصحة والفساد في الشراء ففيه قولان. الخامسة والعشرون تعارضت بينتا الإجازة والرد في بيع الفصولي فبينة المشتري أولى . السادسة والعشرون تعارضت بينتا السكوت والرد في نكاح البكر فبينتها أولى بخلاف ما إذا برهن على إجازتها وهي على ردها فبينته أولى السابعة والعشرون تعارضت بينتا البيع والوقف عليه مسجلاً فبينة مدعي البيع أولى إلا إذا عين الواقف فبينة الوقف أولى لأنه مقضياً عليه فلا بد من التعيين كبينة الملك مع بيئة العتق ا هـ .

قوله : (فإن قضى بإحداهما أولاً بطلت الأخرى لأن الأولى ترجحت باتصال القضاء بها فلا تنقض بالثانية ونظيره لو كان مع رجل ثوبان أحدهما نجس فتحرى وصلى في ثم وقع تحريه على طهارة الآخر لا تجوز له الصلاة فيه لأن الأول اتصل بحكم الشرع فلا ينتقض بوقوع التحري في الآخر قوله : ( ولو شهدا بسرقة بقرة واختلفا في لونها قطع بخلاف الذكورة والأنوثة والغصب وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : لا قطع في الوجهين. وقيل الاختلاف في لونين يتشابهان كالسواد والحمرة لا في السواد والبياض. وقيل في جميع الألوان. لهما أن السرقة في السوداء غيرها في البيضاء فلم يتم على كل فعل نصاب الشهادة وصار كالغصب بل أولى لأن أمر الحد أهم وصار كالذكورة والأنوثة. وله أن التوفيق ممكن لأن التحمل في الليالي من بعيد واللونان يتشابهان أو يجتمعان فيكون السواد من جانب وهذا يبصره، والبياض من جانب آخر وهذا يشاهده بخلاف الغصب لأن التحمل فيه بالنهار غالباً على قرب منه، والذكورية والأنوثة لا يجتمعان في واحد وكذا الوقوف على ذلك بالقرب منه فلا يشتبه. أطلق في اللون فشمل جميع الألوان وهو الصحيح؛ كذا في الكافي وقدمنا الاختلاف فيه. وفي القنية : خلاف غير ما قدمناه عن أبي جعفر أن هذا الخلاف فيما إذا

Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Disagreement in Testimony. The pledgor and pledgee regarding the value of the pledge: the pledgor's evidence is given precedence. The seventeenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict regarding the existence or absence of a condition, the woman's evidence is given precedence. The eighteenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict regarding the sale by the executor after his dismissal or before it, the buyer's evidence is given precedence due to the additional establishment of the validity of the purchase or the earlier date. It is said the evidence of dismissal is given precedence, and similarly for divorce and manumission by the agent. The nineteenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict concerning a donkey, and the claimant says it is my property that has been absent from me for eight months, and the possessor says I bought it seventeen months ago, and they produce evidence, the claimant's evidence is given precedence. The twentieth: if a woman claims discharge from the dower due to a condition, and her husband claims she is divorced and produces evidence, the woman's evidence is given precedence if the condition is customary and the discharge is valid with it. It is said the husband's evidence is given precedence. The twenty-first: one of two brothers produces evidence that the house in our possession belonged to my mother, inherited between me and my father, and the other produces evidence that it belonged to our father, leaving it as inheritance to us; the first's evidence is given precedence for establishing an additional element. The twenty-second: a woman produces evidence of the dower, stating that her husband had acknowledged it up to this day, and the husband produces evidence that she discharged him from this dower she claims; the evidence of discharge is given precedence, similarly for debt, because the evidence of the claimant of the debt is invalidated by the admission of the defendant when he claims discharge, and the evidence of discharge is not invalidated. This is like witnesses of sale and revocation, for the evidence of revocation is given precedence due to the invalidation of the evidence of sale by the admission of the claimant of revocation. This principle should be memorized, for many cases derive from it. The twenty-third: a man claims six dinars against another; the defendant says he discharged me from this claim and produces evidence, and the claimant produces evidence that he had acknowledged the six dinars to him; it is said the claim of acknowledgment is valid a second time, and it is said it is not valid, and it is said if the opponent mentions acceptance or affirmation, it is valid. The twenty-fourth: evidence of validity and invalidity contradict in a purchase; there are two opinions. The twenty-fifth: evidence of ratification and rejection contradict in the sale of a faḍūlī; the buyer's evidence is given precedence. The twenty-sixth: evidence of silence and rejection contradict in the marriage of a virgin; her evidence is given precedence, contrary to if he proves her ratification while she is rejecting, then his evidence is given precedence. The twenty-seventh: evidence of sale and endowment contradict regarding it registered; the evidence of the claimant of sale is given precedence except if the endower specified, then the evidence of endowment is given precedence because he is subject to the ruling, so specification is necessary, like the evidence of ownership with the evidence of emancipation. End.
The evidences of Shaykh Ghānim al-Baghdādī: If the buyer and seller disagree, one claiming validity and the other claiming invalidity due to an invalid condition or an invalid term, the statement is of the claimant of validity and the evidence is of the claimant of invalidity by agreement of the narrations. And if the claimant of invalidity claims invalidity in the essence of the contract, claiming he bought it for a thousand dirhams and a pound of wine, and the other claims the sale for a thousand dirhams, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in the apparent narration, the statement is of the claimant of validity also, and the evidence is of the other as in the first aspect; and in another narration, the statement is of the claimant of invalidity. Included in al-Ahkam. End.
His statement: 'The claimant's evidence is given precedence' meaning because he is external and the earlier date is not considered because his date is not considered, because it is a date of absence, not a date of ownership, so it does not exist. The date from both sides so that the earlier of them is considered. His statement: 'He produced evidence claiming considered'
The other: and if two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow and disagree on its color, amputation is executed, contrary to the case of male and female. And this according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: no amputation in both cases. It is said the disagreement is in two similar colors like black and red, not in black and white. It is said in all colors. According to them, the theft of a black cow is different from a white one, so the full amount of testimony is not completed for each act, and it becomes like usurpation, rather more so because the matter of punishment is more important, and it becomes like the case of male and female. According to him (Abu Hanifa), reconciliation is possible because the witnessing is at night from a distance, and the two colors are similar or can be combined, so he saw black from one side and white from another, unlike usurpation because witnessing it is usually during the day from close, and masculinity and femininity cannot be combined in one, and likewise knowing that from close is not confusing. He made it absolute regarding color, so it includes all colors, and that is the correct view. Likewise in al-Kafi, and we have presented the disagreement on it. In al-Quniya: a disagreement other than what we have presented from Abu Ja'far that this disagreement is when...
One brother produces evidence) meaning against his paternal brother. The statement of the author: 'If a judgment is given on one first, the other is invalid' etc. Al-Ramli said: Its apparent meaning indicates that in the cases he listed, and in them one of the two pieces of evidence is preferred, if a judgment is given on the less preferred, the preferred one is accepted even if the judgment was connected to the other that is less preferred, because it was preferred before the judgment, unlike the equal ones, for they are only preferred by their connection to the judgment, as is apparent. The conclusion is that a distinction is made between when they are equal, so the first becomes preferred by the connection of the judgment to it, or the judgment preceded on the less preferred, since there is no opposition to it at that time; and between when one is more worthy of acceptance, and judgment is given on other than it, then what is acted upon is established even if the judgment was connected to other than it due to its priority. This is supported by what al-Zayla‘i mentioned in his commentary on the coming issue of a case where two produce evidence on a woman's marriage, from his statement in the reasoning that the one whose evidence precedes belongs to her because it is stronger due to the connection of the judgment to it, because when it preceded and a judgment was made on it, it became confirmed, so it is not invalidated by other than the confirmed. End. For the preferred is stronger before the connection of the judgment to it, so it is confirmed, so the judgment on other than it is invalidated due to its being more worthy before it. But al-Zayla‘i reasoned the case of killing: because when it was judged that he was killed in Mecca, that became a judgment that he was not killed elsewhere, since a single person being killed in two places is inconceivable. This implies that in the cases he listed, the previous judgment is not invalidated absolutely, because it involves negation of its opposite, since it is inconceivable like in a single sale that it is at a grossly unfair price and at the like value, and similarly for its parallels, as is apparent. Then I saw in the Fatawa of the shaykh of my shaykhs, Shihab al-Din al-Halabi, in the book of endowment: if the judge rules by the first evidence, the second evidence is not heard because the first is preferred by the connection of the judgment to it. Qadikhan said: If a woman produces evidence that the deceased married her on the day of Nahr in Mecca, and the judge rules by their testimony, then she produces other evidence that he married her on that day in Khurasan, it is not accepted. End.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, specifically on the chapter of conflicting testimonies. The author begins by listing a series of cases (seventeenth through twenty-seventh) where two contradictory pieces of evidence are presented, and the ruling is given based on which evidence is deemed superior. The criteria for superiority include: establishing an additional fact (زيادة إثبات), the nature of the claim (e.g., external claimant vs. possessor), customary practices, and the principle that evidence of discharge (براءة) prevails over evidence of debt because the latter is invalidated by the admission of the claimant of discharge. The author stresses the importance of memorizing this principle, as many cases derive from it. 

Following this list, a separate quote from the work 'البينات للشيخ غانم البغدادي' addresses a specific scenario: when buyer and seller dispute over the validity of a sale due to an invalid condition or term. The ruling is that the one claiming validity gives the statement, and the evidence is on the claimant of invalidity. However, if the invalidity is in the essence of the contract (e.g., involving wine), there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in the apparent narration, the statement is still with the claimant of validity; in another, with the claimant of invalidity.

The passage then shifts to a commentary on the phrase 'فبينة المدعي أولى', explaining why the claimant's evidence is preferred: because he is an external party (خارج) and his date is not considered as a date of ownership but of absence. 

A major section is devoted to a case of theft of a cow where witnesses disagree on its color. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa rules that amputation is executed, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say no amputation in either case. The reasoning is detailed: Abu Hanifa allows reconciliation of the testimonies because the witnessing might have been at night from a distance, and colors can appear similar or combine (e.g., one side black, another white). The Sahibayn argue that theft of a black cow is a different act from a white cow, so the full nisab (testimony requirement) is not met for any single act, analogous to usurpation or gender difference. The correct view, according to the author, is that the disagreement applies to all colors, and the absolute statement of the text is upheld.

Finally, the passage discusses the principle that once a judgment is given on one piece of evidence, the other is invalidated because the first is strengthened by the connection of the judgment. This is illustrated with a comparison to a man praying in a garment after estimating its purity: once he prays in one, he cannot switch. Al-Ramli and al-Zaylai comment on the nuances: if the two evidences were equal before judgment, the first becomes preferred by the judgment; but if one was already stronger (مرجحة), a judgment on the weaker can be overturned by the stronger later. The passage ends with a fatwa from Shihab al-Din al-Halabi and Qadikhan confirming that a prior judgment based on one evidence precludes hearing a contradictory evidence later.

Key Terms
الزائدة (al-zā’idah): An additional element or fact that one testimony establishes over the other, making it preferable.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence or testimony presented in court, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, that establishes a claim.
الإبراء (al-ibrā’): A declaration of discharge or release from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In case 21 (two brothers and the house), why is the first brother's evidence preferred?
A) Because his evidence has a earlier date.
B) Because he is the older brother.
C) Because he proves an additional fact (mother's ownership before father).
D) Because he is the claimant and the other is the defendant.

Key Takeaway
Evidence that proves an additional fact (ziyada) is preferred over evidence that does not, providing a clear criterion in conflicting testimonies.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
External Claimant, Possessor, and Discharge Priority in Testimonies
List of six cases and a commentary on external claimant and discharge preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine which conflicting testimony is preferred based on the status of the claimant (external vs possessor) and the rule that evidence of discharge outweighs evidence of debt.

Core Idea
The external claimant's evidence beats the possessor's, and evidence of discharge trumps evidence of the original debt.

In addition to the principle of additional establishment, Hanafi law recognizes other factors that give one testimony precedence. The status of the claimant—whether he is external to the property or in possession—and the nature of the claim (discharge vs. original liability) are crucial. This lesson covers cases where these factors decide the outcome, including the buyer-seller dispute over contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Determine the parties' roles
Identify who is the claimant (mudda'i) and who is the possessor (dhu al-yad). The external claimant is the one outside possession.
In property disputes, the external claimant's evidence is preferred over the possessor's because possession itself is a form of proof.
2
Check for discharge (ibra')
If one party claims discharge from a debt or obligation, their evidence is preferred over the evidence of the original debt, because the admission of the debt by the claimant of discharge validates the discharge.
The text explicitly states this in case 22 and generalises it.
3
Apply to sales disputes
In buyer-seller conflicts over contract validity, the claimant of validity gives the statement and the claimant of invalidity must provide evidence. If the invalidity is in the essence (like wine), there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
See the Ghānim al-Baghdādī excerpt.
4
Conclude with the rule
The external claimant and discharge priority rules are fixed. For the buyer-seller dispute, the default is that the statement is with the one claiming validity, and evidence on the one claiming invalidity.
The exception is when the invalidity is in the essence, where there is a difference of narration.

Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Disagreement in Testimony. The pledgor and pledgee regarding the value of the pledge: the pledgor's evidence is given precedence. The seventeenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict regarding the existence or absence of a condition, the woman's evidence is given precedence. The eighteenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict regarding the sale by the executor after his dismissal or before it, the buyer's evidence is given precedence due to the additional establishment of the validity of the purchase or the earlier date. It is said the evidence of dismissal is given precedence, and similarly for divorce and manumission by the agent. The nineteenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict concerning a donkey, and the claimant says it is my property that has been absent from me for eight months, and the possessor says I bought it seventeen months ago, and they produce evidence, the claimant's evidence is given precedence. The twentieth: if a woman claims discharge from the dower due to a condition, and her husband claims she is divorced and produces evidence, the woman's evidence is given precedence if the condition is customary and the discharge is valid with it. It is said the husband's evidence is given precedence. The twenty-first: one of two brothers produces evidence that the house in our possession belonged to my mother, inherited between me and my father, and the other produces evidence that it belonged to our father, leaving it as inheritance to us; the first's evidence is given precedence for establishing an additional element. The twenty-second: a woman produces evidence of the dower, stating that her husband had acknowledged it up to this day, and the husband produces evidence that she discharged him from this dower she claims; the evidence of discharge is given precedence, similarly for debt, because the evidence of the claimant of the debt is invalidated by the admission of the defendant when he claims discharge, and the evidence of discharge is not invalidated. This is like witnesses of sale and revocation, for the evidence of revocation is given precedence due to the invalidation of the evidence of sale by the admission of the claimant of revocation. This principle should be memorized, for many cases derive from it. The twenty-third: a man claims six dinars against another; the defendant says he discharged me from this claim and produces evidence, and the claimant produces evidence that he had acknowledged the six dinars to him; it is said the claim of acknowledgment is valid a second time, and it is said it is not valid, and it is said if the opponent mentions acceptance or affirmation, it is valid. The twenty-fourth: evidence of validity and invalidity contradict in a purchase; there are two opinions. The twenty-fifth: evidence of ratification and rejection contradict in the sale of a faḍūlī; the buyer's evidence is given precedence. The twenty-sixth: evidence of silence and rejection contradict in the marriage of a virgin; her evidence is given precedence, contrary to if he proves her ratification while she is rejecting, then his evidence is given precedence. The twenty-seventh: evidence of sale and endowment contradict regarding it registered; the evidence of the claimant of sale is given precedence except if the endower specified, then the evidence of endowment is given precedence because he is subject to the ruling, so specification is necessary, like the evidence of ownership with the evidence of emancipation. End.
The evidences of Shaykh Ghānim al-Baghdādī: If the buyer and seller disagree, one claiming validity and the other claiming invalidity due to an invalid condition or an invalid term, the statement is of the claimant of validity and the evidence is of the claimant of invalidity by agreement of the narrations. And if the claimant of invalidity claims invalidity in the essence of the contract, claiming he bought it for a thousand dirhams and a pound of wine, and the other claims the sale for a thousand dirhams, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in the apparent narration, the statement is of the claimant of validity also, and the evidence is of the other as in the first aspect; and in another narration, the statement is of the claimant of invalidity. Included in al-Ahkam. End.

And this according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: no amputation in both cases. It is said the disagreement is in two similar colors like black and red, not in black and white. It is said in all colors. According to them, the theft of a black cow is different from a white one, so the full amount of testimony is not completed for each act, and it becomes like usurpation, rather more so because the matter of punishment is more important, and it becomes like the case of male and female. According to him (Abu Hanifa), reconciliation is possible because the witnessing is at night from a distance, and the two colors are similar or can be combined, so he saw black from one side and white from another, unlike usurpation because witnessing it is usually during the day from close, and masculinity and femininity cannot be combined in one, and likewise knowing that from close is not confusing. He made it absolute regarding color, so it includes all colors, and that is the correct view. Likewise in al-Kafi, and we have presented the disagreement on it. The statement of the author: 'If a judgment is given on one first, the other is invalid' etc. Al-Ramli said: Its apparent meaning indicates that in the cases he listed, and in them one of the two pieces of evidence is preferred, if a judgment is given on the less preferred, the preferred one is accepted even if the judgment was connected to the other that is less preferred, because it was preferred before the judgment, unlike the equal ones, for they are only preferred by their connection to the judgment, as is apparent. The conclusion is that a distinction is made between when they are equal, so the first becomes preferred by the connection of the judgment to it, or the judgment preceded on the less preferred, since there is no opposition to it at that time; and between when one is more worthy of acceptance, and judgment is given on other than it, then what is acted upon is established even if the judgment was connected to other than it due to its priority. This is supported by what al-Zayla‘i mentioned in his commentary on the coming issue of a case where two produce evidence on a woman's marriage, from his statement in the reasoning that the one whose evidence precedes belongs to her because it is stronger due to the connection of the judgment to it, because when it preceded and a judgment was made on it, it became confirmed, so it is not invalidated by other than the confirmed. End. For the preferred is stronger before the connection of the judgment to it, so it is confirmed, so the judgment on other than it is invalidated due to its being more worthy before it. But al-Zayla‘i reasoned the case of killing: because when it was judged that he was killed in Mecca, that became a judgment that he was not killed elsewhere, since a single person being killed in two places is inconceivable. This implies that in the cases he listed, the previous judgment is not invalidated absolutely, because it involves negation of its opposite, since it is inconceivable like in a single sale that it is at a grossly unfair price and at the like value, and similarly for its parallels, as is apparent. Then I saw in the Fatawa of the shaykh of my shaykhs, Shihab al-Din al-Halabi, in the book of endowment: if the judge rules by the first evidence, the second evidence is not heard because the first is preferred by the connection of the judgment to it. Qadikhan said: If a woman produces evidence that the deceased married her on the day of Nahr in Mecca, and the judge rules by their testimony, then she produces other evidence that he married her on that day in Khurasan, it is not accepted. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, specifically on the chapter of conflicting testimonies. The author begins by listing a series of cases (seventeenth through twenty-seventh) where two contradictory pieces of evidence are presented, and the ruling is given based on which evidence is deemed superior. The criteria for superiority include: establishing an additional fact (زيادة إثبات), the nature of the claim (e.g., external claimant vs. possessor), customary practices, and the principle that evidence of discharge (براءة) prevails over evidence of debt because the latter is invalidated by the admission of the claimant of discharge. The author stresses the importance of memorizing this principle, as many cases derive from it. 

Following this list, a separate quote from the work 'البينات للشيخ غانم البغدادي' addresses a specific scenario: when buyer and seller dispute over the validity of a sale due to an invalid condition or term. The ruling is that the one claiming validity gives the statement, and the evidence is on the claimant of invalidity. However, if the invalidity is in the essence of the contract (e.g., involving wine), there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in the apparent narration, the statement is still with the claimant of validity; in another, with the claimant of invalidity.

The passage then shifts to a commentary on the phrase 'فبينة المدعي أولى', explaining why the claimant's evidence is preferred: because he is an external party (خارج) and his date is not considered as a date of ownership but of absence. 

A major section is devoted to a case of theft of a cow where witnesses disagree on its color. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa rules that amputation is executed, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say no amputation in either case. The reasoning is detailed: Abu Hanifa allows reconciliation of the testimonies because the witnessing might have been at night from a distance, and colors can appear similar or combine (e.g., one side black, another white). The Sahibayn argue that theft of a black cow is a different act from a white cow, so the full nisab (testimony requirement) is not met for any single act, analogous to usurpation or gender difference. The correct view, according to the author, is that the disagreement applies to all colors, and the absolute statement of the text is upheld.

Finally, the passage discusses the principle that once a judgment is given on one piece of evidence, the other is invalidated because the first is strengthened by the connection of the judgment. This is illustrated with a comparison to a man praying in a garment after estimating its purity: once he prays in one, he cannot switch. Al-Ramli and al-Zaylai comment on the nuances: if the two evidences were equal before judgment, the first becomes preferred by the judgment; but if one was already stronger (مرجحة), a judgment on the weaker can be overturned by the stronger later. The passage ends with a fatwa from Shihab al-Din al-Halabi and Qadikhan confirming that a prior judgment based on one evidence precludes hearing a contradictory evidence later.

Key Terms
المدعي (al-mudda‘ī): The party who makes a claim (da‘wa) in court; often the one who is external to the property (خارج) versus the possessor.
ذو اليد (dhū al-yad): The possessor, i.e., the person who has physical or legal possession of the property in dispute.
الإبراء (al-ibrā’): A declaration of discharge or release from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the buyer-seller dispute from Ghānim al-Baghdādī, if one claims invalidity due to an invalid condition (e.g., usurious term), whose statement is accepted?
A) The claimant of validity.
B) The claimant of invalidity.
C) Both must provide evidence.
D) The judge decides without statements.

Key Takeaway
The external claimant's evidence is preferred over the possessor's, and evidence of discharge over original debt, providing clear priority rules in property and debt disputes.

Shahadat — Testimony

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Theft of a Cow with Color Disagreement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on cow color and rule on prior judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute on whether amputation is executed when witnesses disagree on the color of a stolen cow, and evaluate the reasoning of Abu Hanifa versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
If testimonies can be reconciled, the ruling is applied; otherwise, not—Abu Hanifa reconciles color differences as due to distance, while the Sahibayn treat them as different acts.

A thief steals a cow, and two witnesses testify but disagree on its color. Does the disagreement invalidate the testimony? Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold different views. This lesson analyzes their proofs and the principle of reconciliation (tawfiq) versus treating each testimony as a separate act. We also examine the related principle that once a judgment is rendered, contradictory evidence is not heard.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow. One says the cow was black, the other says white. The question: is amputation (hadd) executed?
This is the core issue.
2
Present Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says yes, amputation is executed because the testimonies can be reconciled: the witnessing may have occurred at night from a distance, where colors appear similar or combine. He argues that tawfiq (reconciliation) is possible.
His proof: possibility of reconciliation distinguishes this from usurpation and gender difference.
3
Present Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no amputation in either case because the theft of a black cow is a different act from a white cow. Therefore, each witness's testimony does not complete the nisab (minimum testimony requirement) for a single act. They analogize to usurpation and gender.
Their proof: each act is separate, so the testimony pool is insufficient.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The text states that the ruling is absolute for all colors (aṭlaqa fī al-lawn fashamila jamī‘a al-alwān wa huwa al-ṣaḥīḥ), indicating that Abu Hanifa's view is correct. Later sources note disagreement but uphold this tarjih.
Also, the commentary from al-Kāfī is cited.
5
Connect to the prior judgment rule
The passage also discusses that if a judgment has already been given on one evidence, the contradictory evidence is invalidated because the first judgment is strengthened by its connection to the court's decision. This is illustrated with the analogy of a man praying in one of two garments after estimation.
This rule prevents reopening cases after a valid judgment.

The seventeenth: if two pieces of evidence contradict regarding the existence or absence of a condition, the woman's evidence is given precedence. It is said the husband's evidence is given precedence. The twenty-first: one of two brothers produces evidence that the house in our possession belonged to my mother, inherited between me and my father, and the other produces evidence that it belonged to our father, leaving it as inheritance to us; the first's evidence is given precedence for establishing an additional element. The twenty-second: a woman produces evidence of the dower, stating that her husband had acknowledged it up to this day, and the husband produces evidence that she discharged him from this dower she claims; the evidence of discharge is given precedence, similarly for debt, because the evidence of the claimant of the debt is invalidated by the admission of the defendant when he claims discharge, and the evidence of discharge is not invalidated. This is like witnesses of sale and revocation, for the evidence of revocation is given precedence due to the invalidation of the evidence of sale by the admission of the claimant of revocation. This principle should be memorized, for many cases derive from it. The twenty-third: a man claims six dinars against another; the defendant says he discharged me from this claim and produces evidence, and the claimant produces evidence that he had acknowledged the six dinars to him; it is said the claim of acknowledgment is valid a second time, and it is said it is not valid, and it is said if the opponent mentions acceptance or affirmation, it is valid. The twenty-fourth: evidence of validity and invalidity contradict in a purchase; there are two opinions. The twenty-fifth: evidence of ratification and rejection contradict in the sale of a faḍūlī; the buyer's evidence is given precedence. The twenty-sixth: evidence of silence and rejection contradict in the marriage of a virgin; her evidence is given precedence, contrary to if he proves her ratification while she is rejecting, then his evidence is given precedence. The twenty-seventh: evidence of sale and endowment contradict regarding it registered; the evidence of the claimant of sale is given precedence except if the endower specified, then the evidence of endowment is given precedence because he is subject to the ruling, so specification is necessary, like the evidence of ownership with the evidence of emancipation. End.
The evidences of Shaykh Ghānim al-Baghdādī: If the buyer and seller disagree, one claiming validity and the other claiming invalidity due to an invalid condition or an invalid term, the statement is of the claimant of validity and the evidence is of the claimant of invalidity by agreement of the narrations. And if the claimant of invalidity claims invalidity in the essence of the contract, claiming he bought it for a thousand dirhams and a pound of wine, and the other claims the sale for a thousand dirhams, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in the apparent narration, the statement is of the claimant of validity also, and the evidence is of the other as in the first aspect; and in another narration, the statement is of the claimant of invalidity. Included in al-Ahkam. End.
His statement: 'The claimant's evidence is given precedence' meaning because he is external and the earlier date is not considered because his date is not considered, because it is a date of absence, not a date of ownership, so it does not exist. The date from both sides so that the earlier of them is considered. His statement: 'He produced evidence claiming considered'
The other: and if two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow and disagree on its color, amputation is executed, contrary to the case of male and female. And this according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: no amputation in both cases. It is said the disagreement is in two similar colors like black and red, not in black and white. It is said in all colors. According to them, the theft of a black cow is different from a white one, so the full amount of testimony is not completed for each act, and it becomes like usurpation, rather more so because the matter of punishment is more important, and it becomes like the case of male and female. According to him (Abu Hanifa), reconciliation is possible because the witnessing is at night from a distance, and the two colors are similar or can be combined, so he saw black from one side and white from another, unlike usurpation because witnessing it is usually during the day from close, and masculinity and femininity cannot be combined in one, and likewise knowing that from close is not confusing. He made it absolute regarding color, so it includes all colors, and that is the correct view. Likewise in al-Kafi, and we have presented the disagreement on it. The statement of the author: 'If a judgment is given on one first, the other is invalid' etc. Al-Ramli said: Its apparent meaning indicates that in the cases he listed, and in them one of the two pieces of evidence is preferred, if a judgment is given on the less preferred, the preferred one is accepted even if the judgment was connected to the other that is less preferred, because it was preferred before the judgment, unlike the equal ones, for they are only preferred by their connection to the judgment, as is apparent. The conclusion is that a distinction is made between when they are equal, so the first becomes preferred by the connection of the judgment to it, or the judgment preceded on the less preferred, since there is no opposition to it at that time; and between when one is more worthy of acceptance, and judgment is given on other than it, then what is acted upon is established even if the judgment was connected to other than it due to its priority. This is supported by what al-Zayla‘i mentioned in his commentary on the coming issue of a case where two produce evidence on a woman's marriage, from his statement in the reasoning that the one whose evidence precedes belongs to her because it is stronger due to the connection of the judgment to it, because when it preceded and a judgment was made on it, it became confirmed, so it is not invalidated by other than the confirmed. End. For the preferred is stronger before the connection of the judgment to it, so it is confirmed, so the judgment on other than it is invalidated due to its being more worthy before it. But al-Zayla‘i reasoned the case of killing: because when it was judged that he was killed in Mecca, that became a judgment that he was not killed elsewhere, since a single person being killed in two places is inconceivable. This implies that in the cases he listed, the previous judgment is not invalidated absolutely, because it involves negation of its opposite, since it is inconceivable like in a single sale that it is at a grossly unfair price and at the like value, and similarly for its parallels, as is apparent. Then I saw in the Fatawa of the shaykh of my shaykhs, Shihab al-Din al-Halabi, in the book of endowment: if the judge rules by the first evidence, the second evidence is not heard because the first is preferred by the connection of the judgment to it. Qadikhan said: If a woman produces evidence that the deceased married her on the day of Nahr in Mecca, and the judge rules by their testimony, then she produces other evidence that he married her on that day in Khurasan, it is not accepted. End.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, specifically on the chapter of conflicting testimonies. The author begins by listing a series of cases (seventeenth through twenty-seventh) where two contradictory pieces of evidence are presented, and the ruling is given based on which evidence is deemed superior. The criteria for superiority include: establishing an additional fact (زيادة إثبات), the nature of the claim (e.g., external claimant vs. possessor), customary practices, and the principle that evidence of discharge (براءة) prevails over evidence of debt because the latter is invalidated by the admission of the claimant of discharge. The author stresses the importance of memorizing this principle, as many cases derive from it. 

Following this list, a separate quote from the work 'البينات للشيخ غانم البغدادي' addresses a specific scenario: when buyer and seller dispute over the validity of a sale due to an invalid condition or term. The ruling is that the one claiming validity gives the statement, and the evidence is on the claimant of invalidity. However, if the invalidity is in the essence of the contract (e.g., involving wine), there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in the apparent narration, the statement is still with the claimant of validity; in another, with the claimant of invalidity.

The passage then shifts to a commentary on the phrase 'فبينة المدعي أولى', explaining why the claimant's evidence is preferred: because he is an external party (خارج) and his date is not considered as a date of ownership but of absence. 

A major section is devoted to a case of theft of a cow where witnesses disagree on its color. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa rules that amputation is executed, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say no amputation in either case. The reasoning is detailed: Abu Hanifa allows reconciliation of the testimonies because the witnessing might have been at night from a distance, and colors can appear similar or combine (e.g., one side black, another white). The Sahibayn argue that theft of a black cow is a different act from a white cow, so the full nisab (testimony requirement) is not met for any single act, analogous to usurpation or gender difference. The correct view, according to the author, is that the disagreement applies to all colors, and the absolute statement of the text is upheld.

Finally, the passage discusses the principle that once a judgment is given on one piece of evidence, the other is invalidated because the first is strengthened by the connection of the judgment. This is illustrated with a comparison to a man praying in a garment after estimating its purity: once he prays in one, he cannot switch. Al-Ramli and al-Zaylai comment on the nuances: if the two evidences were equal before judgment, the first becomes preferred by the judgment; but if one was already stronger (مرجحة), a judgment on the weaker can be overturned by the stronger later. The passage ends with a fatwa from Shihab al-Din al-Halabi and Qadikhan confirming that a prior judgment based on one evidence precludes hearing a contradictory evidence later.

Key Terms
توفيق (tawfīq): Reconciliation of seemingly contradictory testimonies by explaining them as different perspectives of the same event.
نصاب الشهادة (niṣāb al-shahāda): The minimum number of witnesses required to establish a claim, typically two males or one male and two females.
قطع (qaṭ‘): Amputation, the hadd punishment for theft (cutting of the hand).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is amputation executed even if witnesses disagree on the cow's color?
A) Because the nisab is still met if both see a theft.
B) Because the color difference does not change the act of theft; the witnesses may have seen from different sides.
C) Because the cow is the same cow regardless of color.
D) Because the owner identified the cow by a different method.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa reconciles testimonies that differ on non-essential attributes like color, while the Sahibayn treat such differences as separate acts; the madhhab follows Abu Hanifa's view.
