Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Two Conflicting Testimonies When One Is Judged Upon
Expansion of matn: judgment on one voids the other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that judgment on one testimony voids the other and explain the qiyas from ijtihad in purification.

Core Idea
A judgment finalizes the chosen testimony; later opposing evidence cannot reverse it.

When two testimonies conflict and the judge rules on one, does the other remain viable? The Hanafi school answers clearly: no. The first testimony is strengthened by being connected to the judge's decision. This principle is likened to a man who prays after ijtihad in one of two garments, only to later realize the other might be pure—his prayer stands because the first ruling was already enacted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the central hukm: if the judge judges by one testimony, the other becomes void (batalat). This is the explicit statement of the matn.
2
Understand the rationale
The first testimony is 'strengthened by being connected to the judgment' (tarajahat bi-ittisal al-qada). The judge's action creates a legal reality that cannot be undone.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The author presents an analogy: a man with two garments, one definitely impure, performs ijtihad and prays in one. Later his ijtihad points to the other being pure. The prayer remains valid because the first ijtihad was connected to the act of worship.
Identify the asl (garment case), the far' (testimony case), and the illa (connection to a ruling).
4
Apply the analogy
Just as the prayer is not invalidated by later ijtihad, the original judgment is not invalidated by a second testimony. The key is that the first was already finalized by execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن قضى بإحداهما أو لا بطلت الأخرى) لأن الأولى ترجحت باتصال القضاء بها فلا تنقض بالثانية ونظيره لو كان مع رجل ثوبان أحدهما نجس فتحرى وصلى في ثم وقع تحريه على طهارة الآخر لا تجوز له الصلاة فيه لأن الأول اتصل بحكم الشرع فلا ينتقض بوقوع التحري في الآخر
He said: 'If he judges by one of them, the other becomes void' because the first was strengthened by being connected to the judgment, so it is not invalidated by the second. Its analogy: if a man had two garments, one impure, and he performed ijtihad and prayed in one, then his ijtihad fell on the purity of the other, his prayer in the first is not permissible because the first was connected to the ruling of the Sharia, so it is not invalidated by the occurrence of ijtihad on the other.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This is an expansion of the matn ruling: when two conflicting testimonies are presented and the judge issues a ruling based on one, the other testimony becomes void. The reason is that the first testimony is strengthened by the judge's action; once a ruling is rendered and connected to it, it cannot be undone by a later testimony. The author gives an analogy from purification: a man with two garments, one definitely najis, performs ijtihad and prays in one, then later his ijtihad concludes the other is pure. His prayer is still valid because the first ruling (that he prayed in a state of purity based on his ijtihad) is already connected to the Sharia ruling, so it is not overturned by later discovery. Similarly, a judgment on one testimony is final regarding that issue, and the other testimony cannot overturn it.

Key Terms
ترجحت باتصال القضاء (tarajahat bi-ittisal al-qada): The testimony becomes strong by being attached to the judge's decision
تحرى (taharra): He performed ijtihad (personal reasoning) to determine the correct ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two conflicting testimonies are presented and the judge rules based on one, what happens to the other?
A) The other is also accepted if stronger
B) The other is rejected because the first was strengthened by the ruling
C) Both are considered invalid
D) The case is reopened

Key Takeaway
Once a judge issues a ruling on one of two conflicting testimonies, that ruling is final and the other testimony is no longer actionable, analogous to the finality of an act of worship performed after ijtihad.

Disagreement on Color in Theft Testimony: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Ruling and internal Hanafi dispute on color discrepancy in theft testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on witness disagreement over color and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument using the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ on color, the theft is still the same act — reconciliation is possible.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani presents an internal Hanafi dispute regarding the admissibility of testimony when two witnesses describe a stolen cow in different colors. The ruling has significant implications for the imposition of hadd amputation. We will explore the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and see how later scholars refined the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow. One says black, the other white. Does the hadd amputation apply? Abu Hanifa says yes, Sahibayn say no.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; both sides agree on the basic rules of testimony.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa argues that the testimonies can be reconciled because the witnesses may have seen the cow from different angles or under different lighting at night.
He contrasts with gender and usurpation, where reconciliation is impossible.
3
Analyze Sahibayn's dalil
The two companions argue that theft of a black cow and theft of a white cow are different acts, so the nisab (two witnesses on the same act) is not met. They analogize to gender and usurpation.
They emphasize the importance of precision in hadd cases.
4
Examine the later refinement
Later scholars distinguish between opposite colors (black vs white) and similar colors (dark yellow vs red). For similar colors, the testimony is accepted even according to Sahibayn.
This shows the legal reasoning is not rigid but considers practical perception.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The text states that the absolute ruling (all colors) is correct (al-sahih). Thus the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: amputation is imposed.
This is found in al-Kafi and supported by the need for leniency in evidence collection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولو شهدا بسرقة بقرة واختلفا في لونها قطع بخلاف الذكورة والأنوثة والغصب وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : لا قطع في الوجهين. وقيل الاختلاف في لونين يتشابهان كالسواد والحمرة لا في السواد والبياض. وقيل في جميع الألوان. لهما أن السرقة في السوداء غيرها في البيضاء فلم يتم على كل فعل نصاب الشهادة وصار كالغصب بل أولى لأن أمر الحد أهم وصار كالذكورة والأنوثة. وله أن التوفيق ممكن لأن التحمل في الليالي من بعيد واللونان يتشابهان أو يجتمعان فيكون السواد من جانب وهذا يبصره، والبياض من جانب آخر وهذا يشاهده بخلاف الغصب لأن التحمل فيه بالنهار غالباً على قرب منه، والذكورية والأنوثة لا يجتمعان في واحد وكذا الوقوف على ذلك بالقرب منه فلا يشتبه. أطلق في اللون فشمل جميع الألوان وهو الصحيح؛ كذا في الكافي وقدمنا الاختلاف فيه. وفي القنية : خلاف غير ما قدمناه عن أبي جعفر أن هذا الخلاف فيما إذا اختلفا في صفتين متضادتين كالسواد والبياض، فأما في المتقاربتين كما إذا شهد أحدهما على الصفرة والآخر على الحمرة فإنه تقبل لأن الصفرة المشبعة تضرب إلى الحمرة والحمرة إذا رقت تضرب إلى الصفرة، وكثير من العوام لا يميزون بينهما، وكذا إذا شهد أحدهما أنها غبراء والآخر أنها بيضاء تقبل بلا خلاف
He said: 'And if two witness to the theft of a cow and differ in its color, amputation is imposed, contrary to male/female and usurpation.' This is according to Abu Hanifa, and both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: No amputation in both cases. And it is said that the difference is in two similar colors like black and red, not black and white. And it is said in all colors. Their evidence is that theft of a black cow is different from theft of a white cow, so the nisab of testimony is not completed for each act, and it becomes like usurpation, even more so because the matter of hadd is more important, and it becomes like male/female. And his evidence is that reconciliation is possible because the bearing of testimony occurs at night from a distance, and the two colors may be similar or combined, so one sees black from one side and white from another side, unlike usurpation because bearing there occurs by day usually from close, and male/female cannot combine in one, and also observation of that is from close so it is not ambiguous. He gave absolute ruling on color so it includes all colors, and that is correct; as in al-Kafi, and we have already mentioned the difference in it. In al-Qunyah: there is a difference not mentioned by us from Abu Ja'far that this difference is when they differ in two opposite attributes like black and white; as for similar ones like one witnesses yellowness and the other redness, it is accepted because dark yellow tends to red and light red tends to yellow, and many common people do not distinguish between them. Similarly, if one witnesses it is grey and the other white, it is accepted without disagreement.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when two witnesses testify to the theft of a cow but differ in describing its color. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, amputation (had al-sariqa) is still imposed because, in his view, the discrepancy is reconcilable: the witnesses may have seen the cow from different angles or lighting, so their descriptions are not necessarily contradictory. He compares this to the case of a stolen cow where one witness says black, another white: both could be correct if the cow has both colors or appears different under light. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they say no amputation because each witness is effectively testifying to a different cow, so the required two witnesses for the same act are not met. They compare this to cases where witnesses differ on gender (male vs female) or on usurpation (whether the act was usurpation or not), where the hadd is not applied because the testimonies are irreconcilable. The text then presents a middle position: the difference matters only if the colors are opposites (like black and white); if they are similar (like dark yellow and red), the testimony is accepted because the difference is likely due to perception. The authoritative view (al-sahih) is that the ruling applies to all colors, as stated in al-Kafi. A further nuance from al-Qunyah quotes Abu Ja'far: even in opposite colors, the dispute is specific; for similar shades like grey vs white, there is no disagreement — the testimony is accepted.

Key Terms
الذكورة والأنوثة (al-dhukūra wa al-unūtha): Testimony about a male or female victim or animal; difference here is irreconcilable because one animal cannot be both.
الغصب (al-ghaṣb): Usurpation; testimony about whether property was taken with or without force; difference is irreconcilable because the acts are different.
التوفيق (al-tawfīq): Reconciliation; the act of harmonizing apparently contradictory testimonies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if two witnesses differ in describing the color of a stolen cow, what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is invalid and no amputation
B) Amputation is imposed because the difference is reconcilable
C) Only if the colors are similar
D) The case is referred to the judge's discretion

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, witness discrepancy over color does not automatically invalidate testimony; the act of theft is the same, and reconciliation is possible under Abu Hanifa's view, which is the relied-upon position.

Witnesses Differing on Purchase Price
Ruling when witnesses contradict on the price in a sale testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when witnesses differ on the purchase price and explain why the testimony is void.

Core Idea
Testimony is void if witnesses disagree on the price – price is an integral part of the contract.

This lesson examines a key principle in testimony (shahadah): when two witnesses testify about a sale but contradict each other on the price, their testimony is rejected entirely. This is because they have not testified to the same contract; the price is an essential term that defines the transaction. We will explore the ruling, its reasoning, and a subtle intra-Hanafi debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the hukm: the testimony is void (batilah).
2
Understand the reasoning
The witnesses did not agree on a single contract; a purchase for 1000 is different from one for 1500.
The purpose is to prove the contract, so disagreement on the price prevents proof.
3
General application
The ruling applies whether the plaintiff claims the lesser or greater amount, and also if the plaintiff is the seller.
4
Consider al-Samarqandi's view
Al-Samarqandi accepted the testimony arguing the price could have increased, but this is rejected because it changes the contract.
The majority holds the testimony void, based on Imam Muhammad's text in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
5
Different scenarios
If the difference is in the type of price (e.g., dirhams vs dinars), the testimony is also void by agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شهد لرجل أنه اشترى عبد فلان بألف وشهد آخر بألف وخمسمائة بطلت الشهادة لأنهما لم يتفقا على عقد واحد والشراء بألف غير الشراء بألف وخمسمائة والمقصود إثبات العقد فإذا اختلف المشهود به تعذر الحكم لقصور الحجة عن كمال العدد. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان المدعي يدعي أقل المالين أو أكثرهما، وأشار إلى أن المدعي لو كان هو البائع واختلف شاهداه لم تقبل أيضاً لما ذكرنا وذكر علاء الدين السمرقندي أن الشهادة تقبل في مسألة الكتاب لأن التوفيق ممكن لأن الشراء الواحد قد يكون بألف ثم يصير بألف وخمسمائة بأن يشتريه بألف ثم يزيده عليه خمسمائة فقد اتفقا على شراء واحد ا.هـ. وهو عجيب منه فإن المسألة نص محمد في الجامع الصغير وقد أجاب في العناية عن دليله بأنه إذا اشترى بألف ثم زاد خمسمائة فلا يقال اشترى بألف وخمسمائة ولهذا يأخذ الشفيع بأصل الثمن ا هـ . ولم يزد في المعراج على قوله وفيه نوع تأمل، ونقله عنه في فتح القدير ولم يبينه، ثم رأيت الجامع الصغير فإذا هو لم يذكر إلا مسألة البيع، وكلام السمرقندي فيما قيس عليها وهو الشراء فلذا قال بالقبول فيه بخلاف ما إذا اختلفا في جنس الثمن كألف درهم ومائة دينار فإنها لا تقبل اتفاقاً.
And if one testifies for a man that he bought a slave of so-and-so for one thousand and another testifies for one thousand five hundred, the testimony is void because they did not agree on a single contract, and purchase for one thousand is different from purchase for one thousand five hundred, and the purpose is to prove the contract so if the testified matter differs, judgment is impossible due to the deficiency of proof from complete number. He gave it generally so it includes whether the plaintiff claims the lesser amount or the greater. And he indicated that if the plaintiff is the seller and his two witnesses differ, it is also not accepted for what we mentioned. And 'Ala' al-Din al-Samarqandi mentioned that the testimony is accepted in the book's issue because reconciliation is possible because a single purchase may be for one thousand then become one thousand five hundred by him buying for one thousand then adding five hundred, so they agreed on one purchase. End quote. It is surprising from him because the issue is the text of Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and in al-'Inayah it answered his evidence by saying that if he bought for one thousand then added five hundred, it is not said that he bought for one thousand five hundred, and for that reason the pre-emptor takes with the original price. End quote. In al-Mi'raj he did not add except his saying 'and in it is some consideration', and it was quoted from him in Fath al-Qadir and he did not clarify it. Then I saw al-Jami' al-Saghir and it only mentioned the issue of sale, and al-Samarqandi's speech concerns what is analogized to it, which is purchase, so he said acceptance in it, unlike if they differ in the type of price like one thousand dirhams and one hundred dinars, it is not accepted by agreement.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of the author (likely Kanz al-Daqa'iq) that if two witnesses testify to a purchase but contradict on the price, the testimony is void. The reason is that they have not agreed on the same contract: a purchase for 1000 is a different transaction from one for 1500. The purpose of testimony is to prove the contract, and since the object of testimony differs, the required number of witnesses (two agreeing on the same fact) is not met. The ruling applies whether the plaintiff claims the lesser or greater amount, and also if the plaintiff is the seller. The author then discusses al-Samarqandi's contrary opinion who argued that the testimony could be accepted because the purchase could have started at 1000 and then increased to 1500, but this is rejected because if a person buys something for 1000 and later adds 500, the purchase price is still 1000 originally; the increase would be a separate transaction or a change. The text from al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad is cited as authority for the voidness. The ruling is unanimous if the difference is in the type of price (dirhams vs dinars).

Key Terms
لم يتفقا على عقد واحد (lam yattafiqa 'ala 'aqd wahid): They did not agree on a single contract; the testimonies refer to different transactions.
بطلت الشهادة (batalat al-shahadah): The testimony is void; it has no legal effect.
جنس الثمن (jins al-thaman): The type or species of the price (e.g., dirhams vs dinars).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses testify that a man bought a slave, one saying for 1000 and the other for 1500, what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted at the lower amount
B) The testimony is void
C) The testimony is accepted at the higher amount
D) The case is postponed for further evidence

Key Takeaway
When witnesses contradict on the purchase price, the testimony is void because they have not testified to the same contract.

Testimony Without Mentioning Price
Ruling that testimony without price is void

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on testimony regarding a sale without specifying the price and explain why it is invalid in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A sale without a specified price is invalid, so testimony about it is void.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that witnesses who testify to a purchase without mentioning the price do not provide sufficient proof. The judge cannot decree a sale when the price is unknown, as the contract itself would be invalid. The price is an essential element of a valid sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the act: testimony about a purchase. The ruling is that the testimony is not accepted (batil).
The passage explicitly states that the testimony is void.
2
Understand the reason
The reason is that the price is an essential part of the sale contract. A sale without a specified price is invalid in Hanafi law.
The judge cannot judge a contract that is fundamentally defective.
3
Follow the judge's dilemma
The judge cannot give judgment on a contract that lacks an essential term.
The text says: 'it is impossible to give judgment on the contract if the sale from the beginning is without naming the price'.
4
Note the distinction
If witnesses testify to the seller's admission that includes the price, the testimony may be accepted. The passage is cut off but implies a different scenario.
The full rule is partial due to truncation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله إلى أنهما لو شهدا بالشراء ولم يبينا الثمن لم تقبل لما في المبسوط : وإذا ادعى رجل شراء دار في يد رجل وشهد شاهدان ولم يسميا الثمن والبائع ينكر ذلك فشهادتهما باطلة، لأن الدعوى إن كانت بصفة المهادة فهي فاسدة وإن كانت مع تسمية الثمن فالشهود لم شهدوا بما ادعاه المدعي، ثم القاضي يحتاج إلى القضاء بالعقد ويتعذر عليه القضاء بالعقد إذا لم يكن البيع ابتداء بدون تسمية الثمن فكذلك لا يظهر بالقضاء بدون تسمية ، ولا يمكنه أن يقضي بالثمن حين لم يشهد به الشهود ثم قال : فإن شهدا على إقرار البائع مسمى لأنه كما لا يصح
And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated that if they testify to the purchase and do not mention the price, it is not accepted because in al-Mabsut: If a man claims the purchase of a house in the hand of a man and two witnesses testify but do not name the price, and the seller denies, their testimony is void, because if the claim was without description of the price it is invalid, and if it was with naming the price, the witnesses did not testify to what the plaintiff claimed. Then the judge needs to give judgment on the contract, but it is impossible to give judgment on the contract if the sale from the beginning is without naming the price, so similarly judgment cannot be executed without naming the price, and he cannot give judgment on the price when the witnesses did not testify to it. Then he said: If they testify to the admission of the seller named... because it is not valid.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
The author of the sharh indicates that the matn implies that if witnesses testify to a purchase without specifying the price, their testimony is not accepted. This is because the price is a necessary component of a sale contract. The plaintiff's claim must specify the price; if it does not, the claim is invalid. If the claim includes the price but the witnesses do not mention it, their testimony fails to support the claim. The judge cannot decree a sale without knowing the price, as a sale without a specified price is invalid in Hanafi law. The text then mentions a different scenario: if witnesses testify to the seller's admission mentioning the price, that is acceptable, but the full passage is cut off.

Key Terms
البيع بدون تسمية الثمن (al-bay' bidūn tasmiyat al-thaman): A sale contract where the price is not specified; such a contract is invalid (batil) in Hanafi law.

Key Takeaway
Testimony regarding a sale is invalid if the price is not mentioned because the price is an essential element of a valid sale contract.

Testimony When Witnesses Disagree on Consideration
Presents core ruling and illustrative case from al-Bazzaziyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony when witnesses disagree on the consideration in sale, kitaba, khul', and marriage, and apply the exception for marriage.

Core Idea
Disagreement on the price voids testimony in sale, kitaba, and khul', but not in marriage.

In Islamic testimony law, the precise mention of consideration is crucial for contracts involving exchange. This lesson examines the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq as explained in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, where witness disagreement on the price voids testimony, with a notable exception for marriage. We will also explore a case from al-Bazzaziyya that illustrates the importance of mentioning the price or receipt in purchase testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and exceptions
The text states that testimony is void (batil) if witnesses disagree on the amount in sale, kitaba, and khul'. But in marriage, testimony is valid despite disagreement on the dower.
Memorize the three contracts where disagreement voids testimony and the one exception.
2
Understand the rationale
In sale, kitaba, and khul', the consideration is an essential element; ignorance leads to dispute and prevents the judge from decreeing the contract. In marriage, the primary aim is to establish the marriage, and the dower is not a pillar.
3
Analyze the illustrative case from al-Bazzaziyya
When witnesses testify to ownership by purchase without mentioning the price or receipt, the testimony is rejected because the judge cannot rule on a sale with an unknown price.
If they testify to receipt of the price, it becomes valid because the need is only to establish ownership.
4
Apply the distinction
Know when ignorance of the price matters: if the witnesses testify only to the contract, the price must be known; if they testify to receipt, the price can be unknown because no further delivery is needed.
This is a fine point: testimony to receipt validates the ownership claim without specifying price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بطلت الشهادة وكذا الكتابة والخلع فأما في النكاح فيصح بألف وملك المورث لم يقض يقضي يصح البزازية : ادعى محدوداً بسبب الشراء من فلان ودفع الثمن إليه وقبض المدعي بالرضا فشهدا بأنه ملكه بالشراء منه لا تقبل الشهادة لأنه دعوى الملك بسبب والقاضي أيضاً لا بد أن بذلك السبب، ولم يذكروا الثمن ولا قدره ولا وصفه والحكم بالشراء بثمن مجهول لا قيل المدعي ذكر التقابض وشهدا على موافقة ومع التقابض لا حاجة إلى ذكر الثمن قلنا شهدا بالشراء لا غير والتقابض لا يندرج تحت لفظ الشراء لا صريحاً ولا دلالة، وإذا قضى بالشراء لا بد له من القضاء بالثمن أيضاً في هذه الصورة والقضاء بالمجهول لا يتحقق ا هـ
The testimony is void, and similarly the writing (kitaba) and khul', except in marriage it is valid with one thousand. And the ownership of the deceased does not judge... judges... is valid. Al-Bazzaziyya: A limited (?) claimed ownership by purchase from so-and-so, paid the price to him, and the plaintiff received with consent, so they testified that it is his property by purchase from him — the testimony is not accepted because it is a claim of ownership by a cause, and the judge also must (know) that cause. They did not mention the price, its amount, nor its description, and judgment of purchase with an unknown price is not (valid). It was said: the plaintiff mentioned the exchange (taqabud) and they testified in agreement, and with exchange there is no need to mention the price. We said: they testified to the purchase only, and exchange is not included under the word 'purchase' explicitly or by implication. And if the judge judges by purchase, he must also judge the price in this case, and judgment with the unknown is not realized. End.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq states the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: if two witnesses disagree on the amount of consideration in a sale, kitaba (contract of manumission), or khul', their testimony is rejected. The exception is marriage, where disagreement does not invalidate the testimony because the primary aim is to establish the marriage contract, not the specific dowry. The author then cites al-Bazzaziyya to illustrate a related case: two witnesses testify that the defendant owns a property by purchase, but they do not name the price and do not testify to receipt of the price. The testimony is void because the judge cannot decree a sale without knowing the price. However, if the witnesses testify that the seller admitted having received the price, the testimony is valid, because the need is only to establish ownership, not the contract itself. The legal reasoning is that ignorance (jahala) of the price leads to dispute, which prevents the judge from enforcing the contract. But if receipt is acknowledged, there is no need to deliver the price, so ignorance of the amount does not prevent judgment.

Key Terms
الكتابة (al-kitaba): A contract of manumission by which a slave purchases freedom by paying instalments.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses disagree on the amount of the dower in a marriage testimony, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The testimony is void.
B) The testimony is valid.
C) The testimony is valid only if the amount is mentioned in the contract.
D) The testimony is rejected and the marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In exchange contracts, witnesses must agree on the consideration; otherwise testimony is void, but marriage is an exception because the dower is not a condition of validity.

Shahadat — Testimony

Disagreement of Witnesses: Contract vs Debt Claims
Detailed commentary expanding the rule on witness disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish contract claims from debt claims when witnesses disagree on the amount, state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to various contracts.

Core Idea
In contract claims, disagreement voids testimony; in debt claims, the lesser is proven.

When two witnesses testify on the same claim but give different amounts, the outcome depends on the nature of the claim. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the Hanafi rule: if the plaintiff seeks to establish a contract (like kitaba or khul'), conflicting testimony fails; if the plaintiff seeks to prove a debt, the lesser amount is accepted. An intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) arises on the precise ruling, with the mufta bihi being the Sahibayn view. The passage then applies this distinction to other contracts such as sulh, rahn, and ijara, illustrating the practical importance of classifying the claim correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the claim
Determine whether the plaintiff's objective is to establish the contract itself (e.g., kitaba, khul') or to recover a debt (e.g., unpaid dower, loan). The classification is decisive for the testimony rule.
In contract claims, precise consideration is essential; in debt claims, the agreed-upon lesser amount suffices.
2
Apply the rule to witness disagreement
In a debt claim, if one witness says 1000 and another 2000, the mufta bihi (Sahibayn view) decrees the lesser (1000). If one says 1000 and another 1500, all schools agree on the lesser. In a contract claim, the testimony is rejected entirely.
Abu Hanifa would reject all testimony if amounts differ, but the mufta bihi is the Sahibayn view.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Understand the reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that conflicting witnesses cast doubt on both testimonies; the Sahibayn hold that the lesser is agreed upon and thus reliable. This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for judges.
The tarjih (preference) for the Sahibayn view is practical and widely adopted.
4
Apply to analogous contracts
The rule extends to sulh (blood money), emancipation for money, and rahn. For each, identify who the plaintiff must be (e.g., the killer in sulh, the slave in emancipation) to treat it as a contract claim. For ijara, timing matters: at the start of the term it is like a sale (contract claim); after the term, it becomes a debt claim.
The plaintiff's identity determines whether the claim is contract or debt.

He said: (And similarly the writing and the khul') meaning if the two witnesses differ in the amount of the substitute, it is not accepted. He left them unqualified, so it includes the case when the plaintiff is the slave, which is apparent because his purpose is the contract, and the case when the plaintiff is the master because emancipation does not take effect before payment, so the purpose is to establish the cause, as in al-Hidaya. And it was said: If the plaintiff is the master, his evidence is not useful because the contract is not binding on the slave due to his ability to dissolve it by incapacitation. And he left khul' unqualified, but it is restricted to the case when the woman is the plaintiff of khul' because her purpose is to establish the cause, not the money, so it is not established with their disagreement like sale, unlike a claim of debt where the purpose is money. And if the plaintiff is the husband, divorce occurs by his admission, so it becomes a claim of debt, so the lesser agreed upon is established. And he indicated by writing and khul' every contract similar to them, which is sulh for blood, emancipation for money, and pledge. In sulh, the plaintiff must be the killer; in emancipation, the plaintiff must be the slave because the purpose is to establish the contract and the need is great. If the claim is from the other side, it is like a claim of debt in the ways we mentioned due to the establishment of pardon and emancipation by the admission of the right-holder, so the claim remains in debt. If one testifies for a thousand and the other for two thousand, nothing is adjudged according to him (Abu Hanifa), but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the lesser is adjudged. And if one testifies for a thousand and the other for one thousand five hundred, it is adjudged by agreement. As for pledge, if the plaintiff is the pledgor, it is not accepted because he has no interest in the pledge due to its non-bindingness regarding the pledgee, so the testimony is devoid of a claim. But if the plaintiff is the pledgee, it is like a claim of a sale without naming a price and they did not testify to receipt of the price, so the testimony is void because the judge needs to adjudicate the contract and cannot do so without a named price. And if they say: He admitted before us that he sold it to him and received the price, and they did not name the price, it is valid because the need is to adjudicate ownership for the plaintiff, not to adjudicate the contract — the effect of the contract has ended with receipt of the price. And because ignorance only affects because it leads to a dispute hindering delivery and receipt. Do you not see that what does not require delivery, its ignorance is not harmful, unlike what requires delivery? So when he admits to receipt of the price, there is no need to deliver the price, so its ignorance does not prevent the judge from adjudicating the admission. His statement: (So the purpose was to establish the cause). He said in al-Fath: Because the suit of the master for property against his slave is not valid, as there is no debt owed to him from his slave except through the claim of writing, so the slave's denial is directed to it because it is known that no debt is conceivable for him except through it. And the commentator gave the picture as: That he claims a pledge of one thousand and five hundred, and claimed that he took possession of it, then the pledgor took it back, so he sought its return from him, and he brought evidence; one testified for a thousand and the other for one thousand five hundred — then the lesser is established. This is a picture of a claim of contract, so it should not be accepted at all, and he did not mention the picture of a claim of debt. And he pictured it in Fath al-Qadir as the pledgee saying: I claim one thousand five hundred owed to me by him against a pledge he has with me. And the apparent meaning of al-Hidaya is that pledge is of the type of claim of debt. And he criticized it in al-Inaya following al-Nihaya because the contract of pledge is for one thousand, not one thousand five hundred, so the evidence must not be accepted even if the plaintiff is the pledgee because it would belie one of his witnesses. And it was answered that the contract is not binding on the pledgee because he has the authority to return it whenever he wishes, so it is as if nonexistent. Therefore, consideration is given to the claim of debt because a pledge cannot exist except with a debt, so the evidence is accepted as in all debts, and the pledge is established with a thousand implicitly and subordinately. And the author did not mention ijarah, but he indicated it by sale. Therefore, al-Hidaya said: If that is at the beginning of the term, it is analogous to sale; if after the term has passed and the plaintiff is the employer (ajir), it is a claim of debt. He restricted it to the case when the plaintiff is the employer to avoid the case when the plaintiff is the employee (musta'jir), for then it is a claim of contract by consensus because he admits to the wage, so judgment is given against him according to what he admitted; therefore, agreement or disagreement of witnesses is not considered, and the contract is not established due to the disagreement; as in Fath al-Qadir. The summary is that some said if that is an admission by him of the wage, then what he admitted is obligatory and there is no need for witnesses, because if he admits the larger, there is no dispute, and if he admits the smaller, the employer cannot take evidence beyond that; as in al-Nihaya. And in some commentaries: If the suit is from the employee, then this is a claim of contract by consensus. Al-Inaya said: It is in the meaning of ... (unclear). His statement: (And this is a picture of a claim of contract, so it should not be accepted at all). I say: Its answer will come shortly, which is what he mentioned as an answer to the objection of the author of al-Inaya and al-Nihaya. And his statement: 'And he pictured it in Fath al-Qadir etc' — reflect on this picturing, for the intention is to explain that the pledgee's claim of pledge is like a debt to establish the lesser. What he mentioned of the picturing is a bare claim of debt within which is an admission of pledge, so it is not what we are discussing. So what appears is the picturing of the commentator al-Zaylai — reflect. His statement: (An admission) from him, i.e., from the employee. His statement: (So it includes the case when she claims the lesser or the greater of the two sums, and that is the correct view. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This contradicts the narration, for Muhammad in al-Jami' restricted it to the claim of the greater when he said: The testimony for a thousand is valid while she claims one thousand five hundred, and the implication is considered in the narration. And by that statement, the requirement of elaboration on the amount claimed between it being the greater (so it is valid according to him) or the lesser (so there is no dispute in nullity because the plaintiff would be belying the witness of the greater) as the verifying scholars have relied upon. For Muhammad's statement 'while she claims' indicates a restriction of the answer of Abu Hanifa to validity when it is for the greater, not for the lesser, because the 'waw' here is for the circumstantial clause, and circumstances are conditions. So the contract is established by their agreement and (something) of debt. I said: Except that al-Zaylai pointed to an answer to this and said: It is equal whether she claims the lesser of the two sums or the greater... (unclear).
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is the detailed expansion of the ruling. The commentator explains that when the plaintiff's objective is to establish the contract itself (e.g., slave seeking kitaba, wife seeking khul'), disagreement on the consideration voids the testimony. But when the objective is to prove a debt (e.g., husband claiming return of dower), the testimony is accepted, and the lesser amount agreed upon is proven. The passage then presents a famous intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: If one witness says 1000 and the other says 2000, Abu Hanifa rules that nothing is proven, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that the lesser (1000) is proven. If one says 1000 and the other says 1500, all agree the lesser is proven. The reason for Abu Hanifa's position is that the conflicting testimony makes both witnesses suspect, so no testimony is reliable. The Sahibayn view is based on the idea that there is agreement on the lesser, so it can be established. The passage then applies this distinction to rahn (pledge) and ijara (lease). For rahn, if the plaintiff is the pledgor, testimony is rejected because he has no direct interest; if the plaintiff is the pledgee, it is treated as a debt claim, and the lesser amount is proven. For ijara, timing matters: at the beginning of the term, it is like a sale; after the term, if the employer is plaintiff, it is a debt claim. The discussion ends with a nuanced disagreement about whether the distinction based on the plaintiff's role is consistent, and whether the ruling differs if the plaintiff claims the greater or lesser amount. The correct view, as supported by al-Zaylai, is that it is equal—the lesser amount is established regardless.

Key Terms
دعوى العقد (da'wa al-'aqd): A claim where the plaintiff's objective is to establish the existence of a contract (e.g., kitaba, khul', sale). In such claims, disagreement on consideration renders the testimony void.
دعوى الدين (da'wa al-dayn): A claim where the plaintiff's objective is to recover a monetary debt. In such claims, if witnesses disagree on the amount, the lesser amount is proven.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for consideration. When the wife claims khul' (to establish the contract), it is a contract claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a claim for a debt, one witness says 500, the other says 1000. According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the ruling?
A) The case is dismissed because witnesses disagree.
B) The debtor pays 750 (the average).
C) The debtor pays 500 (the lesser amount).
D) The debtor pays 1000 (the greater amount).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the classification of a claim as contract or debt determines the effect of witness disagreement: for debt, the lesser is proven; for contract, testimony is void.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Testimony for Heir vs. Living Person: The Istishab Distinction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony for heir vs. living claimant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between testimony for an heir and a living claimant, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn regarding the need to specify the time of death in testimony.

Core Idea
For an heir, istishab cannot create new ownership; the time of death must be proven.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced rule in shahadat (testimony) concerning heirs. While a living claimant can rely on istishab (presumption of continuity) to prove past ownership, an heir must establish that the deceased owned the property at the moment of death. This distinction gives rise to an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the legal reasoning behind this difference and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal problem
Recognize that the text contrasts testimony for a living claimant (which is accepted via istishab) with testimony for an heir (which is not accepted without specifying the time of death). Note the phrase 'بخلاف الحي' (unlike the living person).
The key issue is whether istishab can establish new ownership for the heir.
2
Understand the role of istishab
Istishab is a proof for preserving what already exists, not for proving what did not exist. For a living claimant, ownership is presumed to continue (continuation), so past testimony suffices. For an heir, ownership is newly acquired through inheritance; istishab cannot create this new right.
The text explicitly says 'الثابت به حجة لإبقاء الثابت لا لإثبات ما لم يكن'.
3
Map the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that testimony 'the property belonged to the deceased' implicitly covers the time of death via istishab of the deceased's ownership. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf's two companions) require explicit mention of ownership at the time of death because inheritance is a new acquisition requiring certainty.
The text states 'فعنده يكفي ذلك، وعندهما لا'.
4
Apply the distinction to the purchase analogy
Unlike death, purchase is a cause (sabab) for ownership; it creates ownership ex nihilo. Therefore, testimony of purchase does not need to prove the seller's ownership at the time of sale. In contrast, death is not a cause for ownership but removes it; hence the heir must prove the deceased's ownership at death.
The text says 'بخلاف الموت فإنه مزيل له'.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The text indicates that the point of disagreement is 'محل الاختلاف' and the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn: testimony for an heir must explicitly state ownership at the time of death. Abu Yusuf's view is weaker and not acted upon.
The tarjih is inferred from the language: it states the disagreement but does not endorse Abu Yusuf's view as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لمورثه لا يقضى له وهو محل الاختلاف بخلاف الحي إذا أثبت أن العين كانت له فإنه يقضى له بها اعتباراً للاستصحاب إذ الأصل البقاء. وكذا إذا أقام البينة أنه اشتراها من فلان فإنه يكني ولا يحتاج إلى إثبات ملك البائع وقته لأن الشراء موضوع للملك بخلاف الموت فإنه مزيل له، ولذا لم يصح التعليق بقوله للوارث إن مات سيدك فأنت حر. ثم اعلم أن القضاء للوارث لا بد فيه للمشهود من الجر كما قدمناه ولا بد فيه من بيان سبب الوراثة فإذا شهدوا أنه أخوه فلا بد فيه من بيان أنه أخوه لأبيه وأمه أو لأحدهما. وفي البزازية : وكذا إذا شهدوا أنه عمه أو مولاه لم تقبل لأن المولى مشترك، فإن قالا هو مولاه أعتقه ولا نعلم له وارثاً غيره فحينئذ تقبل. وفي الظهيرية : ادعى أنه وارث فلان الميت وأقام شاهدين فشهدا أنه وارث فلان الميت لا وارث له سواه فإن القاضي يسألهما عن النسب ولا يقضي قبل السؤال، ولو أقام المدعي بينة أنه وارث فلان وأن قاضي بلد كذا فلان بن فلان قضى بأنه وارثه لا وارث له غيره وأشهدنا على قضائه ولا ندري بأي سبب قضى فإن القاضي يسأل المدعي عن النسب الذي قضى له القاضي به فإن بين قضى له بالميراث لأن قضاء القاضي يحمل على الصحة والسداد ما أمكن ولا ينقض بالشك، ولا يقضي بالنسب الذي بين المدعي لأن هذا القاضي لا يدري أن القاضي الأول هل قضى بذلك النسب أم لا ا هـ. كانت لمورثه بدون إضافة الملك إلى وقت الموت فهو محل الاختلاف بين أبي يوسف وصاحبيه، فعنده يكفي ذلك، وعندهما لا . ولما طولبا بالفرق بين هذا وبين الحي إذا ادعى ملك عين في يد رجل فشهدا بأنها كانت ملك المدعى أو شهد المدعي عين في يد إنسان أنه اشتراها من فلان الغائب ولم يقم بينة على ملك البائع وذو اليد ينكر ملك البائع فإنه يقضى للمشتري وإن لم ينصوا على أنها ملكه . أن كلاً يوم البيع مع من الشراء والإرث يوجب تجدد الملك أشار إلى الجواب بقوله بخلاف الحي الخ» وبيانه على ما في فتح القدير أنهما إذا لم ينصا على ثبوت ملكه حالة الموت فإنما يثبت بالاستصحاب والثابت به حجة لإبقاء الثابت لا لإثبات ما لم يكن وهو المحتاج إليه في الوارث بخلاف مدعي العين فإن الثابت بالاستصحاب بقاء ملكه لا تجدده والملك في الشراء مضاف إليه لا إلى ملك الشراء آخرهما وجوداً وهو سبب موضوع للملك حتى لا يتحقق لو لم يوجبه والشراء ثابت بالبينة، أما هنا فثبوت ملك الوارث مضاف إلى كون المال ملكاً للميت وقت الموت لا إلى الموت لأنه ليس سبباً موضوعاً للملك بل عنده يثبت إن كان له مال فارغ .
It is not judged for the heir, and this is the point of disagreement, unlike the living person who, if he proves that the property was his, is judged for him based on istishab, because the original is continuity. Likewise, if he produces evidence that he bought it from so-and-so, it suffices and he does not need to prove the seller's ownership at the time because purchase is a cause for ownership, unlike death which removes it. For this reason, the conditional statement 'if your master dies, you are free' is not valid for the heir. Then know that judgment for the heir necessarily requires from the witnesses al-jarr as we have mentioned, and it necessarily requires explaining the cause of inheritance. So if they testify that he is his brother, they must explain whether he is his full brother or half-brother. In al-Bazzaziyya: Likewise, if they testify that he is his uncle or his master, it is not accepted because 'master' is ambiguous. If they say, 'He is his master who manumitted him, and we do not know of any other heir for him,' then it is accepted. In al-Zahiriyya: He claims that he is the heir of so-and-so the deceased and produces two witnesses who testify that he is the heir of so-and-so the deceased with no other heir besides him. Then the judge asks them about the lineage and does not judge before asking. If the claimant produces evidence that he is the heir of so-and-so and that the judge of such a town, so-and-so son of so-and-so, ruled that he is his heir with no other heir besides him, and they witnessed his ruling, but they do not know on what basis he judged, then the judge asks the claimant about the lineage for which the judge ruled for him. If he explains, he is given the inheritance because the judge's ruling is presumed to be correct and sound as much as possible and is not invalidated by doubt. And he does not rule on the lineage that the claimant states because this judge does not know whether the first judge ruled on that lineage or not. End. For the heir without adding ownership to the time of death, this is the point of disagreement between Abu Yusuf and his two companions. According to him, that suffices; according to them, it does not. When they were asked to distinguish between this and the living person who claims ownership of a property in someone's hand and two witnesses testify that it was the property of the claimant, or the claimant testifies that he bought it from an absent person without proving the seller's ownership while the possessor denies the seller's ownership, then the buyer is judged for it even if they did not state that it was his property. That each—the purchase and inheritance—necessitates renewed ownership. He pointed to the answer by saying 'unlike the living person' etc. Its explanation according to Fath al-Qadir is that if they do not state the establishment of his ownership at the time of death, then it is established by istishab, but what is established by it is proof for preserving what exists, not for proving what did not exist, which is needed for the heir. Unlike the claimant of the property, what is established by istishab is the continuation of his ownership, not its renewal. Ownership in purchase is attributed to the purchase itself, not to the ownership of the purchase's final existence, and it is a cause for ownership such that it would not be realized if it did not cause it. Purchase is established by evidence. Here, the establishment of the heir's ownership is attributed to the property being the deceased's at the time of death, not to death itself, because it is not a cause for ownership; rather, according to him, it is established if he had property that was free.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rules for testifying on behalf of an heir claiming property from a deceased person. The author first states the general principle: if a person testifies that property belonged to the deceased at the time of death, that testimony alone is not sufficient for the heir to be granted the property; the cause of inheritance (al-jarr) must also be established. In contrast, for a living person who claims that the property was his in the past, testimony to that effect is accepted based on istishab (the presumption of continuity), because the original state is that what was once owned continues to be owned. Similarly, if a living person produces evidence that he purchased the property from someone, he does not need to prove the seller's ownership at the time of the sale, because the contract of sale is legally a cause for ownership. Death, however, is not a cause for ownership but rather removes ownership, so the heir must prove that the deceased owned the property at the moment of death. The author then details the requirement of al-jarr (linking the heir to the deceased) and the need to specify the exact relationship (e.g., full brother or half-brother). Several cases from secondary works (al-Bazzaziyya, al-Zahiriyya) illustrate these principles. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is then presented: Abu Yusuf holds that if witnesses testify that the property belonged to the deceased without specifying the time of death, it is sufficient, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf's companions, i.e., Muhammad and others) require explicit mention that the property was owned at the time of death. The distinction from the living claimant case is based on the nature of istishab: istishab preserves existing ownership but does not establish new ownership, which is what the heir needs. The purchase case is different because purchase itself is a cause of ownership. The passage concludes by emphasizing that the heir's ownership is attributed to the deceased's ownership at death, not to the death itself.

Key Terms
الاستصحاب (al-istishab): A legal principle that presumes the continuation of a previous state until evidence of change is produced. Here, it is used to presume the continuation of ownership for a living claimant.
الجر (al-jarr): The requirement that witnesses explicitly link the heir to the deceased (e.g., by stating the relationship and that the property was inherited).
الوارث (al-warith): The heir who claims property from the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is testimony that property belonged to the deceased not sufficient for the heir without specifying the time of death, while testimony for a living claimant is sufficient?
A) Because the living claimant has stronger rights to the property
B) Because istishab can preserve existing ownership but cannot establish new ownership for the heir
C) Because witnesses must always specify the time for any testimony
D) Because inheritance is not considered a valid cause for ownership

Key Takeaway
For an heir, istishab cannot create new ownership; the time of death must be proven explicitly in testimony.

Testimony to Possession Alone: The Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony to possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on testimony to possession alone and explain why Abu Yusuf's contrary view is rejected, using the distinction between known and unknown matters.

Core Idea
Testimony to mere possession is rejected in Hanafi law because possession is ambiguous—it could be ownership, trust, or guarantee—and a court cannot rule on the unknown.

In this passage, the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the debate over whether testimony that a person possessed a property for a period suffices to prove ownership. While Abu Yusuf analogizes possession to ownership, the majority Hanafi position insists that possession is too indefinite to form a basis for judgment. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The base text states that testimony to possession is rejected. Note the key phrase 'ردت' (it is rejected).
The matn likely comes from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
State Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that possession is a significant legal concept like ownership, and since testimony to ownership is accepted, testimony to possession should also be accepted by analogy.
His view is transmitted as 'وعن أبي يوسف أنها تقبل'.
3
Analyze the majority's response
The majority (al-Zahir, which includes Abu Hanifa and the two companions) responds that possession is unknown (majhul) because it can arise from ownership, trust, or guarantee. A judge cannot rule on an unknown matter.
The text states 'الشهادة قامت بمجهول'.
4
Distinguish from testimony to taking (akhdh)
The text contrasts possession with 'taking' (akhdh), which is known and implies the obligation to return. Testimony to taking is accepted because it is clear and definite.
This distinction shows that the ruling is not arbitrary.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the majority, a claimant cannot prove ownership through testimony of mere possession; according to Abu Yusuf, he can.
The relied-upon position is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو) شهدا بيدجي منذ شهر ردت وعن أبي يوسف أنها تقبل لأن اليد مقصودة كالملك، ولو شهدوا أنها ملكه تقبل فكذا هذا وصار كما لو شهدا بالأخذ من المدعي ووجه الظاهر وهو قولهما إن الشهادة قامت بمجهول لأن اليد منقضية وهي متنوعة إلى ملك وأمانة وضمان فتعذر القضاء بإعادة المجهول بخلاف الملك لأنه معلوم غير مختلف، وبخلاف الأخذ لأنه معلوم وحكمه معلوم وهو وجوب الرد. وقوله منذ شهر ليس بقيد فإن الخلاف ثابت فيما لم يذكره فإنه ذكر الإمام التمرتاشي : لو شهدوا لحي أن العين كان في يده لم تقبل لأن قوله : (لا كما يتوهم من كلام (المصنف فيه أن قوله بلا جر» يشمل الجر من المدعي والشاهد على أن الكلام في الشهادات لا في الدعاوى قوله : ( ومن الشروط قول الشاهد لا وارث له غيره) ظاهره أنه شرط لقبول الشهادة والحكم بها والمراد أنه شرط لقبولها في الحال بدليل قوله «لإسقاط
His saying: (And if) they testify to possession for a month, it is rejected. And from Abu Yusuf that it is accepted because possession is intended like ownership; if they testify that it is his ownership, it is accepted, so the same applies here. And it becomes like if they testified to taking from the claimant. The apparent view, which is their statement, is that the testimony is based on an unknown matter because possession is transient and varies (being ownership, trust, or guarantee), so judgment cannot be given on the unknown, unlike ownership because it is known and not subject to variation, and unlike taking because it is known and its ruling is known, which is the obligation to return. His saying 'for a month' is not a restriction; the dispute exists even if he did not mention it. Indeed, Imam al-Timirtashi mentioned: If they testify for a living person that the property was in his hand, it is not accepted because his saying: (Not as is understood from the author's words that his saying 'without al-jarr' includes al-jarr from the claimant and the witness, but the discussion is about testimonies, not lawsuits. His saying: (And among the conditions is the witness saying 'he has no other heir') apparently it is a condition for accepting the testimony and ruling by it, and what is meant is that it is a condition for accepting it at the moment, as evidenced by his saying 'to remove'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage deals with a dispute regarding testimony to possession (yad) rather than ownership. The matn states that if witnesses testify to possession for a month, it is rejected. Abu Yusuf disagrees and holds that it is accepted because possession (yad) is a significant legal concept like ownership; if testimony to ownership is accepted, testimony to possession should be as well, analogous to testifying that the claimant took the property. However, the majority (al-Zahir) view, which is the position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf's view is stated separately), is that such testimony is based on an unknown matter because possession is ambiguous—it could be ownership, trust, or guarantee—so the judge cannot rule on it. In contrast, ownership is clear and unambiguous, and 'taking' (akhdh) is also clear and implies the obligation to return. Therefore, testimony to possession alone is not accepted. The phrase 'for a month' is not a restriction; the same dispute applies even if no duration is mentioned. The text then references Imam al-Timirtashi's ruling that if witnesses testify that a living person had property in his hand, it is not accepted. The passage then seems to transition back to the conditions for testimony in inheritance, but the text cuts off. The final line appears to be a comment on the condition 'la waritha lahu ghayruhu', but it is incomplete.

Key Terms
اليد (al-yad): Possession of a property, which can be indicative of ownership but is also consistent with other legal relationships (trust, guarantee).
المجهول (al-majhul): An unknown matter that cannot be ruled upon in court because it is ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the majority of Hanafi scholars reject testimony to possession (yad) alone?
A) Because possession does not imply any legal relationship
B) Because possession is ambiguous and can be based on ownership, trust, or guarantee
C) Because witnesses must always testify to ownership
D) Because possession is not a legal concept

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony to mere possession is rejected because possession is an unknown matter; only testimony to a known basis like ownership or taking is sufficient.

Conditions for Accepting Inheritance Testimony and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Past Possession
Conditions and intra-Hanafi disputes on inheritance testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting inheritance testimony in Hanafi fiqh and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding testimony on past possession.

Core Idea
Testimony on past possession is rejected because possession is ambiguous; the dispute illustrates how the school weighs certainty.

Inheritance claims often rely on witness testimony, but Hanafi fiqh imposes strict conditions to prevent fraud and ensure certainty. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq outlines these conditions, including the controversial requirement that witnesses negate other heirs and the debated question whether past possession can be proven by testimony. The intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on the latter issue highlights the tension between analogical reasoning and the demand for clarity in evidentiary matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for accepting inheritance testimony
List the explicit conditions from the text: the witness must have seen the deceased, must state 'no heir other than him' (or equivalent), and must link the deceased to the heir (jarr) in certain cases. Note that jarr is a condition for the claim's validity, not just for judgment.
The text distinguishes between cases where the property is with the seller vs. a third party.
2
Analyze the dispute on the phrase negating other heirs
Compare Abu Hanifa's acceptance of 'I do not know of any heir other than him' with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's requirement for the explicit negative 'there is no heir other than him'. Understand the practical impact: acceptance removes the judge's obligation to delay (talawwum).
The phrase must be stated in the present tense and relates to the deceased's estate.
3
Examine the dispute on testimony on past possession (yad munqadiyya)
Contrast the majority position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rejecting testimony on past possession due to ambiguity (ownership, trust, guarantee) with Abu Yusuf's acceptance by analogy to ownership and taking (akhdh). Trace the analogical reasoning: qiyas from ownership is rejected because ownership is uniform; qiyas from taking is rejected because taking has a clear legal consequence (return).
The text states that if the property was in the claimant's hand and the defendant confesses or witnesses testify to the confession, it is handed over.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
According to al-Bahr al-Raiq, the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: testimony on past possession is not accepted. The text supports this by calling it 'the apparent view' (wajh al-zahir).
This is a tarjih within the Hanafi school, favoring the majority over Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الاختلاف في الشهادة
۲۰۱
صح
أن يفسر فيقول عمه لأبيه وأمه أو لأبيه أو لأمه، ويشترط أيضاً أن يقول ووارثه وإذا أقام البينة لا بد للشهود من نسبة الميت والوارث حتى يلتقيا إلى أب واحد وكذلك هذا في الأخ والجد ا هـ . . وفي البزازية وكذا إذا شهدوا أنه ابن ابنه أو بنت ابنه لا بد أن يقولوا إنه وارثه. وقيد بالملك لأن إثبات شراء المورث لا يتوقف على الجد لما في الظهيرية : ادعى داراً في يد رجل أن أباه اشتراها من ذي اليد بألف درهم ومات أبوه فجحد البائع ذلك دعواه وإن لم يذكر في دعواه أن أباه مات وتركها ميراثاً له وهو الذي يقال الجر شرط عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لصحة الدعوى، ثم القاضي يسأل البينة فإذا أقام البينة على ذلك وقالوا لا نعلم له وارثاً غيره يقضي القاضي بالبينة ويأمر المدعي أن ينقد الثمن، ولو كانت الدار في يد رجل آخر غير البائع لا بد من الجر لصحة الدعوى ا هـ . وبه ظهر أن الجر شرط صحة الدعوى لا كما يتوهم من كلام المصنف من أنه شرط القضاء بالبينة فقط. ومن شرط قبول الشهادة بالميراث أن يدرك الشاهد الميت ولذا قال في البزازية : شهدا أن فلان بن فلان مات وترك هذه الدار ميراثاً ولم يدركا الميت فشهادتهما باطلة لأنهما شهدا بملك لم يعاينا سببه ولا رأياه في يد المدعي ؛ كذا في البزازية. ومن الشروط قول الشاهد لا وارث له غيره. وفي البزازية : ويشترط ذكر لا وارث له غيره لإسقاط التلوم عن القاضي. وقوله لا أعلم له وارثاً غيره عندنا بمنزلة ولا وارث له غيره ولو قال لا وارث له غيره بأرض كذا تقبل عنده خلافاً لهما ا هـ. ولا يشترط ذكر اسم الميت حتى لو شهدوا أنه جده أبو أبيه ووارثه ولم يسم الميت تقبل بدون ذكر اسم الميت. وفي الأقضية شهدا بأنه جد الميت وقضى له به ثم جاء آخر وادعى أنه أبو الميت وبرهن فالثاني أحق بالميراث شهدا أنه أخو الميت وقضى له به شهد هذان لآخر على أنه ابن الميت أيضاً لا يبطل القضاء الأول بل يضمنان للثاني ما أخذ الأول من الميراث؛
كذا في البزازية .
قوله : (ولو) شهدا بيده منذ شهر ردت وعن أبي يوسف أنها تقبل لأن اليد مقصودة كالملك، ولو شهدوا أنها ملكه تقبل فكذا هذا وصار كما لو شهدا بالأخذ من المدعي ووجه الظاهر وهو قولهما إن الشهادة قامت بمجهول لأن اليد منقضية وهي متنوعة إلى ملك وأمانة وضمان فتعذر القضاء بإعادة المجهول بخلاف الملك لأنه معلوم غير مختلف، وبخلاف الأخذ لأنه معلوم وحكمه معلوم وهو وجوب الرد. وقوله منذ شهر ليس بقيد فإن الخلاف ثابت فيما لم يذكره فإنه ذكر الإمام التمرتاشي : لو شهدوا لحي أن العين كان في يده لم تقبل لأن قوله : (لا كما يتوهم من كلام المصنف فيه أن قوله بلا جر» يشمل الجر من المدعي والشاهد على أن الكلام في الشهادات لا في الدعاوى قوله : ( ومن الشروط قول الشاهد لا وارث له غيره) ظاهره أنه شرط لقبول الشهادة والحكم بها والمراد أنه شرط لقبولها في الحال بدليل قوله «لإسقاط
منذ شهر ردت ولو أقر المدعى عليه بذلك أو شهد شاهدان أنه أقر أنه كان في يد المدعي دفع إلى المدعي .
Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Disputes in Testimony. Correct: he should explain saying: his paternal uncle from father and mother, or from father, or from mother. And it is also required that he say: 'and his heir.' And when he presents the evidence, the witnesses must specify the relationship of the deceased and the heir so that they meet at one father. Similarly, this applies to the brother and the grandfather, etc. And in al-Bazzaziyya: likewise if they testify that he is his son's son or his daughter's son, they must say he is his heir. And it is restricted to ownership because proving the purchase of the deceased does not depend on the grandfather, as in al-Zahiriyya: someone claimed a house in the hand of a man that his father bought it from the possessor for a thousand dirhams and his father died, and the seller denied that claim, and if he did not mention in his claim that his father died and left it as inheritance for him, this is what is called 'al-jarr' (linking) which is a condition according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad for the validity of the claim. Then the judge asks for evidence, and if he provides evidence and they say 'we do not know of any heir other than him,' the judge rules by the evidence and orders the claimant to pay the price. And if the house was in the hand of another person other than the seller, al-jarr is necessary for the validity of the claim, etc. From this it is clear that al-jarr is a condition for the validity of the claim, not as is mistakenly understood from the author's statement that it is only a condition for ruling by the evidence. Among the conditions for accepting testimony on inheritance is that the witness must have witnessed the deceased. Hence it is said in al-Bazzaziyya: two testified that so-and-so son of so-and-so died and left this house as inheritance, but they did not witness the deceased; their testimony is invalid because they testified to ownership whose cause they did not observe nor saw it in the hand of the claimant. Similarly in al-Bazzaziyya. Among the conditions is the witness's statement: 'there is no heir other than him.' And in al-Bazzaziyya: it is required to mention 'there is no heir other than him' to remove the judge's obligation of postponement (talawwum). And his statement 'I do not know of any heir other than him' according to us is equivalent to 'there is no heir other than him.' And if he said 'there is no heir other than him in such land,' it is accepted according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), etc. And it is not required to mention the name of the deceased, so if they testified that he is his grandfather, father's father, and his heir, and they did not name the deceased, it is accepted without mentioning the name of the deceased. And in al-Aqdiya: two testified that he is the grandfather of the deceased and the judge ruled in his favor, then another came and claimed that he is the father of the deceased and proved it; the second is more entitled to the inheritance. If two testified that he is the brother of the deceased and the judge ruled in his favor, then these two testified for another that he is also the son of the deceased, the first judgment is not invalidated; rather they are liable to the second for what the first took from the inheritance. So in al-Bazzaziyya. His statement: (And if) they testified that he had it in his hand since a month, it is rejected. And from Abu Yusuf: it is accepted because hand (possession) is intended like ownership, and if they testified that it is his ownership, it is accepted; so too this, and it becomes like if they testified to taking from the claimant. And the apparent view is their statement: the testimony has been established on something unknown, because the hand has ceased and it is diverse into ownership, trust, and guarantee; so judgment is impossible due to ignorance, unlike ownership because it is known and not diverse, and unlike taking because it is known and its ruling is known, which is the obligation to return. And his statement 'since a month' is not a restriction, for the dispute exists even if not mentioned. For Imam al-Tamirtashi mentioned: if they testified for a living person that the object was in his hand, it is not accepted, because his statement: '... not as is mistakenly understood from the author's statement that his expression 'without linking' includes linking from the claimant and the witness, considering that the discussion is in testimonies, not in claims. His statement: (And among the conditions is the witness's statement: 'there is no heir other than him') its apparent meaning is that it is a condition for accepting the testimony and ruling by it, and the intent is that it is a condition for accepting it at that moment, due to his statement: 'to remove the postponement (talawwum).' Then on page 202: 'since a month' is rejected, and if the defendant confessed to that or two witnesses testified that he confessed that it was in the hand of the claimant, it is handed over to the claimant.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal discussion on the conditions for accepting testimony regarding inheritance and possession. It begins by explaining that when witnesses testify to a relationship, they must specify the degree (e.g., paternal uncle from both parents or from one side), and also state that the person is an heir. This is required so that the lineage connects to one common ancestor. The condition of 'jarr' (linking the deceased to the heir) is highlighted: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is a condition for the validity of the claim itself, not just for the judgment. This is clarified by the example where someone claims a house bought by his deceased father: if the house is still with the seller, he can claim without mentioning inheritance; but if it is with a third party, he must explicitly state the inheritance link. Another condition is that the witness must have seen the deceased; if they only heard, their testimony is invalid. They must also explicitly say 'there is no heir other than him' to free the judge from the obligation to delay judgment (talawwum). There is a dispute: Abu Hanifa accepts the phrase 'I do not know of any heir other than him' as sufficient, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree. The text then discusses a case where two conflicting proofs are presented (one claiming grandfather, another father) and the latter takes precedence. Then it addresses testimony about past possession (yad) from a month ago. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject it because possession is ambiguous (could be ownership, trust, or guarantee), while Abu Yusuf accepts it analogizing to testimony on ownership. The commentary defends the majority view that testimony on possession is not accepted due to its ambiguity, unlike ownership which is clear. Finally, if the defendant confesses or witnesses testify to his confession that the item was in the claimant's hand, it is handed over to the claimant.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Possession; in this passage, it refers to physical control over property, which can be based on ownership, trust, or guarantee, and thus is ambiguous for testimony.
جر (jarr): Linking the deceased to the heir in a claim, i.e., explicitly stating the inheritance relationship (e.g., 'his father died and left it as inheritance').
تلوم (talawwum): Postponement of judgment by the judge to investigate if any other heir exists; the condition 'there is no heir other than him' removes the need for this.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if two witnesses testify that a man's father's father is his heir but they do not name the deceased?
A) The testimony is rejected because the deceased must be named.
B) The testimony is accepted without mentioning the name of the deceased.
C) The testimony is accepted only if they also state 'no other heir'.
D) The testimony is invalid because they did not witness the deceased.

Key Takeaway
Inheritance testimony in Hanafi fiqh requires strict conditions: witnessing the deceased, explicitly negating other heirs, and in some cases linking the deceased to the heir; testimony on past possession is rejected due to ambiguity.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Ruling on Testimony on Testimony (Shahada 'ala al-Shahada)
States the principle and condition for accepting testimony on testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony on testimony and identify the condition of shubha (doubt) and the number of witnesses required.

Core Idea
Testimony on testimony is accepted only in matters not voided by shubha, and only when two men testify on two witnesses.

Islamic courts rely on testimony to establish facts. Sometimes, witnesses cannot testify directly but can relay the testimony of others. This lesson explains the Hanafi position on such secondary testimony, clarifying its conditions and limitations. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate how the school balances evidence with caution, especially in serious cases like hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'shahada 'ala al-shahada' (testimony on testimony). The ruling is that it is accepted (tuqbal), meaning it is a valid form of evidence.
The ruling is one of permissibility and validity, not obligation.
2
Identify the shubha condition
The acceptance is limited to matters that are 'not invalidated by shubha'. Shubha refers to doubt that could nullify the underlying case, such as in hudud (fixed punishments) or qisas (retaliation). Therefore, testimony on testimony is not accepted in those cases.
This is a key distinction: the restriction is on the subject matter, not the witnesses.
3
Identify the witness requirement
The condition for acceptance is that two men testify on the testimony of two original witnesses. Testimony on the testimony of a single witness is not accepted.
The requirement of two mirrors the general rule for testimony (two male witnesses).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a financial dispute where the original witnesses are deceased. If two upright men heard them testify and can relay that testimony, the judge may accept it, provided the case does not involve hudud or qisas.
This shows the practical scope: property, debts, marriage, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الشهادة على الشهادة
تقبل فيما لا يسقط بالشبهة إن شهد رجلان على شهادة شاهدين لا شهادة واحد
Chapter on Testimony on Testimony. It is accepted in matters that are not invalidated by doubt, if two men testify on the testimony of two witnesses, not the testimony of one.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on testimony on testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada). The ruling is that this type of secondary testimony is accepted only in matters that are not subject to shubha (doubt) - meaning cases where the original matter is not one that could be voided by doubt, such as hudud (fixed punishments) or qisas (retaliation). The condition is that two witnesses must testify on the testimony of two original witnesses; testimony on the testimony of a single witness is not accepted. This is because secondary testimony is weaker, and it requires a higher standard of verification. The primary sources (al-Nihaya, Jami' al-Fusulayn) are referenced for further detail.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony given by witnesses about the testimony of other witnesses (secondary testimony).
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that invalidates punishment or liability; in the context of testimony, it refers to matters like hudud and qisas where additional precautions are taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is testimony on testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) accepted according to this passage?
A) It is accepted in all cases equally.
B) It is accepted only in cases not invalidated by doubt (shubha).
C) It is accepted only if the original witnesses are deceased.
D) It is accepted only if the testifying witnesses saw the original event.

Key Takeaway
Testimony on testimony is a valid form of evidence in Hanafi fiqh, but only for cases not subject to shubha, and requires two men relaying the testimony of two original witnesses.
