Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony upon Testimony: Acceptance and Number of Witnesses
Opening rulings for testimony upon testimony, including acceptance, conditions, and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony upon testimony, identify the conditions for acceptance, and explain the dispute with al-Shafi'i on the number of subsidiary witnesses.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is accepted in rights not repelled by doubt, requiring two subsidiary witnesses.

This lesson examines the opening rulings of the chapter on testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada) from the Hanafi tradition. We will learn when this form of evidence is accepted, the required number of subsidiary witnesses, and the key dispute with al-Shafi'i. The passage is from al-Hidayah's commentary and includes essential principles for understanding evidence law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle of acceptance
Determine which types of cases accept testimony upon testimony. The text states it is accepted in matters not invalidated by doubt (shubha). This excludes hudud and qisas.
Istihsan is the basis due to necessity.
2
Determine the number of witnesses required
The text requires two men (or one man and two women) to testify on the testimony of two original witnesses. The subsidiary witnesses must form a complete niṣāb.
This applies even if the original witnesses are women.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Al-Shafi'i requires four subsidiary witnesses (two on each original witness) while Hanafi requires two total. Compare the proofs: Hanafi cites the hadith of Ali and qiyas; Shafi'i uses an analogy to women.
Important: the practical consequence differs in burden of proof.
4
Explore special cases
The text discusses testimony upon judgment, a son testifying on his father's testimony, and testimony involving disbelievers. Note each ruling.
Some cases, like testimony on judgment, are disputed within Hanafi.
5
Distinguish testimony upon testimony from testimony upon judgment
Testimony on a judge's judgment is a separate category. While testimony upon testimony is accepted in rights, testimony upon judgment has specific conditions and is not accepted in certain cases.
Be careful not to conflate the two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اليد محتملة يد غصب أو يد ملك فإن كانت يد غصب عن ذي اليد لا تجب إعادته، وإن كانت يد ملك تجب فلا تجب بالشك؛ كذا في النهاية وجامع الفصولين قوله: (ولو أقر المدعى عليه بذلك أو شهد شاهدان أنه أقر أنه كان في يد المدعي دفع إلى المدعي) لأن الإقرار معلوم فتصح الشهادة به وجهالة المقر به لا تمنع صحة الإقرار وفي البزازية : الأصل في باب الشهادة أن الشهادة بالملك المنقضي مقبولة لا باليد المنقضية لأن الملك لا يتنوع واليد تتنوع باحتمال أنه كان له فاشتراه منه ا هـ . قيد بالإقرار باليد مقصوداً لأنه لو أقر له بها ضمناً لم تدفع إليه كما سيأتي في الإقرار وإنما قال دفع إليه دون أن يقول إنه إقرار بالملك له لأنه لو الحقيقة هو الخارج، ولو أقر المدعي عليه أني أخذته من المدعي لأنه كان ملكي فلو كذبه المدعي في الأخذ منه لا يؤمر بالتسليم إلى المدعي إقراره وبرهن على ذي اليد، ولو صدقه يؤمر بتسليمه إلى المدعي فيصير المدعي ذا يد فيحلف أو يبرهن الآخر ا هـ . وقيد بكونه أقر أنه كان بيده لأنه لو أقر أنه كان بيد المدعي بغير حق ففيه اختلاف ؛ قيل هو إقرار له باليد وبه يفتى وقيل لا إلا أن يقر أنه كان بيده بحق؛ كذا في جامع الفصولين. وقيد بالإقرار بكونه في يد المدعي لأنه لو ادعى عقاراً فأقر المدعى عليه أنه بيده لم تقبل حتى يبرهن المدعي أو يعلم القاضي بخلاف المنقول وسيأتي في الدعوى إن شاء الله تعالى والله أعلم. لا يخفى حسن تأخير شهادة الفروع عن الأصول قوله : (تقبل فيما لا يسقط بالشبهة) التلوم والمراد بالتولم تأخير القضاء مدة حتى يغلب على ظنه أن لا وارث له كما أفاده في متفرقات القضاء عند قوله «تركة قسمت بين الورثة أو الغرماء الخ وتمام المسألة هناك عن شرح أدب القضاء فراجعها قوله : (وشمل التقرير الخ) الظاهر أنه التعزير لأنه المصرح به في الأجناس . أي يقبل أداء الفروع في حق لا تسقطه اللشبهة استحساناً لشدة الحاجة إليها إذ شاهد الأصل أداء الشهادة لبعض العوارض فلو لم تجز الشهادة على شهادته أدى إلى إتواء الحقوق ولهذا جوزنا الشهادة على الشهادة وإن كثرت إلا أن فيها شبهة من حيث البدلية أو من حيث إن فيها زيادة الاحتمال وقد أمكن الاحتراز عنه بجنس الشهود فلا تقبل فيما يندرئ بالشبهات كالحدود والقصاص. أطلقه فشمل الوقف وهو الصحيح إحياء له وصوناً عن اندراسه، وشمل التقرير وهو مصرح به في الأجناس وقضاء القاضي وكتابه كما في الخانية، وما في المبسوط من أن الشاهدين لو شهدا على شهادة شاهدين أن قاضي بلدة كذا حد فلاناً قذف تقبل حتى ترد شهادة فلان لا يرد نقضاً على قولنا لا تقبل في الحدود فإن المشهود به فعل القاضي وهو مما يثبت مع الشبهات والمراد بالشهادة بالحد الشهادة بوقوع أسبابها الموجبة لها مع أن في المحيط لا تقبل هذه الشهادة وشمل النسب كما في خزانة المفتين. وفي القنية : أشهد القاضي شهوداً أني حكمت لفلان على فلان بكذا فهو إشهاد باطل لا عبرة به والحضور شرط اهـ. وفي يتيمة الدهر : وكتبت إلى الحسن بن زياد إذا أشهد القاضي على قضائه الشاهدين اللذين شهدا في تلك الحادثة هل يصح إشهاده اياهما ؟ فقال : نعم لكنه ينفصل عن القبول في الحكم ا هـ . قوله : (إن) شهد رجلان على شهادة شاهدين أي كل من الشاهدين فعلى كل أصل شاهدن، سواء كانا هما أو غيرهما وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز الأربع على كل أصل اثنان لأن كل شاهدين قائمان مقام واحد فصارا كالمرأتين. ولنا قول علي رضي الله عنه لا يجوز على شهادة رجل إلا شهادة رجلين ولأن نقل شهادة الأصل من الحقوق فهما لو شهدا بحق ثم شهدا بحق آخر فتقبل. وقوله «رجلان» وقع اتفاقاً لأنه يجوز أن يشهد عليها رجل وامرأتان لتمام النصاب وكذا لا يشترط أن يكون المشهود على شهادته رجلاً لأن للمرأة أيضاً أن تشهد على شهادتها رجلين أو رجلاً وامرأتين ويشترط أن يشهد على شهادة كل امرأة نصاب الشهادة ؛ كذا ذكر الشارح. وقد توهم المقدسي في الحاوي أنه قيد احترازي فقال : ولا تقبل شهادة النساء على الشهادة ا.هـ. وهو غلط أطلق الرجلين فشمل شهادة الابن على شهادة الأب فإنها جائزة وعلى قضائه لا يجوز؛ كذا الخلاصة. في وصحح في خزانة المفتين وفي البرازية الجواز على قضائه أيضاً. وفي كافي الحاكم : وإن شهد كافران على شهادة مسلمين لكافر على كافر بحق لم تجز، وكذا لو شهد كافران على قضاء قاض لكافر أو المسلم على كافر ولو شهد مسلمان على شهادة كافر جازت الشهادة ا هـ .
قوله : (لا شهادة واحد على شهادة واحد أي لا تقبل أطلق في الواحد الثاني فشمل المرأة لما قدمناه أنه لا بد من نصاب الشهادة على شهادتها. والمراد من الواحد الأول ما كان أقل من نصاب الشهادة فلذا قال في الخزانة : ولو أن عشرة نسوة شهدن على شهادة واحد أو على شهادة امرأتين أو على شهادة امرأة لا يقبل الحاكم ذلك حتى يشهد معهن رجل ا هـ .
Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony. It is accepted in what is not invalidated by doubt, if two men testify on the testimony of two witnesses, not the testimony of one. The hand (possession) may be a hand of usurpation or a hand of ownership. If it was a hand of usurpation from the possessor, its return is not obligatory; and if it was a hand of ownership, it is obligatory, so it does not become obligatory due to doubt. Thus in al-Nihaya and Jami' al-Fusulayn. His saying: (And if the defendant confessed to that, or two witnesses testified that he confessed that it was in the possession of the plaintiff, it is given to the plaintiff) because the confession is known, so testimony by it is valid, and ignorance of the thing confessed does not prevent validity of confession. In al-Bazzaziyya: The principle in the chapter of testimony is that testimony of elapsing ownership is accepted, not of elapsing possession, because ownership does not vary, while possession varies by the possibility that it was his and he bought it from him etc. It is restricted to confession of possession intentionally, because if he confessed it implicitly, it would not be given to him as will come in confession. And he only said 'given to him' without saying it is a confession of ownership, because if he proved that it was his ownership, it is accepted. For in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He took an item from the hand of another and said, 'I took it from his hand because it was my property,' and he proved that, it is accepted, because although he is a possessor by virtue of the present situation, since he confessed taking it from him, he confessed that the real possessor is the other. And if the defendant confessed, 'I took it from the plaintiff because it was my property,' if the plaintiff denies his taking, he is not ordered to hand over to the plaintiff due to his confession and proof of possession; if he affirms him, he is ordered to hand it over to the plaintiff, so the plaintiff becomes a possessor, so he either takes an oath or the other proves. It is restricted to his confessing that it was in his hand, because if he confessed that it was in the plaintiff's hand without right, there is disagreement: it is said it is a confession of possession and by it is given fatwa; and it is said no, unless he confesses that it was in his hand by right. Thus in Jami' al-Fusulayn. And it is restricted to confession that it is in the plaintiff's hand, because if he claimed real estate and the defendant confessed that it was in his hand, it is not accepted until the plaintiff proves or the judge knows, unlike movables, and it will come in the claim if Allah wills. And Allah knows best. It is not hidden the goodness of delaying the testimony of branches (subsidiary witnesses) from the roots (original witnesses). His saying: (accepted in what is not invalidated by doubt): The meaning of 'talmm' is delaying the judgment for a time until it dominates his opinion that there is no heir for him, as is mentioned in the miscellany of judgment at his saying 'an estate divided among heirs or creditors etc.' and the complete discussion there from Sharh Adab al-Qada. So refer to it. His saying: (And it includes the punishment etc.) Apparently it is ta'zir because it is explicitly stated in al-Ajnas. That is, the performance of branches is accepted in a right that is not invalidated by doubt, by istihsan due to the extreme need for it, since the original witness may be prevented from performing testimony due to some obstacles. If testimony upon his testimony were not permitted, it would lead to loss of rights. Therefore we allowed testimony upon testimony even if multiplied, except that there is doubt in it from the perspective of substitution or because it has increased probability, and it is possible to guard against it by the type of witnesses, so it is not accepted in what is repelled by doubts, such as hudud and qisas. He made it unrestricted, so it includes waqf, and that is the correct view to revive it and protect it from being lost. And it includes punishment (ta'zir), and it is explicitly stated in al-Ajnas, and the judgment of the judge and his book, as in al-Khaniyya. What is in al-Mabsut that if two witnesses testify on the testimony of two witnesses that the judge of such a town had flogged so-and-so for slander, it is accepted until the testimony of so-and-so is rejected, does not contradict our saying that it is not accepted in hudud, because what is testified to is the act of the judge, which is established despite doubts. And what is meant by testimony of hadd is testimony of occurrence of its causes that obligate it, although in al-Muhit this testimony is not accepted. And it includes lineage as in Khizanat al-Muftin. In al-Qunniyya: If the judge makes witnesses testify that I gave judgment for so-and-so against so-and-so for such, it is invalid testimony, no consideration to it, and presence is a condition. And in Yatimah al-Dahr: I wrote to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad: if the judge makes the two witnesses who testified in that incident testify to his judgment, is it valid? He said: Yes, but it is separate from acceptance in the ruling. His saying: (if two men testify on the testimony of two witnesses) i.e., each of the two witnesses testifies on each original witness, whether they are the same or others. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible to have four on each original two, because every two witnesses stand in place of one, so they become like two women. Our proof is the saying of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'It is not permissible on the testimony of one man except the testimony of two men,' and because the transmission of the testimony of the original is from rights, so if two witnessed a right then witnessed another right, it is accepted. His saying 'two men' occurred by agreement, because it is permissible that one man and two women testify on it for completing the number, and likewise it is not required that the one whose testimony is witnessed be a man, because a woman may also have two men or one man and two women testify on her testimony, and it is required that the number of testimony be witnessed on the testimony of each woman; thus mentioned the commentator. Al-Maqdisi in al-Hawi mistakenly thought it was a restrictive condition and said: 'The testimony of women on testimony is not accepted.' That is a mistake. He made 'two men' unrestricted, so it includes the testimony of a son on the testimony of his father, for it is permissible, but on his judgment it is not permissible; thus in al-Khulasa. And it is corrected in Khizanat al-Muftin and in al-Baraziyya the permissibility on his judgment also. In Kafi al-Hakim: If two disbelievers testify on the testimony of two Muslims for a disbeliever against a disbeliever for a right, it is not valid. Likewise if two disbelievers testify on the judgment of a judge for a disbeliever or a Muslim against a disbeliever, and if two Muslims testify on the testimony of a disbeliever, the testimony is valid. His saying: (not the testimony of one on the testimony of one) i.e., it is not accepted. He made the second 'one' unrestricted, so it includes women, because we have said that the full number of testimony is required for testifying on her testimony. And what is meant by the first 'one' is what is less than the full number of testimony. Therefore it is said in al-Khizanah: If ten women testify on the testimony of one, or on the testimony of two women, or on the testimony of one woman, the judge does not accept that until a man testifies with them.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada) from al-Hidayah's text. The author first states the core ruling: testimony upon testimony is accepted in matters that are not invalidated by doubt (i.e., financial rights, property, contracts) but not in hudud and qisas, because these are repelled by doubts. This is based on istihsan due to necessity: if the original witness cannot testify (due to death, travel, etc.), the subsidiary witness may testify to preserve rights. The passage then discusses the condition that two men must testify on the testimony of two witnesses, not one witness. A dispute with al-Shafi'i is presented: Shafi'i requires four witnesses (two on each original witness), while Hanafi requires only two in total. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of Ali (رضي الله عنه) and qiyas: just as two witnesses can testify to a right, they can testify to another testimony. The text further clarifies that this condition is not restrictive: a man and two women can serve as subsidiary witnesses, and women can be the subject of testimony upon testimony, provided a full complement (two men or one man two women) testifies. The passage also applies the ruling to waqf, ta'zir, judgment of a judge, and lineage. Special cases are noted: testimony of a son on his father's testimony is admissible, but on his judgment is disputed. Testimony of disbelievers is not accepted on behalf of Muslims, but Muslims can testify on the testimony of a disbeliever for a right. Finally, the condition that one witness cannot testify on the testimony of one witness is explained: the minimum for testifying on another's testimony is the full number (two men or one man two women); less than that is not accepted even with many women.

Key Terms
الشهادة على الشهادة (al-shahāda ʿalā al-shahāda): Testimony of subsidiary witnesses who testify to the testimony of original witnesses, used when original witnesses cannot testify directly.
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents application of hadd penalties; matters repelled by such doubts are not proven by testimony upon testimony.
نصاب الشهادة (niṣāb al-shahāda): The required number of witnesses for a valid testimony; generally two men or one man and two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, in which of the following matters is testimony upon testimony accepted?
A) Hudud penalties
B) Qisas (retaliation)
C) Financial rights (huquq)
D) Marriage contracts

Key Takeaway
Testimony upon testimony is accepted in all rights except hudud, qisas, and matters repelled by doubts, with the condition that two men (or one man and two women) testify on the testimony of two original witnesses.

Testimony upon Testimony: Istihsan and Exceptions
Ruling on accepting shahada ala shahada and its exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shahada ala shahada, explain the istihsan rationale, and identify the exceptions (hudud, qisas) with their underlying principle.

Core Idea
Shahada ala shahada is accepted by istihsan to prevent loss of rights, but rejected in hudud and qisas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada). It explains the basis of istihsan due to necessity and outlines the exceptions. As a future faqih, you must understand where this secondary testimony is permissible and where it is blocked, and why the school uses istihsan over strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State the Hanafi position: testimony upon testimony is accepted in all rights except those repelled by doubts. The basis is istihsan due to necessity (hajah) to prevent loss of rights (idha' al-huquq).
Note the term 'istihsan'—a departure from qiyas for a stronger reason.
2
Examine the exceptions
Identify the exceptions: hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). These are repelled by doubts (shubahat). Since secondary testimony involves a degree of doubt, it is not accepted.
The principle: 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubahat' (punishments are averted by doubts).
3
Apply the ruling to specific cases
Work through the applications mentioned: waqf (endowments), tax registers (taqrir), judge's decree (qada'), and lineage (nasab). These are all included because the rights involved are not repelled by doubts.
Note the objection about flogging for qadhf: the testimony is about the judge's action, not the hadd itself, so it is accepted.
4
Understand the rational for istihsan
The text states that if secondary testimony were not allowed, it would lead to loss of rights (idha' al-huquq). This necessity justifies the departure from the general rule that testimony should be first-hand.
Istihsan is a valid source of law in the Hanafi school, especially when strict analogy would cause hardship.
5
Distinguish from other schools
Although not explicitly in the text, note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require original witnesses to be unavailable or have stricter conditions. The Hanafi position is broader due to istihsan.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference based on different usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الشهادة على الشهادة قد يعجز عن في أي يقبل أداء الفروع في حق لا تسقطه اللشبهة استحساناً لشدة الحاجة إليها إذ شاهد الأصل أداء الشهادة لبعض العوارض فلو لم تجز الشهادة على شهادته أدى إلى إتواء الحقوق ولهذا جوزنا الشهادة على الشهادة وإن كثرت إلا أن فيها شبهة من حيث البدلية أو من حيث إن فيها زيادة الاحتمال وقد أمكن الاحتراز عنه بجنس الشهود فلا تقبل فيما يندرئ بالشبهات كالحدود والقصاص. أطلقه فشمل الوقف وهو الصحيح إحياء له وصوناً عن اندراسه، وشمل التقرير وهو مصرح به في الأجناس وقضاء القاضي وكتابه كما في الخانية، وما في المبسوط من أن الشاهدين لو شهدا على شهادة شاهدين أن قاضي بلدة كذا حد فلاناً قذف تقبل حتى ترد شهادة فلان لا يرد نقضاً على قولنا لا تقبل في الحدود فإن المشهود به فعل القاضي وهو مما يثبت مع الشبهات والمراد بالشهادة بالحد الشهادة بوقوع أسبابها الموجبة لها مع أن في المحيط لا تقبل هذه الشهادة وشمل النسب كما في خزانة المفتين.
The Book of Testimonies, Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony. He may be unable to perform [the original]. It means: the testimony of substitutes is accepted in a right that is not nullified by doubt, as a matter of istihsan due to the severe need for it, because the original witness may be prevented from performing the testimony due to some impediments. If testimony upon his testimony were not permitted, it would lead to loss of rights. Therefore we have permitted testimony upon testimony, even if numerous, except that there is a doubt in it from the aspect of substitution or from the aspect that it involves increased probability, and it is possible to avoid that by the type of witnesses. So it is not accepted in matters that are repelled by doubts, such as hudud and qisas. He made it absolute, so it includes waqf, which is the correct view, to preserve it and protect it from being obliterated; and it includes the [tax] register, which is explicitly mentioned in al-Ajnas; and the judge's decree and his writing, as in al-Khaniyyah. And what is in al-Mabsut that if two witnesses testify upon the testimony of two witnesses that the judge of such-and-such a town had flogged so-and-so for slander, it is accepted, even if the testimony of so-and-so is rejected, does not refute our statement that it is not accepted in hudud, because the subject of testimony is the judge's action, which is established despite doubts; and what is meant by testimony of hadd is testimony regarding the occurrence of its causes that necessitate it, although in al-Muhit it is stated that such testimony is not accepted. And it includes lineage, as in Khizanat al-Muftin.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with a proof, explaining when testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada) is accepted in the Hanafi school. The author states that it is accepted for rights that are not invalidated by doubt (i.e., financial rights and similar), based on istihsan due to necessity. Original witnesses may be unable to attend court, so allowing secondary witnesses prevents loss of rights. However, this type of testimony involves doubt because it is second-hand, so it is not accepted in punishments (hudud and qisas) that are repelled by doubts. The ruling is general, including waqf (endowments) because there is a need to preserve them, and tax records, judges' decrees, and writings. The author addresses an objection: even though flogging for qadhf (slander) is a hadd, if witnesses testify that the judge ordered it, the testimony is accepted because the subject is the judge's action, not the hadd itself. However, al-Muhit says such testimony is not accepted. The passage also includes lineage (nasab) as a matter where testimony upon testimony is accepted.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada ala shahada): Testimony given by a witness who has heard the original witness testify, repeating that testimony in court.
إتواء الحقوق (idha' al-huquq): Loss or destruction of rights that would occur if secondary testimony were not allowed.
شبهة (shubhah): Doubt or ambiguity that causes a ruling to be averted (e.g., hudud are averted by doubts).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Istihsan due to necessity

D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Shahada ala shahada is accepted by istihsan to prevent loss of rights, except in hudud and qisas which are repelled by doubts.

Number of Witnesses for Testimony upon Testimony
Inter-madhhab dispute on nisab of secondary witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required number of secondary witnesses for testimony upon testimony and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school, including the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
For testimony upon testimony, Hanafis require two secondary witnesses per original, while Shafi'is require four in total for two originals.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nisab (required number) of secondary witnesses when testifying upon the testimony of original witnesses. The ruling has direct implications for court proceedings. Understanding the dispute clarifies how each school uses textual evidence (dalil naqli) and analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi rule
Identify the Hanafi position: two secondary witnesses are required for each original witness. Note that the same two secondary witnesses can testify on behalf of multiple originals.
This is the mufta bihi position based on the hadith of 'Ali (RA).
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that each pair of secondary witnesses stands in place of one original witness, so for two originals, four secondary witnesses are needed. He analogizes the pair to two women (i.e., half of a male witness).
The Shafi'i position is mukhtalaf fih.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis cite the hadith of 'Ali (RA): 'Testimony upon the testimony of a man is not accepted except by two men.' This text explicitly requires two secondary witnesses for each original, without requiring distinct pairs.
The word 'rajulain' (two men) is taken as the minimum, not a restriction on gender or identity.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
The Hanafis counter that the analogy (qiyas) to women is invalid because the original witness can be female, and the law allows a man and two women as secondary witnesses. The requirement adapts to the gender of the original.
Thus, the nisab for secondary witnesses mirrors that of original testimony: two men, or one man and two women.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if there are two original witnesses, Hanafis accept the same two secondary witnesses to testify on both originals, while Shafi'is require four distinct secondary witnesses (two for each original). This changes the number of witnesses needed in court.
The difference affects the efficiency and feasibility of testimony upon testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إن) شهد رجلان على شهادة شاهدين أي كل من الشاهدين فعلى كل أصل شاهدان، سواء كانا هما أو غيرهما وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز الأربع على كل أصل اثنان لأن كل شاهدين قائمان مقام واحد فصارا كالمرأتين. ولنا قول علي رضي الله عنه لا يجوز على شهادة رجل إلا شهادة رجلين ولأن نقل شهادة الأصل من الحقوق فهما لو شهدا بحق ثم شهدا بحق آخر فتقبل. وقوله «رجلان» وقع اتفاقاً لأنه يجوز أن يشهد عليها رجل وامرأتان لتمام النصاب وكذا لا يشترط أن يكون المشهود على شهادته رجلاً لأن للمرأة أيضاً أن تشهد على شهادتها رجلين أو رجلاً وامرأتين ويشترط أن يشهد على شهادة كل امرأة نصاب الشهادة ؛ كذا ذكر الشارح. وقد توهم المقدسي في الحاوي أنه قيد احترازي فقال : ولا تقبل شهادة النساء على الشهادة ا.هـ. وهو غلط أطلق الرجلين فشمل شهادة الابن على شهادة الأب فإنها جائزة وعلى قضائه لا يجوز؛ كذا الخلاصة. في وصحح في خزانة المفتين وفي البرازية الجواز على قضائه أيضاً. وفي كافي الحاكم : وإن شهد كافران على شهادة مسلمين لكافر على كافر بحق لم تجز، وكذا لو شهد كافران على قضاء قاض لكافر أو المسلم على كافر ولو شهد مسلمان على شهادة كافر جازت الشهادة ا هـ .
His statement: “If two men testify upon the testimony of two witnesses” means each of the two witnesses (i.e., the secondary witnesses) testifies upon the testimony of each original witness, so there are two secondary witnesses for each original witness, whether they are the same two or different ones. Al-Shafi’i said: “It is not permissible; four [secondary witnesses] are required, two for each original, because each pair of secondary witnesses stands in place of one [original], so they become like two women.” Our proof: The statement of ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): “Testimony upon the testimony of a man is not accepted except by two men.” Also, because the transmission of the original testimony is a right; if they testify upon one right and then upon another right, it is accepted. And his saying “two men” is accidental, because it is permissible that a man and two women testify upon her [the original female witness] testimony to complete the required number. Similarly, it is not required that the one whose testimony is being witnessed be a man, because a woman may also have two men or a man and two women testify upon her testimony. And it is required that for each woman's testimony, the full number (nisab) of witnesses is present. So mentioned the commentator. Al-Maqdisi erroneously thought in al-Hawi that it was a restrictive condition and said: “The testimony of women upon testimony is not accepted.” That is a mistake. He made “two men” absolute, so it includes the testimony of a son upon the testimony of his father; it is permissible, but upon his decree (qa’da) it is not permissible. So in al-Khulasa. And it is authenticated in Khizanat al-Muftin and al-Bazzaziyyah that it is also permissible upon his decree. In Kafi al-Hakim: If two disbelievers testify upon the testimony of two Muslims for a disbeliever against a disbeliever regarding a right, it is not allowed. Similarly, if two disbelievers testify upon the decree of a judge for a disbeliever or a Muslim against a disbeliever. But if two Muslims testify upon the testimony of a disbeliever, the testimony is allowed.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the required number of secondary witnesses when testifying upon the testimony of original witnesses. The Hanafi position is that for each original witness, two secondary witnesses are needed, regardless of whether they are the same two for all originals or different. Imam al-Shafi’i disagreed, requiring four secondary witnesses (two for each original) because each pair stands in place of one original, equating them to women. The Hanafis counter with the hadith of ‘Ali (RA) that “testimony upon the testimony of a man is not accepted except by two men,” and analogy with other rights. The commentator clarifies that “two men” is not a restrictive condition; it is permissible for a man and two women to testify upon a female original witness. Hence, women can be secondary witnesses. The passage also addresses special cases: a son can testify upon his father’s testimony but not upon his judicial decree (some authenticate permissibility), and the ruling for disbelievers’ testimony.

Key Terms
شاهد أصل (shahid asl): The original witness who directly witnessed the event or right.
نصاب الشهادة (nisab al-shahada): The required number of witnesses (e.g., two men, or one man and two women).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hanafis require two secondary witnesses for each original witness, but the same two can serve for multiple originals, unlike the Shafi'i requirement of distinct pairs.

Ruling: One Witness Upon One Witness Is Not Accepted
Ruling statement: secondary testimony conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding secondary testimony and identify which combinations of witnesses are accepted or rejected.

Core Idea
A single secondary witness cannot replace the nisab; full complement is required even when testifying upon another's testimony.

This passage clarifies an important principle in Hanafi testimony law: the testimony of one person upon the testimony of one person is not accepted. The term 'one' is interpreted strictly, and even when multiple secondary witnesses testify, they must collectively meet the minimum nisab for the original testimony. Let's parse the conditions and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The text opens with a clear ruling: 'No testimony of one upon the testimony of one.' Understand that 'one' in the first position refers to the secondary witness (far'), and 'one' in the second position refers to the original witness (asl).
The ruling is absolute: it is not accepted (la tuqbal).
2
Interpret the scope of 'one'
The second 'one' is made absolute, meaning it includes a woman as the original witness. Thus, even if the original witness is a woman, a full nisab of secondary witnesses is required. The first 'one' means less than the nisab (i.e., a single witness).
Al-Khazanah explains: even ten women testifying upon one man are insufficient until a man joins them.
3
Apply the rule to complex scenarios
Consider cases where the secondary witnesses are a full nisab (e.g., two men) but testifying upon a single original. The judge does not act until another original testimony is provided. Also, examine a case where a secondary witness later testifies upon his own testimony: this is invalid because it would establish three-fourths of a right from one witness.
The rule preserves the integrity of testimony by requiring proper nisab at both levels.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا شهادة واحد على شهادة واحد أي لا تقبل أطلق في الواحد الثاني فشمل المرأة لما قدمناه أنه لا بد من نصاب الشهادة على شهادتها. والمراد من الواحد الأول ما كان أقل من نصاب الشهادة فلذا قال في الخزانة : ولو أن عشرة نسوة شهدن على شهادة واحد أو على شهادة امرأتين أو على شهادة امرأة لا يقبل الحاكم ذلك حتى يشهد معهن رجل ا هـ . وأشار إلى أنه لو شهد النصاب على شهادة واحد لم يقض فلو شهد عشرة على شهادة واحد تقبل ولكن لا يقضي حتى يشهد شاهد آخر لأن الثابت بشهادتهم شهادة واحد؛ كذا الخزانة. وفي البزازية معزياً إلى الأصل : شهدا على رجل وأحدهما في شهادة فرع عن آخر ثم شهد هذا بعد نقل شهادة الأصل على شهادة نفسه لا تقبل لأدائه إلى أن يثبت بشهادة واحد ثلاثة أرباع الحق وأنه خلاف وضع الشهادة، ولو شهد واحد على شهادة نفسه وآخران على شهادة غيره يصح ا هـ
His statement: “No testimony of one upon the testimony of one” means it is not accepted. He made the second “one” absolute, so it includes a woman, as we mentioned earlier that the full number (nisab) of witnesses is required for testifying upon her testimony. And what is meant by the first “one” is what is less than the nisab of testimony. Hence al-Khazanah said: “If ten women testify upon the testimony of one man, or upon the testimony of two women, or upon the testimony of one woman, the judge does not accept it until a man testifies with them.” And he indicated that if the full nisab testifies upon the testimony of one [original witness], he does not judge. So if ten testify upon the testimony of one, it is accepted, but he does not judge until another witness testifies, because what is established by their testimony is the testimony of one [original]. So stated al-Khazanah. In al-Bazzaziyyah, attributed to the original: “Two [secondary witnesses] testified against a man, and one of them was a secondary witness from another [original], then this [secondary] after transmitting the original testimony testifies upon his own testimony: it is not accepted, because it leads to three-fourths of the right being established by one witness, and that is contrary to the nature of testimony. But if one testifies upon his own testimony and two others upon the testimony of someone else, it is valid.”
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining that the testimony of a single secondary witness upon the testimony of a single original witness is not accepted. The term 'one' in the second position includes a woman, meaning even if a woman is the original, a full nisab of secondary witnesses is required. The first 'one' means less than the nisab (a single witness). So if ten women testify upon the testimony of one man, it is insufficient until a man joins them. Even if the secondary witnesses are a full nisab for one original, the judge does not act until another original testimony is provided, because only one original's testimony is established. The passage also discusses a complex case: two secondary witnesses testify against a man, but one of them is a secondary witness from another original; then after transmitting, he testifies upon his own testimony. This is invalid because it would mean that one witness's testimony establishes three-fourths of the right, contradicting the purpose of testimony. However, if one testifies upon his own and two others upon another's, it is valid.

Key Terms
نصاب الشهادة (nisab al-shahada): The minimum number of witnesses required for testimony to be valid (e.g., two men or one man and two women).
شهادة واحد على شهادة واحد (shahada wahid 'ala shahada wahid): Testimony of one secondary witness upon the testimony of one original witness; ruled not accepted.
خزانة (al-Khazanah): A Hanafi legal text (likely a reference work) cited for the ruling on secondary testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Not accepted until a man testifies with them
C) Accepted because the nisab of witnesses is complete
D) Accepted if they are all trustworthy

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony requires a full nisab (two men or one man and two women) for the original testimony, and even then judgment may be delayed until a second original testifies.

Required Wording for Bearing Testimony upon Testimony
Explanation of the required wording for ishhad (bearing testimony upon testimony).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact Arabic wording required for ishhad and identify the conditions that make it valid, including the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the location of hearing.

Core Idea
The secondary witness must use precise wording—'ashhadu ‘ala shahadati anni ashhadu'—or the testimony is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains the precise wording a secondary witness must use when bearing testimony upon testimony (ishhad). The Hanafi school requires explicit assignment (tahmil) and a specific formulation to avoid ambiguity and potential falsehood. Understanding these conditions is crucial for the validity of such testimony in court. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding whether the secondary must have heard the original in court or outside it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its required wording
The act is ishhad: a secondary witness (far‘) bears testimony upon the testimony of an original witness (asl). The required wording is 'ashhadu ‘ala shahadati anni ashhadu anna fulanan aqqara ‘indi bi kadha.' Note each part: 'ashhad', 'ala shahadati', 'anni ashhadu'.
2
Understand the need for tahmil and tawkil
The secondary is like a deputy (na’ib), so the original must explicitly assign (tahmil) by saying 'ashhad' and authorize (tawkil) the secondary. Without these, the secondary cannot testify.
The secondary is not a true agent; otherwise combining original and secondary witnesses from different originals would be problematic.
3
Parse the restrictions (qayd) on the wording
The phrase is restricted with 'ashhad' (must be the verb 'ashhad', not a request), 'ala shahadati' (must specify 'upon my testimony', not 'bi shahadati' or '‘alayya'), and 'ala' (must be 'upon', not 'bi'). Each restriction avoids ambiguity that could lead to lying.
Alternative wordings like 'ashhad ‘alayya' could be understood as testifying against oneself, which is a command to lie.
4
Analyze the secondary's acceptance
Silence upon assignment is sufficient acceptance. However, explicit rejection ('la aqbal') prevents the secondary from becoming a witness. The text also notes that hearing in court allows testimony without explicit wording? Actually, for court hearing, the secondary can testify without the original saying 'ashhad'? The passage mentions that if the secondary hears in court, he can testify, but the restriction of wording still applies? The text is ambiguous; we follow the restriction that the original must say 'ashhad' even in court? Actually, the commentary says that if the secondary hears the witness in court, he can testify without explicit assignment. But the main text says the opposite. We need to note the dispute.
Al-Ramli clarifies that the requirement of explicit 'ashhad' applies when hearing outside court; hearing in court suffices.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa allows the secondary to testify if he heard the original outside court; Abu Yusuf disallows it. The later scholars prefer Abu Yusuf's view as more precautionary (ahwat).
The precautionary view is that testimony should not be borne based on out-of-court hearing to avoid potential inaccuracies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والإشهاد أن يقول اشهد على شهادتي أني أشهد أن فلاناً أقر عندي بكذا لأن الفرع كالنائب عنه فلا بد من التحميل والتوكيل ولا بد أن يشهد عند القاضي لينقله إلى مجلس القاضي. ولم يذكر المؤلف بعد قوله أقر عندي بكذا وأشهدني على نفسه لأنه ليس بشرط لأن من سمع إقرار غيره حل له الشهادة وإن لم يقل له اشهد كما قدمناه. وإنما قالوا الفرع كالنائب ولم يجعلوه نائباً لما قدمناه أن له أن من يقضي بشهادة أصل وفرعين عن أصل آخر، ولو كان الفرع نائباً حقيقة لما جاز الجمع بين الأصل والخلف؛ كذا في النهاية. وقد يقال إنه فرع عمن تعذر حضوره لا عن الأصل الحاضر فلا يضر الجمع لو جعل نائباً حقيقة إذ هو جمع بين أصل وفرع أصل آخر . قيد بقوله «اشهد» لأنه لو لم يقل له اشهد لم يسعه أن يشهد على شهادته وإن سمعها منه لما قدمناه وقيد بقوله «على شهادتي» لأنه لو قال اشهد علي بذلك لم تجز له الشهادة لأنه لفظ يحتمل لاحتمال أن يكون الإشهاد على نفس الحق المشهود به فيكون أمراً بالكذب. وقيد بـ«على» لأنه لو قال بشهادتي لم تجز له لاحتمال أن يكون أمراً بأن يشهد مثل شهادته بالكذب وقيد بالشهادة على الشهادة لأن الشهادة بقضاء القاضي صحيحة وإن لم يشهدهما القاضي عليه. وذكر في الخلاصة اختلافاً بين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف فيما إذا سمعاه في غير مجلس القضاء فجوزه أبو حنيفة وهو ،، ومنعه أبو يوسف وهو الأحوط ا هـ . وأشار بعدم اشتراط قبوله إلى أن سكوت الفرع عند تحميله يكفي لكن لو قال لا أقبل قال في القنية : ينبغي أن لا يصير شاهداً حتى لو قوله : (قيد بقوله اشهد لأنه لو لم يقل له أشهد لم يسعه أن يشهد الخ قال الرملي : وفي السراج الوهاج نقلاً عن النهاية أن هذا محله فيما إذا سمعه في غير مجلس القضاء، أما لو سمع في مجلس القضاء شاهداً يشهد جاز له أن يشهد على شهادته اهـ قوله : (فيما إذا سمعاه) أي الشاهدان سمعا القاضي. وفي البزازية : سمعا من الحاكم يقول حكمت لهذا على هذا بكذا ثم نصب حاكم آخر لهما أن يشهدا به عليه إن سمعاه منه في المصر وهو الأحوط والذي عليه علم الهدى(۱) والمتأخرون أن (۱) قوله ( علم الهدى) هو الإمام الماتريدي اهـ منه . الأقيس،
His statement: “And al-ishhad is that he says: I testify upon my testimony that I bear witness that so-and-so confessed to me about such-and-such,” because the secondary witness is like a deputy of him [the original], so there must be assignment (tahmil) and authorization (tawkil). And he must testify before the judge to transfer it to the court. The author did not mention after “confessed to me about such-and-such” the phrase “and he asked me to bear witness against himself” because it is not a condition; whoever hears another’s confession is permitted to testify even if he did not say “bear witness [against me],” as we have stated. They said the secondary witness is like a deputy, but they did not make him a deputy in reality, because as we said, he can [the judge] judge based on the testimony of an original and two secondary witnesses from another original. If the secondary were truly a deputy, it would not be permissible to combine the original and the substitute; so stated in al-Nihayah. It may be said that he is a deputy for one whose presence is difficult, not for the original who is present, so the combination does not harm if he is made a true deputy, because it is a combination of an original and the substitute of another original. He restricted with the word “ashhad” because if he did not say to him “ashhad” [I testify], it is not permissible for him to testify upon his testimony even if he heard it from him, as we stated. And he restricted with “ala shahadati” because if he said “ashhad ‘alayya bi dhalik” (testify against me regarding that), it is not permissible for him to testify, because the wording is ambiguous, as it might imply testifying upon the very right itself, which would be a command to lie. And he restricted with “ala” [upon] because if he said “bi shahadati” (with my testimony), it is not permissible, due to the probability that it is a command to testify like his testimony, which is a lie. And he restricted with testimony upon testimony because testimony regarding the judge’s decree is valid even if the judge did not make them witness over it. Mentioned in al-Khulasa a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding when they heard it outside the court: Abu Hanifa permitted it, and Abu Yusuf prohibited it, and that is more precautionary. And he indicated by not requiring acceptance that the silence of the secondary witness upon his assignment (tahmil) is sufficient, but if he said “I do not accept,” it is said in al-Qunyah: “He does not become a witness; even if he…” Then his statement: “He restricted with the word ‘ashhad’ because if he did not say ‘ashhad’ to him, it is not permissible for him to testify…” Al-Ramli said: In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, quoting from al-Nihayah, that this applies when he heard it outside the court. As for if he heard in the court a witness testifying, it is permissible for him to testify upon his testimony. Then his statement: “When they heard it” i.e., the two witnesses heard the judge. In al-Bazzaziyyah: “They heard from the judge saying: ‘I have decreed for this against this regarding such-and-such,’ then another judge is appointed; they may testify regarding it against him if they heard it from him in the city, and that is the precautionary view, and the view of ‘Ilm al-Huda (Imam al-Maturidi) and the later scholars is that the more analogical [view]…
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the proper wording for bearing testimony upon testimony (ishhad). The secondary witness must say: “Ashhad ‘ala shahadati anni ashhadu anna fulanan aqqara ‘indi bi kadha” (I testify upon my testimony that I bear witness that so-and-so confessed to me about such-and-such). This is because the secondary is like a deputy, requiring explicit assignment (tahmil) and authorization (tawkil). The author notes that the original witness does not need to explicitly ask for bearing testimony; simply hearing the confession suffices for the original. The secondary is not a true deputy, otherwise combining original and secondary witnesses would be problematic. The wording must include “ashhad” (I testify), “ala shahadati” (upon my testimony), and “ala” (upon). Variations like “ashhad ‘alayya” (testify against me) or “bi shahadati” (with my testimony) are invalid due to ambiguity. There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: if the secondary hears the original outside the court, Abu Hanifa allows it, Abu Yusuf does not, with the latter being more precautionary. Silence of the secondary upon assignment is sufficient acceptance, but explicit rejection prevents him from becoming a witness. The text also discusses hearing from a judge: if the judge declares his decree, the secondary can testify upon it if heard in the mosque (city), according to later scholars including al-Maturidi.

Key Terms
إشهاد (ishhad): The act of bearing testimony upon testimony; the secondary witness confirms that he heard the original witness testify.
تحميل (tahmil): The assignment of the original witness to the secondary witness to bear testimony on his behalf.
توكيل (tawkil): Authorization, similar to agency; the secondary acts as a deputy but not a true agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct wording for a secondary witness according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ashhadu anna fulanan aqqara (I bear witness that so-and-so confessed)
B) Ashhadu ‘ala shahadati anni ashhadu anna fulanan aqqara (I testify upon my testimony that I bear witness that so-and-so confessed)
C) Ashhadu ‘alayya bi dhalik (I testify against me regarding that)
D) Ushhiduka an tashhada (I ask you to testify)

Key Takeaway
The validity of bearing testimony upon testimony depends on the exact wording; variations that introduce ambiguity are invalid.

Shahadat — Testimony

Conditions for Valid Ishād (Testimony on Testimony)
Definition of ishad with conditions and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid ishad and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the location of the original testimony.

Core Idea
ISHAD: explicit wording + tahmil + tawkil – but the venue of original testimony is disputed within the school.

In Hanafi court procedure, when an original witness cannot attend, he may delegate his testimony to a branch witness through ishad. This lesson dissects the precise wording and conditions required for such delegation, and explores a key disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his student Abu Yusuf over whether the original testimony must have been heard inside the courtroom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential components of ishad
From the definition, note that the original witness must say 'I testify upon my testimony that I testify...' (ashhadu 'ala shahadati anna ashhad). This phrase includes three elements: the verb 'ashhadu', the preposition 'ala', and the word 'shahadati'. The clause after 'anna' states the content of the original testimony.
Any deviation from this exact structure invalidates the delegation.
2
Recognize why tahmil and tawkil are necessary
The branch witness (far') is like a deputy (na'ib). Therefore, he must receive the burden (tahmil) and explicit authorization (tawkil) from the original witness. Without these, he cannot transmit the testimony.
This distinguishes ishad from ordinary testimony where hearing alone suffices.
3
Understand the restriction to court testimony
The original witness must give his testimony in court (in the presence of the judge) so that the branch can convey it to the judge's court. The passage notes that this is part of the definition.
But this condition is precisely what Abu Yusuf disputes.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The passage records that Abu Hanifa permits ishad even if the original testimony was heard outside court, while Abu Yusuf requires it to be in court for precaution (ihtiyat). Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
This is a legitimate difference within the school; both views are based on evidence.
5
Apply the conditions to determine validity of a given scenario
Given a scenario involving a phrase used or location, decide whether ishad is valid according to Abu Hanifa and/or Abu Yusuf, and specify which condition is satisfied or violated.
This step tests your ability to operationalize the rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على شهادة واحد والإشهاد أن يقول اشهد على شهادتي أني أشهد أن فلاناً أقر عندي بكذا لأن الفرع كالنائب عنه فلا بد من التحميل والتوكيل ولا بد أن يشهد عند القاضي لينقله إلى مجلس القاضي. ولم يذكر المؤلف بعد قوله أقر عندي بكذا وأشهدني على نفسه لأنه ليس بشرط لأن من سمع إقرار غيره حل له الشهادة وإن لم يقل له اشهد كما قدمناه. وإنما قالوا الفرع كالنائب ولم يجعلوه نائباً لما قدمناه أن له أن من يقضي بشهادة أصل وفرعين عن أصل آخر، ولو كان الفرع نائباً حقيقة لما جاز الجمع بين الأصل والخلف؛ كذا في النهاية. وقد يقال إنه فرع عمن تعذر حضوره لا عن الأصل الحاضر فلا يضر الجمع لو جعل نائباً حقيقة إذ هو جمع بين أصل وفرع أصل آخر . قيد بقوله «اشهد» لأنه لو لم يقل له اشهد لم يسعه أن يشهد على شهادته وإن سمعها منه لما قدمناه وقيد بقوله «على شهادتي» لأنه لو قال اشهد علي بذلك لم تجز له الشهادة لأنه لفظ يحتمل لاحتمال أن يكون الإشهاد على نفس الحق المشهود به فيكون أمراً بالكذب. وقيد بـ«على» لأنه لو قال بشهادتي لم تجز له لاحتمال أن يكون أمراً بأن يشهد مثل شهادته بالكذب وقيد بالشهادة على الشهادة لأن الشهادة بقضاء القاضي صحيحة وإن لم يشهدهما القاضي عليه. وذكر في الخلاصة اختلافاً بين أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف فيما إذا سمعاه في غير مجلس القضاء فجوزه أبو حنيفة وهو ،، ومنعه أبو يوسف وهو الأحوط ا هـ .
On testimony upon a single [witness] and ishad is that he says: 'I testify upon my testimony that I testify that so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such' because the branch is like his deputy, so tahmil and tawkil are necessary, and he must testify before the judge to convey it to the judge's court. The author did not mention after his statement 'acknowledged before me such-and-such' and 'he asked me to testify on his behalf' because it is not a condition, since whoever hears another's acknowledgment is permitted to testify even if he did not say to him 'testify', as we have presented. They said the branch is like a deputy, but they did not make him a deputy because we have presented that he may rule by the testimony of an original and two branches from another original, and if the branch were truly a deputy, combining the original and the substitute would not be permissible. It may be said that he is a branch of one whose presence is impossible, not of the present original, so combining would not harm if he were made a true deputy, for it is combining an original and a branch of another original. He restricted it with his statement 'testify' because if he did not say to him 'testify', he could not testify on his testimony even if he heard it from him, as we have presented. He restricted it with 'upon my testimony' because if he said 'testify upon that', his testimony would not be permitted because the wording is ambiguous, possibly being testimony on the very right witnessed, thus being a command to lie. He restricted it with 'upon' because if he said 'with my testimony', it would not be permitted, due to the possibility that it is a command to testify like his testimony, which is a lie. He restricted it to 'testimony upon testimony' because testimony upon a judge's ruling is valid even if the judge did not have them testify before him. In al-Khulasa, a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is mentioned regarding when they heard it outside the court: Abu Hanifa permitted it, and Abu Yusuf prohibited it, which is more precautionary.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage defines the technical term 'ishad' (delegated testimony) and its conditions in Hanafi fiqh. The author explains that the secondary witness (far') acts as a deputy (na'ib) of the original witness (asl), so proper burdening (tahmil) and delegation (tawkil) are required. The original witness must explicitly say 'I testify upon my testimony' (ashhadu 'ala shahadati) in court. The author then clarifies why certain phrases are not acceptable: saying 'testify upon that' (ishhad 'ala dhalik) is ambiguous and could imply perjury; saying 'with my testimony' (bi-shahadati) is similarly problematic. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows secondary testimony even if the original witness testified outside the court, while Abu Yusuf rejects it, considering it more precautionary (al-ahwat). The commentator notes that the restriction to court testimony is for clarity and authenticity.

Key Terms
الإشهاد (al-ishad): The act of the original witness delegating the branch witness to testify on his testimony
التحميل (al-tahmil): The original witness burdening the branch with the testimony
الفرع (al-far'): The secondary witness who testifies on the testimony of the original witness
التوكيل (al-tawkil): The original witness authorizing the branch to act as his deputy in testifying

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if an original witness says to a listener 'ashhadu 'ala dhalik' (testify upon that), is the listener permitted to testify as a branch witness?
A) Yes, because 'ashhadu' indicates delegation.
B) Yes, but only if the listener explicitly accepts.
C) No, because the wording is ambiguous and could imply perjury.
D) No, because the listener must have witnessed the event himself.

Key Takeaway
Valid ishad requires the exact phrase 'ashhadu 'ala shahadati anna ashhadu…' along with explicit tahmil and tawkil; the intra-Hanafi dispute concerns whether the original testimony must have been heard in court.

Shahadat — Testimony

Phrasing and Conditions for Secondary Testimony
Ruling with dispute on phrasing and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shortest acceptable phrasing for branch testimony and identify the three conditions that permit secondary testimony.

Core Idea
Branch testimony requires a clear delegation phrase; it is only allowed when the original witness is dead, ill, or traveling.

Secondary testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is a practical necessity when the original witness cannot appear in court. The Hanafi school has developed specific rules for how the branch witness must phrase his testimony and the circumstances that justify resorting to it. This lesson examines the range of acceptable phrasings, from the longest to the shortest, and the conditions that must be present for the testimony to be valid. Understanding these rules ensures that the testimony conveys the original's claim accurately and is accepted by the judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase variants
The passage lists several phrasings for the branch's performance, differing in length and number of 'shin' letters. The shortest contains two shins: 'Ashhadu 'ala shahadati fulan bi-kadha'. Identify each variant and note which scholars preferred the shortest form.
The shortest form is attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani as recorded in al-Siyar al-Kabir.
2
Examine the identity requirement
The branch must name the original witness and his lineage; vague references make the testimony invalid. Understand why this prevents 'burdening by conjecture' (tahammul bi-mujazafa).
This preserves the chain of testimony and avoids uncertainty.
3
List the conditions for permission
Secondary testimony is only allowed when the original is dead, ill, or traveling. These conditions incapacitate the original, creating a need (haja) for branch testimony. Note that the passage also mentions exceptions, such as a secluded woman (mukhaddara).
Travel is defined differently among Hanafi scholars; the more convenient view (arfaq) allows it even for short distances.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on travel
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) defines travel as a specific distance (e.g., three days journey), while Abu Yusuf and later scholars consider any distance that prevents returning the same day. Recognize which view is mufta bihi.
Fakhr al-Islam and Abu al-Layth prefer the lenient view.
5
Apply the conditions to special cases
The passage extends the permission to secluded women even without travel, and mentions the dispute about imprisoned witnesses. Evaluate whether these cases fit the underlying rationale (need/haja).
Imprisonment is not explicitly listed but is debated among later jurists.

And he indicated by not requiring acceptance that the silence of the branch during his burdening is sufficient, but if he said 'I do not accept,' al-Qunyah says: it is proper that he does not become a witness, even if... And the performance of the branch is that he says: 'I testify that so-and-so asked me to testify on his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before him and said to me: testify upon my testimony such-and-such.' And there is no testimony for the branch except with the death of his original, or his illness, or his travel; if he testifies after that, it is not accepted. In al-Hawi al-Qudsi: It is not proper for a witness to testify on the testimony of one who is not just in his view. And his statement: (And the performance of the branch is that he says: 'I testify that so-and-so asked me to testify on his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such and said to me: testify upon my testimony such-and-such.' Because his testimony and his mention in the testimony of the original and the mention of the middle burdening are necessary, and it has five 'shin's. And there is a longer wording than this with eight 'shin's, and a shorter one with four 'shin's by mentioning 'so-and-so ordered me to testify' dropping 'asked me to testify,' and the shortest of all is what has two 'shins' by saying 'I testify upon the testimony of so-and-so such-and-such.' Muhammad mentioned it in al-Siyar al-Kabir, and it is the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, and it is easier and shorter. It is narrated that Abu Ja'far was opposed by the scholars of his time, so he brought out the narration from al-Siyar, and they submitted to him. His statement 'so-and-so' is an example; otherwise, it is necessary to mention the witness of the original, as in al-Sughra: The branch witnesses must mention the names of the originals and the names of their fathers and grandfathers, so that if they say 'we testify that two men we know asked us to testify on their testimony that they testify such-and-such' and they do not name them or do not know their names, it is not accepted because they undertook a burden based on conjecture, not on knowledge. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And there is no) testimony for the branch except with the death of his original, or his illness, or his travel, because its permissibility is due to need, and it is only resorted to when the original is incapacitated, and with these things incapacitation is realized. And we considered travel because incapacitation [arises] from distance, and the duration of travel is legally considered far, such that many rulings are based on it. And from Abu Yusuf: If he is in a place such that if he went to perform testimony he could not return that night to attend to people's rights. They said: the first is better and it is the apparent narration as in al-Hawi, and the second is more convenient and it is adopted by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth and many shaykhs. And Fakhr al-Islam said: it is good. In al-Sirajiyyah: and on it, it is permissible no matter how, so that it is related from him that if the original was in a corner of the mosque, the fatwa... And if the branch testified on his testimony in another corner of that mosque, their testimony is accepted. And the author's speech indicates that the sultan and the amir are not allowed to be asked for testimony in the city, and it is in al-Qunyah, and the apparent meaning of his speech is restriction, but it is not so, for it is clearly stated in al-Qunyah that if the original is a secluded woman, it is permissible for her to delegate testimony on her testimony, and she is one who does not mix with men, even if she goes out for a need or to the bathhouse. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the original witness is imprisoned in the city and delegates testimony on his testimony, is it permissible for the branch to testify on his testimony? And if he testifies before the judge, does he judge by it? Al-Dhakhirah says: The shaykhs of our time differed. The speech of the scholar and the just is accepted, and the speech of the oppressor and the ignorant is not, except the ignorant just person if he improves his interpretation, it is accepted, otherwise not. And it is no secret that the knowledge of the judges of our land is no more than a doubt, let alone proof, except in the book of the judge due to necessity.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage discusses the performance (ada') of the branch witness and the conditions under which secondary testimony is valid. First, it clarifies that the branch's silence during tahmil is sufficient acceptance; explicit rejection ('I do not accept') prevents him from becoming a witness. Then it details the various acceptable phrasings for the branch's testimony, from longer formulations with eight 'shin' letters to the shortest with only two, which is the choice of Muhammad al-Shaybani (from al-Siyar al-Kabir) and preferred by later Hanafi scholars like Abu al-Layth and al-Sarakhsi for its ease. The passage emphasizes that the branch must identify the original witness by name and lineage; vague references are insufficient. Next, it lists the three conditions that permit secondary testimony: death, illness, or travel of the original witness, because secondary testimony is only allowed due to need (hajah) when the original is incapacitated. Travel is defined as a distance that would cause legal hardship. There is a dispute: the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) defines travel as a specific distance, but Abu Yusuf allows it even for short distances if the original cannot return quickly to fulfill rights. The more convenient view (arfaq) is adopted by many. The passage also notes exceptions: a secluded woman (mukhaddara) may delegate testimony even without travel, and an imprisoned original witness is a matter of dispute among later scholars. Finally, it addresses the character of the judge: only a just and knowledgeable judge's testimony is accepted, but the passage laments that contemporary judges lack such qualifications.

Key Terms
أداء الفرع (ada' al-far'): The branch witness's verbal testimony in court, conveying the original's testimony
المرض (al-marad): Illness of the original witness that prevents him from attending court to testify
السفر (al-safar): Travel of the original witness that makes it difficult to return for testimony
التحميل (al-tahmil): The act of burdening the branch witness by the original, asking him to bear testimony
الشين (al-shin): The Arabic letter 'shin' (ش); used as a shorthand to count the occurrences of the phrase 'ashhadu' or 'shahada' in the performance wording

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the shortest acceptable phrasing for the branch witness's performance according to the passage?
A) أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته أن فلاناً أقر بكذا
B) أشهد على شهادة فلان بكذا
C) أمرني فلان أن أشهد
D) لا يصير شاهداً

Key Takeaway
Branch testimony must use a clear delegation phrase and is only permitted when the original witness is dead, ill, or traveling, with the shortest phrasing being the preferred practice.

The Required Wording for Secondary Testimony (Shahadat al-Far')
Explaining the required phrasing for a secondary witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum required phrasing for a secondary witness and explain why the two-shin form is preferred according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The secondary witness must explicitly link his testimony to the primary; the shortest accepted form contains only two 'shin' letters.

In Hanafi law, a witness may testify on another's testimony under necessity, but the wording must be precise. This lesson examines the phrasing required for secondary testimony (shahadat al-far'), focusing on the shortest form that the school ultimately adopted after scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The secondary witness (al-far') must testify using a specific phrase that links his testimony to the primary witness (al-asl). The ruling is that this wording is a condition for acceptance.
2
Recognize the condition for accepting secondary testimony
The secondary's testimony is only accepted when the primary is dead, ill, or traveling. If the secondary testifies without this, the testimony is rejected.
This condition is separate from the wording.
3
Examine the variant wordings
The author lists four forms based on the number of 'shin' letters: eight, five, four, and two. The five-shin form is the 'middle authorization' (al-tahmil al-awsat); the two-shin form is the shortest.
The number of 'shin' letters refers to the letter 'ش' in the Arabic phrasing.
4
Follow the tarjih (preference) for the shortest form
Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir mentions the two-shin form: 'اشهد على شهادة فلان بكذا'. Later authorities like Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and al-Sarakhsi chose it. Abu Ja'far faced opposition but proved it from the source, leading to acceptance.
This demonstrates how madhhab positions are established through textual evidence and scholarly consensus.
5
Note the additional requirement of naming the primary
The secondary must identify the primary by name and lineage; otherwise, the testimony is rejected as reckless.
This is from al-Sughra, quoted in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بكذا وأداء الفرع أن يقول اشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته أن فلاناً أقر عنده وقال لي اشهد على شهادتي بكذا ولا شهادة للفرع إلا بموت أصله أو مرضه أو سفره فإن شهد بعد ذلك لا تقبل ا هـ . وفي الحاوي القدسي : ولا ينبغي أن يشهد الشاهد على شهادة من ليس بعدل عنده ا هـ . وهو قوله : ( وأداء الفرع أن يقول أشهد أن فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته إن فلاناً أقر عندي بكذا وقال لي اشهد على شهادتي بكذا لأنه لا بد من شهادته وذكره في شهادة الأصل وذكر التحميل الأوسط وفيه خمس شينات، ولها لفظ أطول من هذا فيه ثماني شينات وأقصر منه ، أربع شينات بذكر أمرني فلان أن أشهد بإسقاط أشهدني وأقصر من الكل ما فيه شينان بأن يقول أشهد على شهادة فلان بكذا ذكره محمد في السير الكبير وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث وأبي جعفر وشمس الأئمة السرخسي، وهو أسهل وأيسر وأقصر وروي أن أبا جعفر كان يخالفه فيه علماء عصره فأخرج لهم الرواية من السير فانقادوا إليه . وقوله «فلان» تمثيل وإلا فلا بد من بيان شاهد الأصل لما في الصغرى : شهود الفرع يجب أن يذكروا أسماء الأصول وأسماء آبائهم وأجدادهم حتى لو قالا نشهد أن رجلين نعرفهما أشهدانا على شهادتهما أنهما يشهدان بكذا وقالا لا نسميهما أو لا نعرف أسماءهما لم تقبل لأنهما تحملا مجازفة لا عن معرفة ا هـ . والله أعلم
And the performance of the secondary witness is that he says: 'I bear witness that so-and-so asked me to bear witness on his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such, and said to me: Bear witness on my testimony of such-and-such.' And there is no testimony for the secondary witness except with the death of the primary, or his illness, or his travel; if he testifies after that, it is not accepted. End quote. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: It is not appropriate for a witness to testify on the testimony of one who is not upright in his view. End quote. And his statement: (And the performance of the secondary is that he says: 'I bear witness that so-and-so asked me to bear witness on his testimony that so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such and said to me: Bear witness on my testimony of such-and-such') because his testimony and mention of it in the testimony of the primary and the mention of the middle authorization is necessary. In it are five 'shin' letters. And it has a longer wording than this with eight 'shin' letters, and a shorter one with four 'shin' letters by mentioning 'so-and-so ordered me to bear witness' dropping 'asked me'. And the shortest of all is what has two 'shin' letters, that he says: 'I bear witness on the testimony of so-and-so such-and-such.' This was mentioned by Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir, and it is the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, and it is the easiest, simplest, and shortest. And it is narrated that Abu Ja'far was opposed by the scholars of his time, but he brought out the narration from al-Siyar for them, so they submitted to him. And his statement 'so-and-so' is an example; otherwise, it is necessary to specify the primary witness, as in al-Sughra: Secondary witnesses must mention the names of the primaries, their fathers, and their grandfathers, such that if they said 'we testify that two men we know asked us to bear witness on their testimony that they testify to such-and-such' and they do not name them or know their names, it is not accepted because they undertook it recklessly, not from knowledge. End quote. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the proper wording for secondary testimony (shahadat al-far'). The author begins by stating the ruling that secondary testimony is only accepted when the primary witness is dead, ill, or traveling. Then he elaborates on the phrasing. The key point is that the secondary witness must explicitly state that he is testifying on the testimony of the primary. Several forms are mentioned: a long form with eight 'shin' letters, a middle form with five, a shorter with four, and the shortest with only two. The preferred form according to Imam Muhammad, Abu al-Layth, Abu Ja'far, and al-Sarakhsi is the two-shin form: 'Ashhadu 'ala shahadati fulanin bi-kadha' (I bear witness on the testimony of so-and-so such-and-such). This was controversial but was established by citing a narration from al-Siyar al-Kabir. The author also notes that the secondary must identify the primary by name and lineage; otherwise, the testimony is rejected as reckless.

Key Terms
الفرع (al-far'): The secondary witness who testifies on the testimony of the primary witness (al-asl).
الأصل (al-asl): The primary witness whose testimony is being transmitted by the secondary witness.
شهادة على شهادة (shahadat 'ala shahada): Testimony upon testimony; indirect testimony where a secondary witness repeats the original witness's testimony.
التحميل الأوسط (al-tahmil al-awsat): The intermediate form of authorization that includes an intermediate phrase like 'he said to me: bear witness'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Four
C) Five
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the secondary witness to explicitly link his testimony to the primary using a concise phrase; the minimum accepted is the two-shin form from al-Siyar al-Kabir.
