Secondary Testimony: The Dispute Over Travel as an Excuse
Stating the three excuses and the intra-Hanafi dispute on travel duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the strict and lenient Hanafi views on travel as an excuse for secondary testimony and identify the operative ruling.

Core Idea
Travel excuses secondary testimony only if the primary witness is absent for three days and nights - but a more lenient view permits it for any absence.

Secondary testimony (shahādat al-farʿ) is permitted only when the primary witness is unable to testify directly due to death, illness, or travel. But what counts as travel? The Hanafi school has a well-known intra-madhhab dispute on this point, with the dominant view requiring an absence of three days and nights, while a more lenient view, attributed to Abu Yusuf and later scholars, accepts even a short absence. Understanding this dispute sharpens our ability to apply the school's rulings with precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three excuses for secondary testimony
Read the opening phrase: secondary testimony is allowed only with death, illness, or travel of the primary witness. Understand that these excuses make the primary unable to testify directly.
The three excuses are exhaustive according to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the rationale for the excuses
The text explains that permissibility is based on need (ḥājah) and inability (ʿajz) of the primary. Each excuse must genuinely prevent the primary from attending court.
Illness must prevent attendance; travel must be a real distance.
3
Analyze the dispute on the duration of travel
The dominant view (ẓāhir al-riwāyah) requires the primary to be absent for three days and nights (masīrat thalāthat ayyām). Abu Yusuf holds that even a shorter trip suffices if the primary cannot return home the same day. Later scholars like Abu al-Layth allow any real absence, even within the same city.
The source mentions the example of moving from one corner of the mosque to another.
4
Determine the operative ruling (muftā bihī)
The text from al-Khāniyyah and others indicates that the relied-upon position is the strict view requiring three days and nights. This is the position adopted for fatwa, though the lenient view is noted as more convenient (arfaq).
Knowing the muftā bihī is crucial for practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا) شهادة للفرع إلا بموت أصله أو مرضه أو سفره لأن جوازها عند الحاجة وإنما تمس عند عجز الأصل وبهذه الأشياء يتحقق العجز به وإنما اعتبرنا السفر لأن العجز بعد المسافة ومدة السفر بعيدة حكماً حتى أدير عليها عدة الأحكام فكذا من هذا الحكم. . وعن أبي يوسف : إن كان في مكان لو غدا إلى أداء الشهادة لا يستطيع أن يبيت في إحياء لحقوق الناس. قالوا: الأول أحسن وهو ظاهر الرواية كما في الحاوي، والثاني أرفق وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث وكثير من المشايخ. وقال فخر الإسلام : إنه حسن . وفي السراجية : وعليه يجوز كيفما كان حتى روي عنه إنه إذا كان الأصل في زاوية المسجد الفتوى. وعن فشهد الفرع على شهادته في زاوية أخرى من ذلك المسجد تقبل شهادتهم. ودل كلام المصنف أن السلطان والأمير لا يجوز إشهادهما في البلد وهي في القنية وظاهر كلامه الحصر في وليس كذلك فقد صرح في القنية بأن الأصل إذا كانت امرأة مخدرة يجوز إشهادها على شهادتها وهي التي لا تخالط الرجال ولو خرجت لقضاء حاجة أو للحمام ا.هـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : إذا كان شاهد الأصل محبوساً في المصر فأشهد على شهادته هل يجوز للفرع أن يشهد على شهادته؟ وإذا شهد عند القاضي هل يحكم بها؟ قال في الذخيرة: اختلف فيه مشايخ زماننا قال كلام العالم والعادل مقبول وكلام الظالم والجاهل لا إلا الجاهل العادل إن أحسن التفسير يقبل وإلا فلا، ولا خفاء أن علم قضاة بلادنا ليس بشبهة فضلاً عن الحجة إلا في كتاب القاضي للضرورة. وأطلق في التهذيب جوازها بحبس الأصل وقيد شهادة الفرع أي . عند القاضي لأن وقت التحمل لا يشترط له أن يكون بالأصول عذر لما في خزانة المفتين والإشهاد على شهادة نفسه يجوز وإن لم يكن بالأصول عذر حتى لو حل بهم العذر من مرض أو سفر أو موت يشهد الفروع ا هـ . وأطلق في مرضه وقيد في الهداية بأن لا يستطيع الحضور إلى مجلس القاضي. وفي شرح المجمع للمصنف : المرض الذي لا يتعذر معه الحضور لا يكون عذراً ا . وظاهر قوله «أو سفره» أنه يجوز بمجرد سفر الأصل بأن يجاوز بيوت مصره قاصداً ثلاثة أيام ولياليها وإن لم يسافر ثلاثاً، وظاهر كلام المشايخ أنه لا بد من غيبة الأصل ثلاثة أيام ولياليها كما أفصح به في الخانية .
His statement: (And no) testimony for the secondary except with the death of his primary, or his illness, or his travel, because its permissibility is due to need, and it is resorted to at the inability of the primary, and by these things inability is realized. And we only considered travel because inability after the distance and duration of travel is far in ruling, such that many rulings are based on it. So likewise from this ruling. And from Abu Yusuf: If the primary is in a place such that if he went out to perform the testimony he could not return home in time for his rights of people. They said: The first is better and it is the apparent narration as in al-Hawi, and the second is more convenient and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth and many shaykhs adopted it. And Fakhr al-Islam said: It is good. And in al-Sirajiyyah: According to it, it is permissible however it may be, such that it is narrated from him that if the primary is in one corner of the mosque, and the secondary testifies on his testimony in another corner of that mosque, their testimony is accepted. And the author's statement indicates that the sultan and the amir are not allowed to have their testimony transmitted in the city, and that is in al-Qunyah. And the apparent meaning of his statement is restriction, but it is not like that, for it is explicitly stated in al-Qunyah that if the primary is a veiled woman who does not mix with men, it is permissible to have her testimony transmitted, even if she goes out for a need or to the bathhouse. End quote. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the primary witness is imprisoned in the city and he instructs someone to bear witness on his testimony, is it permissible for the secondary to testify on his testimony? And if he testifies before the judge, will he judge by it? He said in al-Dhakhirah: The shaykhs of our time differed. He said: The word of the scholar and upright is accepted, and the word of the oppressor and ignorant is not, except the ignorant upright if he purports to interpret it is accepted, otherwise not. And there is no doubt that the knowledge of the judges of our land is not even a doubt, let alone a proof, except in the book of the judge out of necessity. And in al-Tahdhib, its permissibility was absolute regarding the imprisonment of the primary, and he restricted the secondary's testimony i.e. before the judge because the time of undertaking does not require an excuse for the primary, as in Khizanat al-Muftin. And it is permissible to have testimony transmitted on his own testimony even if there is no excuse for the primary, such that if an excuse of illness, travel, or death befalls them, the secondary testifies. End quote. And in his illness, he made it absolute, and in al-Hidayah it was restricted to the condition that he cannot attend the judge's court. And in Sharh al-Majma' by the author: An illness that does not prevent attendance is not an excuse. End quote. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'or his travel' is that it is permissible simply by the travel of the primary, that he passes the houses of his city intending three days and their nights, even if he does not travel three days. And the apparent meaning of the statements of the shaykhs is that the absence of the primary must be for three days and their nights, as clarified in al-Khaniyyah.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the three excuses that permit secondary testimony: death, illness, and travel of the primary witness. The underlying rationale is necessity and the primary's inability to testify directly. The author details various opinions, particularly on travel. According to Abu Yusuf, travel is an excuse if the primary cannot return home the same day to attend to his rights. Others, including Abu al-Layth and many shaykhs, take a more lenient view, allowing secondary testimony even for short distances like moving within a mosque. There is also discussion about imprisonment: if the primary is in a prison from which he cannot be released to testify, secondary testimony is allowed. The question of illness is clarified: only an illness that prevents attendance at the judge's court qualifies. For travel, the dominant view requires absence of at least three days and nights, though some consider passing the city limits with intention of a three-day journey sufficient. The passage also addresses special cases like veiled women and rulers, indicating flexibility based on the primary's circumstances.

Key Terms
السفر (al-safar): Travel that excuses the primary witness from testifying directly; defined as absence of three days and nights or more.
العذر (al-'udhr): Excuse such as death, illness, or travel that prevents the primary witness from testifying directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One day
B) Three days and nights
C) Seven days
D) Any length defined by the judge

Key Takeaway
The dominant Hanafi position requires the primary witness to be absent for three days and nights for travel to excuse secondary testimony; this is the mufta bihi, though a lenient view exists.

Secondary Witness's Knowledge of Primary's Uprightness
Ruling on secondary witnesses vouching for primary's 'adalah and dispute when they lack knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the secondary witness's knowledge of the primary's 'adalah and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The secondary witness transmits testimony; his knowledge of the primary's uprightness is not required according to Abu Yusuf, the relied-upon view.

This lesson examines a key procedural question in shahadat: must a secondary witness know that the primary witness is upright? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, with Abu Yusuf's view prevailing. Understanding this helps clarify the roles of transmission and verification in testimony.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the legal question: Is it permissible for a secondary witness to testify without knowing the uprightness of the primary witness? The matn and commentary present the intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds that the secondary witness only transmits (naql); the judge investigates 'adalah. The proof: the secondary's duty is transmission, not modification, and 'adalah may be hidden from him.
3
Identify Muhammad's position and proof
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that testimony is invalid without 'adalah; if the secondary does not know the primary's 'adalah, he has not transmitted a valid testimony, so it is rejected.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Yusuf's response: the judge can later verify 'adalah, similar to when primary witnesses themselves attend. The transmission itself does not require knowledge of 'adalah.
5
Determine the tarjih and thamarah
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Yusuf's view, as stated in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi. Practically, this means more secondary testimonies are accepted, easing evidence collection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن عدلهم الفروع (صح) أي قبل تعديلهم لأنهم . من أهله. وفي الصغرى : وهو ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح لأن الفرع نائب ناقل عبارة الأصل إلى مجلس القاضي فبالنقل ينتهي حكم النيابة فيصير أجنبياً فيصح تعديله ا هـ . والمراد أن الفروع معروفون بالعدالة عند القاضي فعدلوا الأصول وإن لم يعرفهم بها فلا بد من تعديلهم وتعديل أصولهم. وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أن أحد الشاهدين لو عدل صاحبه وهو معروف بالعدالة عند القاضي فإنه يجوز لأن العدل لا يتهم بمثله واختاره في الهداية ونقل فيه قولين في النهاية . والحاصل كما في الخانية أن القاضي إن عرف الأصول والفروع بالعدالة قضى بشهادتهم، وإن عرف أحدهما دون الآخر سأل عمن لم يعرفه، وإذا شهد الفروع على شهادة أصل فردت شهادته لفسق الأصل لا تقبل شهادة أحدهما بعد ذلك اهـ . قوله: (وإلا عدلوا) أي إن لم يعد لهم الفروع ولم يعرفهم القاضي بالعدالة سأل عنهم وهذا عند أبي يوسف. وقال محمد: لا تقبل لأنه لا شهادة إلا بالعدالة فإذا لم يعرفوها لم ينقلوا الشهادة فلا تقبل. ولأبي يوسف أن الواجب عليهم النقل دون التعديل لأنه قد يخفى عليهم، وإذا نقلوا يتعرف القاضي العدالة كما إذا حضروا بأنفسهم وشهدوا كذلك في الهداية والكافي، وظاهره أنه يجوز للفرع التحمل والأداء وإن لم يعرف عدالة الأصل. وفي خزانة المفتين : الفرع إذا لم يعرف الأصل
His statement: (If the secondary witnesses declares the primaries upright, it is valid) i.e. their modification is accepted because they are among its people. And in al-Sughra: It is the apparent narration and it is correct because the secondary is a deputy, transmitting the statement of the primary to the judge's court; by transmission, the rule of deputyship ends, so he becomes a stranger, so his modification is valid. End quote. The meaning is that the secondary witnesses are known for uprightness to the judge, so they modify the primaries; if they do not know them by uprightness, it is necessary for them to modify and modify their primaries. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated that if one of two witnesses modifies his companion while he is known for uprightness to the judge, it is permissible because an upright person is not suspected of his like. And he chose this in al-Hidayah and narrated two statements in al-Nihayah. The summary, as in al-Khaniyyah, is that if the judge knows the primaries and secondaries for uprightness, he judges by their testimony; if he knows one but not the other, he asks about the one he does not know; and if the secondary witnesses testify on the testimony of a primary and his testimony is rejected due to the primary's transgression, the testimony of one of them afterwards is not accepted. End quote. His statement: (Otherwise, they modify them) i.e. if the secondary witnesses do not declare them upright and the judge does not know them for uprightness, he asks about them. This is according to Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: It is not accepted because there is no testimony except with uprightness; if they do not know it, they have not transmitted the testimony, so it is not accepted. And for Abu Yusuf, what is obligatory upon them is transmission, not modification, because it may be hidden from them, and when they transmit, the judge investigates uprightness, just as if they themselves attended and testified. Similarly in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi, and its apparent meaning is that it is permissible for the secondary to undertake and perform testimony even if he does not know the uprightness of the primary. And in Khizanat al-Muftin: If the secondary does not know the primary...
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of the secondary witnesses' knowledge of the primary witness's uprightness ('adalah). The matn states that if the secondary witnesses declare the primaries upright (i.e., vouch for their 'adalah), it is accepted. The reason is that the secondary is a deputy transferring testimony; after transmission, he becomes a stranger and can validly testify to the primary's uprightness. However, differences arise when the secondary does not know the primary's 'adalah. According to Abu Yusuf, the secondary is only required to transmit the testimony; the judge then investigates the primary's uprightness. Muhammad disagrees, arguing that without knowledge of uprightness, the secondary cannot validly transmit because testimony presupposes uprightness. The relied-upon position, as in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi, is Abu Yusuf's view, allowing the secondary to testify even without knowing the primary's 'adalah, leaving verification to the judge. The passage also discusses the scenario where one secondary witness modifies the other: if one is known to be upright, his modification of his companion is accepted.

Key Terms
تعديل (ta'dil): Declaring a witness to be upright ('adl); modification.
عدالة ('adalah): Uprightness; a quality required for a witness's testimony to be accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what should a judge do if secondary witnesses testify without knowing the primary's uprightness?
A) Reject the testimony immediately
B) Accept the testimony and then investigate the primary's uprightness
C) Ask the secondary witnesses to bring proof of the primary's uprightness
D) Summon the primary witness to testify directly

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the secondary witness's lack of knowledge about the primary's uprightness does not invalidate the testimony; the judge investigates, per the relied-upon view of Abu Yusuf.

Branch Witnesses and the Statement 'لا نخبرك': An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains three scenarios of branch witnesses' statements and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the second scenario.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for branch witnesses by distinguishing the three scenarios and evaluating the positions in the dispute over 'لا نخبرك'.

Core Idea
When branch witnesses say 'لا نخبرك', the Hanafi school is split: the popular view treats it as a defect; al-Halawani and Abu Yusuf accept it as hesitation.

In Hanafi testimony law, branch witnesses (الفروع) report the testimony of original witnesses (الأصول). The judge may ask the branch about the original's justice. What the branch says in response determines whether their testimony is accepted. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains three scenarios, with a detailed intra-madhhab dispute on the second scenario where the branch says 'we do not inform you'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three statements the branch witnesses might make to the judge: silence, 'لا نخبرك', and explicit accusation.
2
Focus on the second scenario
Examine the disagreement between the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) as recorded in al-Khaniyah regarding 'لا نخبرك'.
Al-Khassaf holds non-acceptance as zahir al-riwaya; al-Halawani advocates acceptance.
3
Analyze the qiyas
Understand al-Khassaf's analogy: if explicit accusation ('إنا نتهمه') is a defect, then 'لا نخبرك' is also a defect because it implies lack of knowledge or suspicion.
The illa is the indication of a defect.
4
Consider the counterargument
Abu Yusuf and al-Halawani argue that 'لا نخبرك' is ambiguous; it could be mere hesitation. Since doubt does not establish a defect, the testimony should be accepted.
This reflects the principle that certainty is required for defect (jarh).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a judge following the popular view will reject the branch testimony, while one following al-Halawani will accept it and investigate the original's justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعدالة ولا غيرها فهو مسيء في الشهادة على شهادته بتركه الاحتياط ا هـ . وقالوا : الاساءة أفحش من الكراهة . وقوله وإلا صادق بصور: الأولى أن يسكتوا وهو المراد هنا كما أفصح به في الهداية الثانية أن يقول الفروع للقاضي بعد السؤال لا نخبرك فجعله في الخانية على الخلاف بين الشيخين، فقولهما لا نخبرك بمنزلة قولهما لا نعرف الأصل أعدل أم لا. وذكر الخصاف أن عدم القبول جواب ظاهر الرواية كما ذكره القاضي الإمام علي السغدي في شرح أدب القاضي، وذكر الحلواني أن القاضي يقبل شهادتهما ويسأل عن الأصل وهو الصحيح لأن الأصل بقي مستوراً. ووجه المشهور أن قولهما لا تخبرك للأصول واستشهد جرح الخصاف فقال : ألا ترى أنهما لو شهدا عند القاضي على شهادة رجل وقالا للقاضي إنا نتهمه في الشهادة لم يقبل القاضي شهادتهما على شهادته فكذا إذا قال لا نخبرك. ووجه رواية أبي يوسف أن هذا يحتمل أن يكون جرحاً ويحتمل أن يكون توقفاً فلا يثبت الجرح بالشك؛ كذا في الفتاوى الصغرى الثالثة أن يقول الفرع للقاضي إنا نتهمه في الشهادة فإن القاضي لا يقبله ؛ كذا في الخانية وهو شاهد الخصاف.
With justice or other than it, he is sinful in testimony upon his testimony by leaving caution. They said: wrongdoing is more intense than dislike. And his statement: 'otherwise it applies to images: first, that they remain silent and that is intended here as clarified in al-Hidayah; second, that the branch witnesses say to the judge after questioning: 'we do not inform you' – so he made it in al-Khaniyah on the disagreement between the two shaykhs. Their statement 'we do not inform you' is equivalent to their statement 'we do not know whether the original is just or not'. And al-Khassaf mentioned that non-acceptance is the answer of the apparent transmission, as mentioned by Judge Imam Ali al-Sughdi in Sharh Adab al-Qadi. And al-Halawani mentioned that the judge accepts their testimony and asks about the original, and it is correct because the original remains hidden. And the well-known view is that their statement 'we do not inform you' for the originals (is a defect); and al-Khassaf cited the proof of defect saying: 'Do you not see that if they testified before the judge on the testimony of a man and said to the judge: we accuse him in the testimony, the judge would not accept their testimony on his testimony; similarly if they say: we do not inform you.' And the view of the narration of Abu Yusuf is that this could be a defect and could be hesitation, so the defect is not established by doubt; as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. Third: that the branch says to the judge: 'we accuse him in the testimony', then the judge does not accept it; as in al-Khaniyah and it is the proof of al-Khassaf.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage discusses three scenarios regarding what branch witnesses say to the judge and the legal effect on their testimony. The first scenario is that they remain silent; this is the intended meaning according to the Hidayah, and it is permissible but not ideal. The second scenario is that they say 'we do not inform you' regarding the justice of the original witnesses. The author of al-Khaniyah records a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on this. According to al-Khassaf, the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is that such a statement is treated as a defect and the branch testimony is not accepted. Al-Halawani, however, considers it acceptable because the original's condition remains unknown. The popular view (mashhur) analogizes this to an explicit accusation ('we accuse him'), which clearly disqualifies. Abu Yusuf's view is that the statement is ambiguous—it could be a defect or mere hesitation—and since doubt does not establish a defect, the testimony is accepted. The third scenario is an explicit accusation by the branch, which is clearly a defect and not accepted. The author then notes that this analogy is the proof of al-Khassaf.

Key Terms
الفرع (al-far'): The branch witness, i.e., the one who testifies on the testimony of the original witness.
الأصل (al-asl): The original witness, i.e., the one who directly witnessed the event and later his testimony is reported by the branch.
الجرح (al-jarh): Impugning or discrediting the witness; a defect that renders testimony unacceptable.
التوقف (al-tawaqquf): Hesitation or suspension of judgment; not a clear defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khassaf, what is the ruling when branch witnesses say 'لا نخبرك' regarding the original's justice?
A) The testimony is accepted because they may be hesitant.
B) The testimony is not accepted, and this is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwaya).
C) The judge must investigate the original's justice.
D) The branch witnesses are considered unreliable and are disqualified.

Key Takeaway
When branch witnesses express uncertainty about the original's justice, the Hanafi school is divided: the popular view treats it as a defect, while others consider it mere hesitation.

Invalidation of Branch Testimony: Understanding the Original's Denial
Critical refinement of the matn's wording on branch testimony invalidation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why branch testimony is invalid when the original denies the testimony, and distinguish between denial of testimony and denial of tashheed in Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Branch testimony requires tamhil; denial of testimony implies denial of tamhil and thus invalidates.

In Hanafi law, testimony on testimony (shahada 'ala shahada) is valid only when the original witnesses formally appoint the branch witnesses through tashheed. The matn states that branch testimony is invalidated by the original's denial of 'the testimony'. But does this mean denial of the act of testifying or denial of the tashheed? This passage clarifies that both scenarios invalidate the branch testimony, and a careful reading of the furu' shows the underlying condition of tamhil is absent in both cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
State the ruling: branch testimony (shahadat al-furu') is invalid (batil) if the original witnesses deny the testimony. Identify the condition of tamhil (the burden of transmitting testimony) as the basis: tamhil is established by the original's tashheed, and denial of testimony negates tamhil.
2
Distinguish Between Denial of Testimony and Denial of Tashheed
Recognize that 'denial of testimony' (إنكار الشهادة) can be interpreted as outright denial that the original ever testified, or as denial of the tashheed (appointing the branch). Both are distinct, but the Hanafi jurists explain that outright denial is a kinayah (metaphor) that includes denial of tashheed and is even more emphatic.
Al-Zayla'i is defended for not mistakenly conflating the two, but rather for covering both scenarios.
3
Apply the Ruling to Two Scenarios
Consider scenario 1: Original says 'I did not give tashheed' (denial of ishhad). Scenario 2: Original says 'I have no testimony in this case' (denial of testimony). In both, the branch testimony is invalid because tamhil is not established. The matn's wording covers scenario 2, which necessarily implies scenario 1.
Quoting al-Jawhara: If original witnesses deny having testified, branch testimony is rejected.
4
Evaluate the Interpretation of al-Zayla'i
Al-Zayla'i interpreted the matn's 'denial of testimony' as 'denial of tashheed.' Critics argued this conflates two terms, but Juy Zadeh defends him, showing that the interpretation is not a literal substitution but a recognition that the ruling's operative cause (tahmil) fails in both cases. The matn is not restricted to one scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

منفعة له من حيث تنفيذ القاضي قوله على موجب ما يشهد غاية ما أنه يرد به قلنا العدل لا يتهم بمثل ما ذكرت من الشبهة فإن مثلها ثابت في شهادة نفسه فإنها تتضمن القضاء بها، فكما أن الشرع لم يعتبر مع عدالته ذلك مانعًا كذا ما نحن فيه وإلا لا نسد باب الشهادة اهـ . ملخصًا من النهاية والفتح وبه ظهر أن الضمير ليس عائدًا للعدل كما توهمه بعضهم قوله : (الإساءة أفحش من الكراهة أقول: هكذا ذكره في شرحه على المنار بأن قالوا الخ هكذا فسر الزيلعي كلام المصنف قال في الدرر أقول: قد وقعت العبارة في الهداية وشروحه وسائر المعتبرات هكذا وإن أنكر شهود الأصل الشهادة موافقة لما في الكافي، ولا يخفى على أحد مغايرة الإشهاد للشهادة فكيف يصح تفسيرها به؟ ولعل منشأ غلطه قولهم لأن التحميل لم يثبت للتعارض فإن معنى التحميل هو الإشهاد وخفي عليه أن التحميل لا يثبت أيضًا إذا أنكر أصل الشهادة بل هذا أبلغ من إنكار الإشهاد لأنه كناية وهي أبلغ من التصريح اهـ. وفي الشرنبلالية قال الفاضل المرحوم جوي زاده :أقول : لم يرد الزيلعي تفسير لفظ الشهادة بالإشهاد بل أراد أن مدار بطلان شهادة الفرع على إنكار الأصل للإشهاد حتى يبطل، ولو قال لي شهادة على هذه الحادثة لكن لم أشهد والمذكور في المتن تصور المسألة في صورة من صورتي إنكار الإشهاد وهي صورة إنكار الشهادة رأسًا إذ لا شك في فوات الإشهاد في هذه الصورة أيضًا، وأنه ليس المراد بما في صورة إنكار الشهادة رأسًا وصورة الإقرار بها وإنكار الإشهاد تحققت أن كون التركيب أبلغ في الإنكار غير مراد اهـ ما قاله الفاضل، وصورة إنكار الشهادة ما قاله في الجوهرة : وإن أنكر شهود الأصل الشهادة لم تقبل What we preceded from his statement: 'and the testimony of branch witnesses is invalidated by the original's denial of the testimony, i.e., of the tashheed, by their saying such'. How can his statement be acceptable in itself even if the testimony of his companion is rejected? So there is no accusation. And his statement 'ghayat al-usr' i.e., accused because in his modification there is benefit for him in terms of executing the judge's statement according to what he witnesses, the utmost is that he rejects it. We said: The just person is not accused by such suspicion, for its like exists in his own testimony, for it entails judgment by it. Just as the Law did not consider that an obstacle despite his justice, likewise in our case. Otherwise we would close the door of testimony. Summarized from al-Nihayah and al-Fath, and by this it appears that the pronoun is not returning to the just as some imagined. His statement: 'wrongdoing is more intense than dislike' I say: This is what he mentioned in his commentary on al-Manar, but what I saw in al-Taqrir sharh usul al-Bazdawi and al-Tahqiq sharh al-Iksikthi and others is that wrongdoing is lesser than dislike. Perhaps whoever said lesser meant prohibitive dislike, and whoever said more intense meant non-prohibitive. His statement: 'i.e., the tashheed by their saying such' – thus al-Zayla'i interpreted the wording of the author. He said in al-Durar: I say: The phrase in al-Hidayah and its commentaries and all reliable works is thus: 'even if the original witnesses deny the testimony' in agreement with what is in al-Kafi. It is not hidden from anyone the difference between tashheed and testimony, so how can this interpretation be correct? Perhaps the origin of his mistake is their statement: 'because the tamhil is not established due to conflict', for the meaning of tamhil is tashheed, and it was hidden from him that tamhil also is not established if the original denies the testimony, rather this is more potent than denial of tashheed because it is a metaphor, and it is more potent than explicit statement. In al-Sharnaballaliya, the virtuous deceased Juy Zadeh said: I say: Al-Zayla'i did not intend to interpret the word 'testimony' as 'tashheed' but rather he intended that the basis of invalidation of branch testimony is the original's denial of tashheed until it becomes invalid. Even if he says: I have testimony about this incident but I did not give tashheed, and what is mentioned in the text is the conception of the case in one of the two images of denial of tashheed, which is the image of outright denial of testimony, for there is no doubt about the omission of tashheed in this image as well. And it is not intended by the text to restrict invalidation to the image of denial of testimony. And it was not hidden from him that tamhil is also not established with denial of the original testimony; rather it would have been hidden from him had he imagined that the branch testimony is not invalidated then, and far be it from him. Now that you know that invalidation covers both the image of outright denial of testimony and the image of acknowledging it while denying tashheed, it becomes certain that the construction being more potent in denial is not intended. End of the virtuous one's words. And the image of denial of testimony is what is said in al-Jawhara: If the original witnesses deny the testimony, the branch testimony is not accepted, such as if they said: we have no testimony in this incident and then they died or disappeared, then the branch came testifying on their testimony in this incident and said: we did not witness the branch on our testimony, then the branch testimony is not accepted because the tamhil is not established, and it is a condition.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage critically examines the ruling in the matn: 'Shahadat al-furu' is invalidated by the original's denial of the testimony (shahada).' The commentator clarifies that 'denial of testimony' here means denial of tashheed (the act of appointing the branch as witnesses). The proof given is that the condition for branch testimony (tahlil/tahmil) is not established due to the conflict between the original's denial and the branch's claim. A long discussion ensues about al-Zayla'i's interpretation: some critics, like the author of al-Durar, thought al-Zayla'i mistakenly explained 'shahada' as 'tashheed', but al-Sharnaballali's commentator Juy Zadeh defends al-Zayla'i, arguing that the matn actually covers both cases: denial of testimony outright (which necessarily implies denial of tashheed) and acknowledgment of the testimony but denial of tashheed. Thus, the invalidation is general. The passage ends by quoting al-Jawhara: if the original witnesses deny having testified, the branch testimony is invalid because the tamhil (the burden of transmitting testimony) is not established.

Key Terms
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): The act of making witnesses; the original witnesses formally stating that they appoint the branch to testify on their behalf.
التحميل (al-tahmil): The burden of transmitting testimony; the assurance that the original witnesses have entrusted the branch to testify.
الكناية (al-kinayah): A figurative or indirect expression; here, denial of testimony is a kind of metaphor for denial of tashheed, which is more emphatic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct interpretation, what happens to branch testimony if the original witnesses deny having ever testified (إنكار الشهادة)?
A) It remains valid because they only denied the testimony, not the tashheed.
B) It becomes invalid because denial of testimony implies denial of tashheed.
C) It depends on whether the branch witnesses confirm the tashheed.
D) The judge must investigate the truth of the denial.

Key Takeaway
Branch testimony is invalid when the original denies the testimony, because denial of testimony is a kinayah that implies denial of tashheed, and thus the condition of tamhil is absent.

Invalidators of Tashheed: Prohibition, Loss of Eligibility, and Presence of Original Witnesses
Lists three invalidators of tashheed and discusses a subsequent dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three invalidators of tashheed in Hanafi law and explain the effect of each on the validity of branch testimony.

Core Idea
The tashheed is voided by the original's prohibition, loss of eligibility, or presence before judgment—each with a distinct legal consequence.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq enumerates three scenarios that invalidate or suspend the authority of a branch testimony. Understanding these invalidators is crucial for anyone involved in testimony upon testimony, as they define the limits and exceptions of secondary testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalidators
List each invalidator: (1) prohibition (nahy) by the original witnesses, (2) loss of eligibility (khuruj al-asl 'an al-ahliyyah) of the originals, and (3) presence (hudur) of the originals before the judge before judgment.
2
Examine the ruling on prohibition
Note that the majority view (عامة المشايخ) holds that the original's explicit prohibition invalidates the tashheed. However, some scholars disagree. The text also distinguishes testimony from narration (riwaya): in narration, prohibition does not prevent the branch from narrating.
The preferred view is that prohibition is effective for testimony.
3
Examine loss of eligibility
Learn that if the original witnesses become mute, sinful, blind, apostate, or insane, they lose eligibility for testimony, and the branch testimony becomes impermissible. This is based on a quote from Khizanat al-Muftin.
Eligibility must exist at the time of tashheed and at the time of branch testimony.
4
Examine presence before judgment
Understand that if the originals appear before the judge before judgment is passed, the branch testimony is not acted upon (لا يقضى). However, this does not permanently invalidate the tashheed; if the originals disappear again, the branch testimony may be used.
This is analogous to a letter from one judge to another when the plaintiff appears in person.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on overturning judgment
Consider the scenario: judgment has already been passed based on branch testimony, then the originals appear. There is a difference of opinion: some say the judgment is based on the originals' testimony, so it is overturned; others say it is based on the branch testimony, so it stands. The author finds this disagreement remarkable.
The text does not resolve this ikhtilaf, leaving it as an unsettled point.

قوله : (صح. النهي عند عامة المشايخ) يعني فلو غاب الأصول ليس لهم أن يشهدوا على شهادتهم لأن الإشهاد قد بطل بنهيهم فلا ينافي ما سيأتي أنه إذا حضر الأصول قبل القضاء لا يقضى بشهادة الفروع فلا يقال لا حاجة إلى النهي هنا تأمل قوله : (وظاهر قوله لا يقضى الخ على هذا ما كان ينبغي عده الحضور من مبطلات الإشهاد . الخلاصة كتاب الشهادات باب الشهادة على الشهادة على شهادتنا فماتوا وغابوا ثم شهد الفروع لم تقبل لأن التحميل لم يثبت للتعارض بين الخبرين وهو شرط . قيد بالإنكار لأنهم لو سئلوا فسكتوا لم يبطل الإشهاد؛ كذا في الخلاصة. وفيها معزواً إلى الجامع الكبير : إذا شهدا على شهادة رجلين أنه أعتق عبده ولم يقض بشهادتهما حتى حضر الأصلان ونهيا الفروع عن الشهادة صح النهي عند عامة المشايخ. وقال بعضهم : لا يصح. والأول أظهر ا هـ . وأشار المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى إلى أن المروي عنه إذا أنكر الرواية بطلت الرواية؛ كذا في وهي مسألة الأصول واستشكل في فتح القدير عمل المشايخ بالمسائل التي أنكرها أبو يوسف على محمد حين عرض عليه الجامع الصغير وقدمناه الصلاة وذكرناه في شرح المنار وفي الخلاصة : لو نهاه عن الرواية وسعه الرواية عنه فعلى هذا يفرق بين الشهادة والرواية على قول العامة. ومما يبطل الإشهاد خروج الأصل عن أهلية الشهادة لما في خزانة المفتين : وإذا خرس الأصلان أو فسقا أو عميا وارتدا أو جنا لم تجز شهادة الفروع ا هـ . ومما يبطله أيضاً حضور الأصل قبل القضاء. قال في الخانية : ولو أن فروعاً شهدوا على شهادة الأصول ثم حضر الأصول قبل القضاء لا يقضى بشهادة الفروع وظاهر قوله «لا يقضى دون أن يقول بطل الإشهاد أن الأصول لو غابوا بعد ذلك قضى بشهادتهم. وذكر في كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي إذا كتب للمدعي كتاباً ثم حضر بلد المكتوب إليه قبل أن يقضي المكتوب إليه بكتابه لا يقضى بكتابه كما لو حضر شاهد الأصل وفي اليتمية سئل الخجندي عن قاض قضى لرجل بملك الأرض بشهادة الفروع ثم جاء الأصول هل يبطل الفروع ؟ فقال : هذا مختلف بين أصحابنا، فمن قال إن القضاء يقع بشهادة الأصول يبطل، ومن قال القضاء يقع بشهادة الفروع لا يبطل ا هـ . وهذا الاختلاف عجيب
His statement: 'the prohibition is valid according to the generality of scholars' meaning if the original witnesses disappeared, they (the branch) may not testify on their testimony because the tashheed has been invalidated by their prohibition. This does not contradict what will come that if the original witnesses appear before judgment, the branch testimony is not acted upon; so it is not said that there is no need for prohibition here. Ponder. His statement: 'and the apparent meaning of his statement 'it is not judged', based on this, it should not have considered presence as among the invalidators of tashheed. Al-Khulasah: Book of Testimonies, Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony: ...upon our testimony, they died and disappeared, then the branch testified, it was not accepted because the tamhil was not established due to conflict between the two reports, and it is a condition. It is restricted to denial because if they were asked and remained silent, the tashheed is not invalidated; as in al-Khulasah. In it, attributed to al-Jami' al-Kabir: If two witnessed on the testimony of two men that he freed his slave and the case was not judged until the original witnesses appeared and forbade the branch from testifying, the prohibition is valid according to the generality of scholars. Some said: it is not valid. The first is more apparent. The author indicated that what is narrated from him (Abu Hanifa) is that if he denies the narration, the narration is invalidated; as in the principles. And it is problematic in Fath al-Qadir the practice of scholars with the issues that Abu Yusuf denied to Muhammad when he presented al-Jami' al-Saghir to him, and we have presented it in the section of prayer and mentioned it in Sharh al-Manar. In al-Khulasah: If he forbade him from narrating, it is permissible for him to narrate from him; thus there is a distinction between testimony and narration according to the general statement. Among what invalidates tashheed is the original's exit from eligibility for testimony, as in Khizanat al-Muftin: If the two originals become mute, or become sinful, or become blind, or apostatize, or become insane, the branch testimony is not permitted. Among what also invalidates it is the presence of the original before judgment. He said in al-Khaniyah: If branch witnesses testified on the testimony of the originals, then the originals appeared before judgment, the branch testimony is not acted upon. The apparent meaning of his statement 'it is not acted upon' without saying 'the tashheed is invalidated' is that if the originals disappear afterward, their testimony would be acted upon. And it is mentioned in Kitab al-Qadi ila al-Qadi: If he wrote a letter for the plaintiff, then the person to whom the letter was sent appeared in the town of the addressee before the addressee judged by his letter, the letter is not acted upon, just as if the original witness appeared. In al-Yatimiya, al-Khujandi was asked about a judge who judged for a man regarding ownership of land based on branch testimony, then the originals came: does it invalidate the branch? He said: This is disputed among our companions. Some say the judgment is based on the originals' testimony, so it invalidates; others say the judgment is based on the branch testimony, so it does not invalidate. This difference is strange.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage discusses several factors that invalidate the tashheed (and consequently branch testimony). First, the original witnesses' explicit prohibition (nahy) of the branch from testifying: the consensus of the majority of scholars is that this prohibition is effective, invalidating the tashheed. However, some scholars disagree, but the first view is considered more apparent. The author notes a distinction between testimony and narration (riwaya): in hadith narration, if a scholar forbids his student from narrating, the student may still narrate, but in testimony the prohibition is effective. Second, loss of the original's eligibility for testimony, such as becoming mute, sinful, blind, apostate, or insane, invalidates the tashheed. This is illustrated by a quotation from Khizanat al-Muftin. Third, the presence of the original witnesses before the judge before judgment effectively suspends the branch testimony. The text clarifies that this does not completely invalidate the tashheed; if the originals disappear again, the branch testimony may be acted upon. An analogy is drawn with a judge's written correspondence. Finally, a question is raised about a judgment already passed: if judgment was based on branch testimony and later the originals appear, is the judgment overturned? There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars, with some saying it is overturned and others not. The author finds this disagreement remarkable.

Key Terms
النهي (al-nahy): The original witnesses forbidding the branch from testifying, which invalidates the tashheed.
خروج الأصل عن الأهلية (khuruj al-asl 'an al-ahliyyah): The original witness loses the legal capacity to testify (e.g., by apostasy, blindness, muteness, etc.), which invalidates the branch testimony.
حضور الأصل (hudur al-asl): The original witnesses appearing before the judge before the judgment is passed; this prevents acting on branch testimony but does not completely invalidate the tashheed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the tashheed if the original witnesses become apostates after appointing the branch?
A) The tashheed remains valid because it occurred before apostasy.
B) The tashheed is invalidated and branch testimony is not permitted.
C) The branch may still testify but must inform the judge of the apostasy.
D) It depends on whether the apostasy is proven by evidence.

Key Takeaway
Three things can void or suspend the effectiveness of a tashheed: the original's prohibition, loss of eligibility, and presence before judgment—with the first two being permanent and the last temporary.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Invalidation of Secondary Testimony and Identification Requirements
Rulings on invalidity of secondary testimony and identification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid secondary testimony and identify which factors invalidate it, using Hanafi principles.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony collapses if originals deny, prohibit, or lose eligibility.

Secondary testimony (شهادة الفروع) is a concession that eases proof, but it rests on fragile foundations. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq shows that the original witnesses' denial, their explicit prohibition, or their loss of legal capacity all destroy the secondary testimony. The author also emphasizes that accurate identification of parties is essential from the moment of certification (الإشهاد).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition for secondary testimony
The secondary testimony is accepted only if the assignment (التحميل) is proven. This means the originals must have formally charged the secondaries to bear witness on their behalf.
The passage states: 'لأن التحميل لم يثبت'
2
Recognise the invalidators: denial, prohibition, loss of eligibility
The text lists three main invalidators: (1) the originals deny having testified, (2) the originals forbid the secondaries, (3) the originals lose eligibility (become blind, mute, sinful, apostate, insane). Also, the originals' presence before judgment prevents passing judgment on secondary testimony.
Each invalidator is derived from specific fiqh scenarios.
3
Analyse the ikhtilaf on prohibition's effect
The majority of Hanafi mashayikh hold that the prohibition is valid and nullifies the certification. Some said it is not valid. The tarjih favours the majority view, analogising to hadith narration.
قياساً على الرواية: إذا أنكر المروي عنه الرواية بطلت
4
Apply the identification requirement in certification
When certifying testimony, the parties must be identified to the fullest extent possible—lineage, tribe, etc. The assembly of certification is like the assembly of judgment. If the defendant denies being the named person, the plaintiff must prove identity; if the defendant admits the name but claims a namesake, the defendant must prove that.
الإعلام بأقصى ما يمكن

الإشهاد وهي صورة إنكار الشهادة رأساً إذ لا شك في فوات الإشهاد في هذه الصورة أيضاً، وأنه ليس المراد بما في المتن حصر البطلان بصورة إنكار الشهادة ولم يخف عليه أن التحميل لا يثبت أيضاً مع إنكار أصل الشهادة، وإنما يكون خافياً عليه لو توهم عدم بطلان شهادة الفرع حينئذ وحاشاه عن ذلك. وإذ قد عرفت أن البطلان يعم صورة إنكار الشهادة رأساً وصورة الإقرار بها وإنكار الإشهاد تحققت أن كون التركيب أبلغ في الإنكار غير مراد اهـ ما قاله الفاضل، وصورة إنكار الشهادة ما قاله في الجوهرة : وإن أنكر شهود الأصل الشهادة لم تقبل شهادة الفروع بأن قالوا ليس لنا شهادة في هذه الحادثة وغابوا أو ماتوا، ثم جاء الفروع يشهدون على شهادتهم في هذه الحادثة وقالوا لم نشهد الفروع على شهادتنا، فإن شهادة الفروع لم تقبل لأن التحميل لم يثبت وهو شرط اهـ قوله : (صح. النهي عند عامة المشايخ) يعني فلو غاب الأصول ليس لهم أن يشهدوا على شهادتهم لأن الإشهاد قد بطل بنهيهم فلا ينافي ما سيأتي أنه إذا حضر الأصول قبل القضاء لا يقضى بشهادة الفروع فلا يقال لا حاجة إلى النهي هنا تأمل قوله : (وظاهر قوله لا يقضي الخ على هذا ما كان ينبغي عده الحضور

قوله : (وكذا كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي) لأنه في معنى الشهادة على الشهادة إلا أن القاضي لكمال ديانته ووفور ولايته ينفرد بالنقل. ولم يذكر المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى جواب المدعى عليه ولا بد منه فإنه إن قال لست أنا فلان بن فلان الفلاني كان البيان على المدعي وأنه أقر أنه فلان بن فلان وادعى الاشتراك في الاسم والنسب كان البيان على المدعى عليه ولذا قال في الخانية : القاضي إذا كتب كتاباً وكتب في كتابه اسم المدعى عليه ونسبه على وجه الكمال فقال المدعى عليه لست أنا فلان بن فلان الفلاني والقاضي المكتوب إليه لا يعرفه يقول القاضي للمدعي أقم البينة أنه فلان بن فلان فإن قال المدعى عليه أنا فلان بن فلان وفي هذا الحي أو الفخذ أو في هذه الحارة أو في هذه البلدة رجل غيري بهذا الاسم يقول له القاضي أثبت ذلك، فإن أثبت ذلك تندفع عنه الخصومة كما لو علم القاضي
فلان
بن
البحر الرائق ج٧/ م ١٤
Book of Testimonies, Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony. 'On our testimony, they died or were absent, then the secondary witnesses testified, it was not accepted because the assignment [of testimony] was not established due to conflict between the two reports, and it is a condition.' It is restricted by denial because if they were asked and remained silent, the certification does not become invalid; likewise in al-Khulasa. In it, attributed to al-Jami' al-Kabir: If two testify on the testimony of two men that he freed his slave, and judgment was not passed on their testimony until the originals came and forbade the secondary witnesses from testifying, the prohibition is valid according to the majority of mashayikh. And some said: it is not valid. The first is more apparent. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated that if the narrator denies the narration, the narration becomes invalid; likewise in [such and such], it is a principle issue. And it is problematic in Fath al-Qadir regarding the practice of the mashayikh on issues that Abu Yusuf denied to Muhammad when he presented al-Jami' al-Saghir to him, and we have presented it in the chapter of prayer and mentioned it in Sharh al-Manar. In al-Khulasa: If he forbade him from narrating, it is permissible for him to narrate from him, so on this basis there is a distinction between testimony and narration according to the general view. Among the things that invalidate the certification is the originals leaving the eligibility for testimony, as in Khizanat al-Muftin: If the originals become mute, or sinful, or blind, or apostate, or insane, the testimony of the secondary witnesses is not permissible. Among the things that also invalidate it is the presence of the originals before judgment. He said in al-Khaniyya: If secondary witnesses testified on the testimony of the originals, then the originals came before judgment, judgment is not passed on the testimony of the secondary witnesses. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'judgment is not passed' without saying 'the certification becomes invalid' is that if the originals were to leave afterward, judgment would be passed on their testimony. It is mentioned in the book of 'Judge to Judge' that if he wrote a letter for the plaintiff, then came to the town of the addressee before the addressee judged by his letter, judgment is not passed by his letter, just as if the original witness came. In al-Yatimiyya, al-Khujandi was asked about a judge who ruled for a man regarding ownership of land by testimony of secondary witnesses, then the originals came: does the secondary [testimony] become invalid? He said: This is disputed among our companions. Some say judgment occurs by the testimony of the originals, so it becomes invalid; some say judgment occurs by the testimony of the secondary, so it does not become invalid. This difference is strange. [The author then discusses the case of denial of testimony itself and the distinction between denial of testimony and denial of certification.] ... His statement: 'The prohibition is valid according to the majority of mashayikh' means, if the originals were absent, they are not allowed to testify on their testimony because the certification has become invalid by their prohibition, so it does not contradict what will come that if the originals come before judgment, judgment is not passed on the testimony of the secondary. So it cannot be said that there is no need for the prohibition here. Consider his statement: 'The apparent meaning of his statement that judgment is not passed...' on this, it was not appropriate to count presence among the invalidators of certification. The text continues with the scenario of testifying on the testimony of two men against a woman identified as 'so-and-so daughter of so-and-so the such-and-such' for one thousand, and the secondary witnesses said they know her but when they brought a woman they said they do not know if she is this one or not. The plaintiff is told to bring two witnesses that she is so-and-so. Similarly, in the case of a judge's letter. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) indicated by his statement 'against so-and-so' etc. that it is a condition in certification to inform to the fullest extent possible. Hence in al-Khaniyya: if a man certifies a man on his testimony, if the one owed and the one owing are present at the certification, his statement 'I testify that this so-and-so acknowledged before me that for so-and-so son of so-and-so this is owed one thousand dirhams' is valid. If they are absent, or one present and the other absent or dead, he should attribute the absent or dead to his father, grandfather, tribe, and whatever he is known by, because the assembly of certification is like the assembly of judgment. Just as in the performance of testimony, informing to the fullest extent possible is a condition in certification. In al-Bazzaziyya: In the divorce of Shaykh al-Islam, he acknowledged that he owes 'so-and-so son of so-and-so the such-and-such' a certain amount, then a man came with this name and claimed it, and he said 'I meant another man by it,' he is believed in qada and the debt is not enforced against him. In Wasiyya of al-Khaniyya: A sick man said to a man, 'I owe you one thousand dirhams,' he gives all the money to the heirs, nothing is withheld. If he said 'I owe Muhammad one thousand,' and Muhammad is unknown, the amount of the debt is withheld. In al-Misbah: 'fulan' without alif and lam is a designation for humans, and with them is a designation for animals; it is said 'I rode the fulana' and 'I milked the fulana.' His statement: 'Similarly, the judge's letter to a judge' because it is in the meaning of testimony upon testimony, except that the judge, due to his complete piety and extensive authority, is unique in transmission. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the defendant's response, but it is necessary. For if he says 'I am not so-and-so son of so-and-so the such-and-such,' the burden of proof is on the plaintiff. And if he acknowledges that he is so-and-so son of so-and-so but claims coincidence in name and lineage, the burden of proof is on the defendant. Hence in al-Khaniyya: If a judge writes a letter and writes the name and lineage of the defendant completely, and the defendant says 'I am not so-and-so,' and the recipient judge does not know him, the judge says to the plaintiff: bring proof that he is so-and-so. If the defendant says 'I am so-and-so, but in this neighborhood or clan or street or town there is another man with this name,' the judge tells him to prove it. If he proves it, the case against him is dismissed, just as if the judge knew.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically the chapter on testimony upon testimony. The author, Ibn Nujaym, expands the rulings regarding the validity of secondary testimony (شهادة الفروع). The passage begins by addressing a scenario where the original witnesses (الأصول) deny having testified, and the secondary witnesses then come to testify. The ruling is that the secondary testimony is not accepted because the assignment (التحميل) was not established—there is a conflict between the statements of the two sets of witnesses. This is conditioned on the original witnesses' explicit denial; if they remained silent when asked, the certification is not invalidated. The author then cites a case from al-Jami' al-Kabir: if originals forbid the secondary witnesses from testifying, that prohibition is valid according to the majority of scholars, though some differed. The relied-upon position is that it is valid, meaning the secondary witnesses can no longer testify. This is then analogized to hadith narration: if a narrator denies his narration, it becomes invalid, though some distinguish between testimony and narration. Next, the passage lists other invalidators of the certification (الإشهاد): the originals losing eligibility for testimony (becoming mute, sinful, blind, apostate, or insane). Also, the presence of the originals before judgment is a cause for not passing judgment on secondary testimony, but the author notes that this merely prevents judgment, not necessarily invalidates the certification entirely—if the originals leave again, perhaps the secondary testimony could still be used? There is a difference of opinion on this among scholars, as mentioned from al-Yatimiyya. The passage then moves to a practical case: secondary witnesses testify that two originals testified against a woman identified as 'so-and-so daughter of so-and-so', but when a woman is presented, the secondary witnesses cannot identify her. The plaintiff must then bring two witnesses to confirm her identity, because the testimony was only about knowledge (معرفة) of identity, not visual identification. This illustrates the principle that in certification, one must provide the fullest possible identification (الإعلام بأقصى ما يمكن). The author cites al-Khaniyya: if both parties are present, simple description suffices; if one is absent, lineage, tribe, etc. are needed. The same applies to judge's letters: the judge must sufficiently identify the parties. Finally, the passage discusses the defendant's response: if he denies being the person named, the plaintiff must prove identity; if he admits the name but claims another man with same name exists, the defendant must prove that there is a namesake. This shows the importance of clear identification in legal proceedings.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The original witness who directly observed the event and whose testimony is transmitted by the secondary witness.
الفرع (al-far'): The secondary witness who testifies on the testimony of the original witness (asl).
الإشهاد (al-ishhad): The act of formally certifying one's testimony before witnesses, i.e., the assignment (tahmil) of testimony.
التحميل (al-tahmil): The assignment of testimony from the original to the secondary witness; the act of charging the secondary to bear witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the original witnesses (asl) lose their eligibility for testimony (e.g., become blind) before judgment, what is the ruling on the testimony of the secondary witnesses (far')?
A) It remains valid because the certification is already complete.
B) It becomes invalid because the asl's eligibility is a condition for the far''s testimony.
C) It is suspended until the asl recovers.
D) The judge has discretion to accept or reject.

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony collapses if the original witnesses deny, prohibit, or lose eligibility — it is not irrevocable.

Shahadat — Testimony

Identifying Absent Persons: Grandfather vs Subtribe
Intra-Hanafi dispute on identification details in judge's letters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on what lineage details are required for identifying an absent person in a judge's letter, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Identifying a person by tribe alone is insufficient; the subtribe or grandfather is necessary to avoid confusion.

When a judge writes to another judge about an absent party, the letter must include enough details to identify that person. But how much lineage is enough? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require the grandfather, while Abu Yusuf accepts the father if the person is well-known. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the role of the subtribe (fakhdh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its purpose
Recognize that this passage deals with ta'rif (identification) in a judge's letter (kitab al-qadi) to another judge. The purpose is to uniquely identify the person so the receiving judge can act on the letter.
2
State the positions of the three imams
Note that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require the grandfather (jadd) in addition to name and father. Abu Yusuf is satisfied with father alone if the person is known by profession or other indication.
The text also discusses that mentioning the subtribe (fakhdh) can substitute for the grandfather.
3
Locate the proofs behind each position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that identification must prevent confusion, and a general tribe name (e.g., Tamimi) is too broad. The grandfather or specific subtribe narrows it down. Abu Yusuf argues that if the person is well-known by his father or profession, that suffices because people are commonly identified that way.
The text does not quote explicit dalil but gives the reasoning (ta'lil).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a letter, if only name and father are mentioned, the receiving judge may reject it according to Imam and Muhammad, but accept it according to Abu Yusuf.
The mufta bihi is that the grandfather is necessary unless the person is universally famous (like Imam Abu Hanifa).
5
Note the role of the subtribe (fakhdh)
The passage explains that mentioning the fakhdh (specific subtribe) stands in place of the grandfather because it refers to the highest ancestor. This is based on the principle that identification is achieved by a specific attribution, not a general one.
The text provides a detailed hierarchy of Arab tribal levels: sha'b, qabila, 'imara, batn, fakhdh, fasila.

يكفي وبه يفتى لحصول التعريف بذكر ثلاثة : العبد والمولى وأبوه. وإن ذكر اسم العبد والمولى أن نسب إلى قبيلة الخاص لا يكفي على ما ذكره السرخسي، ويكفي على ما ذكره شيخ الإسلام لوجوه ثلاثة، وإن لم يذكر Book of the Judge's Letter to a Judge. And if they both (the witnesses) say regarding her (the woman) 'the Tamimi', it is not permissible until they attribute her to her subtribe... And whoever admits that he testified falsely is publicly shamed but not punished... And she is sharing with him in name and lineage, because when there is a sharer in name and lineage, he is not specifically identified for the letter... The gist is that identification by pointing to the present (person), and for the absent, it is necessary to mention the name, and lineage, and attribution to the father is not sufficient according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Muhammad, and it is necessary to mention the grandfather, contrary to Abu Yusuf... And the correct view is that attribution to the grandfather is necessary... And if he uses a kunya without naming, it is not accepted unless he is famous like the Imam... And he said: It is required to look at her face for identification... And does it require testimony of more than two just witnesses that she is so-and-so daughter of so-and-so? Imam said: A group must testify that she is so-and-so daughter of so-and-so. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Testimony of two just witnesses suffices, and the fatwa is upon that because it is easier...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rules of identification (ta'rif) when writing a judge's letter or when testifying regarding an absent person. The author first discusses the case when the witnesses describe a woman only as 'Tamimi' (i.e. from the tribe of Tamim) – this is insufficient because Tamim is a large tribe; they must specify the subtribe (fakhdh) for proper identification. He then provides linguistic and tribal definitions of 'fakhdh' from various sources, noting the hierarchy: sha'b, qabila, 'imara, batn, fakhdh, fasila. The key point is that general attribution does not achieve identification. The passage then moves to intra-Hanafi disputes: Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require mentioning the grandfather in the lineage, while Abu Yusuf suffices with the father. However, if the person is well-known by a laqab (nickname) or profession, it may suffice. There is also disagreement on whether the subtribe can substitute for the grandfather – the author notes that according to al-Hidayah, mentioning the subtribe stands in place of the grandfather since it refers to the highest ancestor. Later scholars like Shaykh al-Islam and Sadr al-Shari'a give fatwa based on ease, accepting identification with three elements (e.g., slave's name, master, master's father). The passage also discusses conditions for the judge writing the letter: he must personally view the woman and write her description; having the scribe do it would involve two men viewing her unnecessarily. Finally, there is a dispute on how many witnesses are needed to confirm her identity: Imam requires a group (jamā'a) while the Sahibayn accept two just witnesses, and the fatwa is on their view. The commentary concludes with notes from al-Khizana and Qadikhan that if identification is achieved by name, father, and grandfather, the laqab is not needed, but if not achieved without the laqab, it is necessary.

Key Terms
فخذ (fakhdh): The subtribe, a subdivision of a tribe (specifically the fifth level in Arab tribal hierarchy: sha'b, qabila, 'imara, batn, fakhdh, fasila). It is the group closest to the individual.
تعريف (ta'rif): The process of identifying a person in legal contexts, especially for testimony or letters, by specifying name, lineage, and other distinguishing features.
الجد الأدنى (al-jadd al-adna): The immediate grandfather (father's father), as opposed to al-jadd al-a'la (the highest ancestor, like the eponym of a tribe). The text says mentioning the fakhdh (which is like the highest ancestor) stands in place of the immediate grandfather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the minimum identification required in a judge's letter for an absent person who is not universally famous?
A) Name and father only
B) Name, father, and grandfather (or specific subtribe)
C) Name and tribe only
D) Name, father, and profession

Key Takeaway
Identifying a person by a general tribe name is insufficient; a specific subtribe or the grandfather is required to avoid confusion, unless the person is universally famous.

Shahadat — Testimony

Conditions for Identifying the Original Witness in Shahada ala Shahada: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Grandfather vs. Clan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness identification conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three required elements for witness identification in shahada ala shahada and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the grandfather's name is indispensable or can be substituted by the clan.

Core Idea
The correct view requires grandfather's name for witness identification, but Abu Yusuf accepts the clan as a substitute.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the procedural requirements for identifying the original witness in testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada). The central dispute among the Hanafi masters is whether mentioning the grandfather is necessary or whether the clan (fakhdh) suffices. We will walk through the conditions, the disagreement, and the practical implications for a judge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three standard elements for witness identification
According to al-Hakim's al-Mukhtar, three things are needed: name, lineage to father, and lineage to grandfather or clan or profession.
The clan or profession can substitute for grandfather according to some views.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require grandfather explicitly; Abu Yusuf considers the clan (fakhdh) sufficient on the apparent narration.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Understand the exception for famous persons
If the witness is universally famous (like Imam Abu Hanifa), bare name suffices and no father or grandfather is needed.
Fame removes all ambiguity.
4
Apply the principle to a concrete scenario
A witness is identified as 'Zayd from the tribe of Tamim'. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, this is insufficient because the grandfather is missing; according to Abu Yusuf, it suffices because Tamim is a fakhdh.
Practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) depends on which view the judge follows.
5
Determine the operative fatwa
The correct view (الصحيح) in the text is that grandfather is indispensable, but for the number of witnesses (two suffice) the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf and Muhammad due to ease.
The judge should follow the correct view for the conditions of identification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الشهادات باب الشهادة على الشهادة ۲۱۱ قبيلته الخاص لا يكفي، وإن ذكر اسم العبد ومولاه ونسب العبد إلى مولاه ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه يكفي وبه أفتى الصدر لأنه وجد ثلاثة أشياء، وشرط الحاكم في المختصر للتعريف ثلاثة أشياء: الاسم والنسبة إلى الأب والنسبة إلى الجد أو الفخذ أو الصناعة. والصحيح أن النسبة إلى الجد لا بد منه وإن كان معروفاً بالاسم المجرد مشهوراً كشهرة الإمام أبي حنيفة يكفي، ولا حاجة إلى ذكر الأب والجد وفي الدار كدار الخلافة وإن مشهورة لا بد من ذكر الحدود عنده، وعندهما هي كالرجل. ولو كنى بلا تسمية لم تقبل إلا إذا كان مشهوراً كالإمام. ولو كتب من ابن فلان إلى فلان لم يجز إلا أن اشتهر كابن أبي ليلى ولو كتب إلى أبي فلان لم يجز لأن الجزء ينسب إلى الكل لا العكس؛ كذا في البزازية. ثم قال: ويشترط نظر وجهها في التعريف وإن أراد ذكر حليتها يترك موضع الحلية حتى يكون القاضي هو الذي يكتب الجلية أو يملي الكاتب لأنه إن حلاها الكاتب لا يجد القاضي بداً من أن ينظر إليها فيكون فيه نظر رجلين وفيما ذكرنا نظر رجل واحد فكان أولى. وهل يشترط شهادة الزائد على عدلين في أنها فلانة بنت فلان أم لا؟ قال الإمام: لا بد من شهادة جماعة على أنا فلانة بنت فلان. وقالا: شهادة عدلين تكفي وعليه الفتوى لأنه أيسر ا هـ. وهو ظاهر إلا قوله إن النسبة إلى الفخذ لا تكفي عن الجد ففي الهداية ثم التعريف وإن كان يتم بذكر الجد عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف على ظاهر الرواية، فذكر الفخذ يقوم مقام الجد لأنه اسم الجد الأعلى فنزل منزلة الجد الأدنى ا هـ. وكذا تمثيله في البزازية للفخذ بتميمي غير صحيح علمته آنفاً. وفي خزانة المفتين: ولو ذكر لقبه واسمه واسم أبيه قيل يكفي، والصحيح أنه لا يكفي؛ فإذا قضى قاض بدون ذكر الجد ينفذ وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: وإن حصل التعريف باسمه واسم أبيه ولقبه لا يحتاج إلى ذكر الجد وإن كان لا يحصل إلا بذكر الجد لا يكفي. والمدينة والقرية والكورة ليست بسبب للتعريف ولا تقع المعرفة بالإضافة إليها وإن دامت، فإذا كان الرجل يعرف باسمه واسم أبيه وجده لا يحتاج إلى اللقب، وإن كان لا يحصل إلا بذكر اللقب بأن كان يشاركه في المصر غيره في ذلك الاسم واللقب كما في أحمد بن سم قوله: (والصحيح أن النسبة الخ سيأتي رده قوله: وهل يشترط شهادة الزائد على العدلين في أنها فلانة الخ) قال الرملي قال الطرابلسي في معين الحكام ولو عرفها رجلان وقالا نشهد أنها فلانة بنت فلان حل للشاهد أن يشهد وفاقاً لأن في لفظ الشهادة من التأكيد ما ليس في لفظ الخبر لأنه يمين بالله تعالى معنى ولو كان بلفظ الخبر. وإنما يجوز عند أبي حنيفة لو أخبر جماعة لا يمكن تواطؤهم على الكذب، وعندهما لو أخبره عدلان أنها فلانة بنت فلان بن فلان يحل له الشهادة اهـ. ما هنا فانظر ما بينه وبين أو رأى. المخالفة. وقدم في شرح قوله «وله أن يشهد بما سمع من الفتاوى الصغرى ما يوافق ما ذكره هنا فتأمل والذي يظهر أن ما في معين الحكام هو المعتبر لما ذكره عن محمد بن عمر فهذا لا يقع التعريف به لأن في ذلك المصر يشاركه غيره، فالحاصل أن المعتبر إنما هو حاصل المعرفة وارتفاع الاشتراك ا هـ. وفي إيضاح الإصلاح: وفي العجم ذكر الصناعة بمنزلة الفخذ لأنهم ضيعوا أنسابهم.
Book of Testimonies, Chapter of Testimony upon Testimony. ... His specific tribe is not sufficient... And if he mentions the slave's name and his master and traces the slave to his master, Sheikh al-Islam said it suffices and the Sadr gave fatwa accordingly because three things are found. Al-Hakim in al-Mukhtar stipulated three things for identification: name, lineage to father, and lineage to grandfather or clan or profession. The correct view is that lineage to grandfather is indispensable, but if he is known by his bare name and famous like the fame of Imam Abu Hanifa, it suffices, and there is no need to mention father and grandfather...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for identifying the original witness in testimony upon testimony (shahada ala shahada). The commentator explains that mere mention of tribe is insufficient; three elements are generally required: name, father's name, and grandfather's name or clan/profession. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require grandfather, while Abu Yusuf allows clan to substitute for grandfather.  The text also covers writing from 'son of so-and-so' to 'so-and-so' and other specific cases. The final position is that the criterion is actual knowledge and removal of ambiguity.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rīf): The process of identifying the original witness in shahada ala shahada so that the judge knows who they are.
الفخذ (al-fakhdh): A sub-tribe or clan, considered as a higher ancestor for identification purposes.
النسبة (al-nisbah): Lineage or attribution, e.g., to father, grandfather, tribe, or profession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view (الصحيح) in this passage, what is the minimum requirement for identifying a witness in shahada ala shahada?
A) Name and father's name only
B) Name, father's name, and grandfather's name
C) Name, tribe, and profession
D) Name and nickname only

Key Takeaway
In shahada ala shahada, the standard identification requires name, father, and grandfather; the grandfather is indispensable in the correct view, though some Hanafi masters accept the clan as a substitute.
